Method of Learning

Classification of Essential and Accidental Attributes in a Science
Defining subject matter and classifying essential vs accidental attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify attributes (ʿawāriḍ) into essential and accidental categories and identify the types of mediation that govern each category.

Core Idea
A science discusses only the essential attributes of its subject; accidental attributes are excluded.

In this passage, the commentator resolves a potential objection about discussing the subject itself, then defines the 'subject' of a science and systematically classifies attributes into six types—three essential and three accidental. Understanding this classification is fundamental to defining any Islamic science, including usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The passage begins with a question: how can the author say the subject of this science is proofs and rulings, if the rule is that a science discusses attributes of its subject, not the subject itself? Recognize the apparent contradiction.
2
Understand the Resolution
The commentator resolves it by assuming a deleted genitive construct: 'discussion about the states of proofs and rulings'. Note that this is a standard technique in Arabic grammar to align the expression with the principle.
3
Define 'Subject' and 'Attribute'
Learn that the subject of a science is the thing whose essential attributes are discussed. An attribute (ʿāriḍ) is something external to the essence of a thing, predicated on it.
4
Classify the Six Types of Attributes
Work through the enumeration: attributes attach either without mediation or with mediation. If with mediation, the mediation is either a part (internal) or external. For external, four possibilities: equal, more general, more specific, opposite. The first three (without mediation, via part, via equal) are essential; the last three are accidental.
Pay attention to the critique of the example for type one—it actually falls under type two.
5
Apply the Classification to the Science of Usul
Understand that usul al-fiqh discusses only the essential attributes of its subject (proofs and rulings). This defines the scope and prevents discussion of irrelevant matters.

Source Text

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتنويج
سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے کہا اور ماقبل کی تفصیل سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اس علم میں ادلہ اور احکام سے بحث ہوگی اور اسکا موضوع اولہ اور احکام ہیں حالانکہ ضابطہ ہے کہ کسی علم کے نفس موضوع سے بحث نہیں ہوتی اور اس سے لازم آتا ہے کہ نفس موضوع سے بحث ہو حالانکہ بحث عوارض سے ہوتی ہے۔
جواب: ۔ دیا یہاں مضاف محذوف ہے اور یہ حذف مضاف کلام عرب میں کثیر ہے اب عبارت ہوگی بحث عن احوال الا دلتہ والا حکام فلا اعتراض۔
قوله فموضوع هذا العلم - یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے شاریخ نے اس عبارت میں مطلق موضوع کی تعریف اور عوارض ذاتیہ کی بحث بیان کی ہے۔ تو مطلق موضوع کہتے ہیں جس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی جائے وہ شی اس علم کا موضوع کہلاتی ہے۔ عوارض ذاتیہ : ۔ عوارض جمع ہے عارض کی اور عارض وہ ہے جوشی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشی پر محمول ہو مثلا یہ ٹوپی سر پر عارض ہے حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر محمول ہے یہ حسی مثال ہے عوارض کی چھے قسمیں ہیں۔ تمام عوارض کی وجہ حصر:۔ عارض معروض کولاحق ہو گا بلا واسطہ یا بالواسطہ اگر بالواسطہ لاحق ہوتو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے وہ واسطہ معروض کا جز ہوگا یا امر خارج ہوگا پھر اگر امر خارج ہو تو چار حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو وہ امر خارج معروض کے مساوی ہوگا یا اخص ہوگا یا معروض سے اہم ہوگا یا معروض کے مباین ہوگا ۔ ان میں سے پہلی تین اقسام عوارض ذاتیہ کی ہیں اور باقی اقسام عوراض غریبہ کی ہیں۔ اس وجہ حصر سے ہر ایک کی تعریف بھی معلوم ہوگئی۔ تعریفات عوارض ذاتیہ: پہلی قسم : عرض ذاتی شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی سے خارج ہو کر شئی پر محمول ہو محض اس کی ذات کی وجہ سے بغیر کسی واسطہ کے جیسے اور اک برائے انسان کہا جاتا ہے الانسان مدرك اب آئیں اور اک عارض ہے اور انسان معروض ہے اور ادراک کا عارض ہونا بلا واسطہ ہے۔
فائدہ :۔ پہلی قسم کی جو شاریخ نے مثال دی ہے درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ انسان یا تو حیوان ناطق کا نام ہے یا نفس ناطق کا نام ہے اگر اول ہے جیسا کہ مشہور ہے تو پھر اور اک انسان کو بالذات ( حیوان ناطق کے مجموعہ کے واسطہ سے ) لاحق نہیں ہوسکتا بلکہ ناطق کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہے تو ادراک بواسطہ جز کے انسان کو لاحق ہوا۔ اور اگر انسان صرف ناطق کا نام ہے تو پھر آگے یہ تمثیل که حرکت انسان کو حیوان کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہے یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ انسان فقط ناطق کا نام ہے تو حیوان انسان کا جز ہی نہیں ہے تو پھر بواسطہ جز کے عارض ہونے والی صورت میں یہ تمثیل درست نہیں ہوگی اس لیے بہتر یہ ہے کہ پہلی قسم کی تمثیل میں یوں کہا جائے کہ جیسے علم و قدرت باری تعالیٰ کو لاحق ہیں بلا واسطہ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
دوسری قسم : عرض ذاتی شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشی پر محمول ہو ایسے امر کے واسطے سے جو معروض کی حقیقت میں داخل ہو کر معروض سے اہم ہو یعنی معروض کا جز ہو اور اس سے عام ہو جیسے حرکت عارض ہو انسان کو اور یوں کہا جائے الانسان متحرک آسمیں انسان معروض اور حرکت عارض ہے بواسطہ حیوان کے۔ اور حیوان انسان سے ائم ہے اور اس کی حقیقت میں داخل ہے یعنی اسکا جز ہے۔ کیونکہ انسان کی حقیقت حیوان ناطق ہے۔
تیسری قسم : عرض ذاتی شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو کئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشنی پرمحمول ہوا ایسے امر کے واسطہ سے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض کے مساوی ہو جیسے محک عارض ہو انسان کو اور کہا جائے الانسان ضاحک اس میں انسان معروض ہے اور محک اس کو عارض ہے تعجب کے واسطہ سے اور یہ تعجب انسان کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر انسان کے مساوی ہے کہا جاتا ہے الانسان متعجب و کل متعجب انسان ۔
عوارض غریبہ کی پہلی قسم : عرض غریب مٹی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر شے پر محمول ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض سے اہم ہو جیسے حرکت عارض ہوا بیض کو بواسطہ جسم کے اور کہا جائے الابیض متحرک۔
دوسری قسم : عرض غریب مٹی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر ٹی پر عارض ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض سے اخص ہو جیسے محک حیوان کو لاحق ہو بواسطہ انسان کے۔
تیسری قسم:۔ عرض غریب شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشٹی کو لاحق ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض کے مباین ہو جیسے حرارت پانی کو عارض ہو بواسطہ آگ کے۔
فائدہ:۔ یہ وجہ حصر بیان کی ہے متاخرین کے مذہب کے مطابق ہے کہ تیسری قسم میں متاخرین نے کہا کہ واسطہ معروض کا جز ہو اور اعم بھی ہو اور شاریخ نے یہی بیان کیا ہے یہ مثال بھی متاخرین کے مذہب کے مطابق دی ہے۔ متقدین کے نزدیک واسطہ کا اہم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ والمراد بالبحث ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اسمیں شارع نے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی کیفیت کو بیان کیا
Question: This is that the author said, and from the previous detail it is also known that in this science there will be discussion about proofs and rulings, and its subject is proofs and rulings, although the principle is that in any science the subject itself is not discussed, and this necessitates that the subject itself be discussed, whereas discussion is about attributes. Answer: There is a deleted genitive construct here, and this deletion of the genitive is frequent in Arabic speech; now the expression becomes: discussion about the states of proofs and rulings, so no objection. His statement: 'So the subject of this science' - This is the first part of the commentary's expression; the commentator in this expression has explained the definition of the absolute subject and the discussion of essential attributes. So the absolute subject is called that thing whose essential attributes are discussed; that thing is called the subject of that science. Essential attributes: Attributes is the plural of attribute, and an attribute is that which is external to the reality of a thing and is predicated on the thing; for example, this cap is an attribute on the head, being external to the reality and predicated - this is a sensory example. Attributes have six types. The reason for enumeration: An attribute will attach to the thing either without mediation or with mediation. If it attaches with mediation, then it is either that the mediation is a part of the thing or an external matter. Then if it is an external matter, there are four possibilities: either that external matter is equal to the thing, or more specific than it, or more general than it, or opposite to it. Among these, the first three types are essential attributes, and the remaining types are accidental attributes. From this enumeration the definition of each is also known. Definitions of essential attributes: First type: An essential attribute is that effect and state of a thing which is external to the thing's reality and predicated on the thing solely due to its essence without any mediation; like 'intellect' is said for a human: 'al-insānu mudrik' - so 'intellect' is an attribute and 'human' is the thing, and the attribution of intellect is without mediation. Benefit: The example given by the commentator for the first type is not correct, because a human is either the name of 'rational animal' or the name of 'rational soul'. If the first is the case, as is well-known, then intellect cannot attach to a human by essence (through the aggregate of rational animal) but rather attaches through the 'rational'; so intellect attaches to a human through mediation of a part. And if human is only the name of 'rational', then the later example that movement attaches to human through the mediation of 'animal' is not correct, because human is only the name of 'rational', so 'animal' is not a part of human; then in the case of attaching through mediation of a part, this example would not be correct. Therefore it is better to say in the example of the first type like knowledge and power attach to Allah Most High without mediation. And Allah knows best. Second type: An essential attribute is that effect and state of a thing which is external to the thing's reality and predicated on the thing through a matter that is included in the thing's reality and is more general than the thing, i.e., it is a part of the thing and is general in relation to it; like movement attaches to a human - and it is said 'al-insānu mutaḥarrik' - here human is the thing and movement is an attribute through the mediation of 'animal'. And 'animal' is more general than human and is included in his reality, i.e., it is a part of him, because the reality of human is rational animal. Third type: An essential attribute is that effect and state of a thing which is external to the thing's reality and predicated on the thing through a matter that is external to the thing's reality and equal to the thing; like laughter attaches to a human - and it is said 'al-insānu ḍāḥik' - here human is the thing and laughter is an attribute upon him through the mediation of wonder, and this wonder is external to the reality of human and equal to human; it is said 'al-insānu mutaʿajjib' and every 'mutaʿajjib' is human. First type of accidental attributes: An accidental attribute is that effect and state of a thing which is external to the thing's reality and predicated on the thing through the mediation of a matter that is external to the thing's reality and more general than the thing; like movement attaches to a white thing through the mediation of body, and it is said 'al-abyaḍu mutaḥarrik'. Second type: An accidental attribute is that effect and state of a thing which is external to the thing's reality and attached to the thing through the mediation of a matter that is external to the thing's reality and more specific than the thing; like laughter attaches to an animal through the mediation of a human. Third type: An accidental attribute is that effect and state of a thing which is external to the thing's reality and attached to the thing through the mediation of a matter that is external to the thing's reality and opposite to the thing; like heat attaches to water through the mediation of fire. Benefit: This enumeration that has been explained is according to the school of the later scholars (mutaʾakhkhirīn), that in the third type the later scholars said that the mediation is a part of the thing and also more general; and the commentator has explained this, and this example is also given according to the school of the later scholars. According to the earlier scholars (mutaqaddimīn), the mediation being more general is not necessary. And the intended meaning of 'discussion' - This is the second part of the commentary's expression; in it the commentator has explained the quality of discussion about essential attributes.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing a potential objection regarding the subject matter of this science. The author's statement that the subject is proofs and rulings might imply discussing the subject itself, whereas the rule is that a science discusses the attributes of its subject, not the subject per se. The commentator resolves this by supposing a deleted word, so the actual meaning is 'discussion about the states of proofs and rulings'. This is a standard usul principle: every science discusses the essential attributes (ʿawāriḍ dhātiyya) of its subject. The commentator then defines the absolute subject: it is the thing whose essential attributes are studied. He proceeds to classify attributes (ʿawāriḍ) into six types, enumerated based on how they attach to the subject (maʿrūḍ): either without mediation (first type), or through a mediation that is either a part of the subject (second type) or something external. For external mediation, it can be equal, more specific, more general, or opposite to the subject. The first three of these (without mediation, through a part, through an equal) are considered essential attributes (ʿawāriḍ dhātiyya) because they arise from the subject's essence or its necessary concomitants. The remaining three (through something more general, more specific, or opposite) are accidental attributes (ʿawāriḍ gharība) because the mediating factor is not inherent to the subject. The passage gives examples, but provides a critical footnote: the example of 'al-insānu mudrik' (human is perceptive) for the first type is flawed because perception attaches via the rational faculty (a part of human), making it mediated. A better example is divine attributes like knowledge and power, which attach to Allah without mediation. This critique reflects the precision required in usul definitions. The passage also notes a difference between earlier and later Hanafi scholars: the later scholars (mutaʾakhkhirūn) require the mediation in the second essential type to be more general (aʿamm), while the earlier scholars did not insist on that condition. Overall, this is a foundational discussion that clarifies how a science's subject is defined and what types of questions it addresses.

Key Terms
عارض (ʿāriḍ): An attribute that is external to the essence of a thing and predicated on it.
عارض ذاتي (ʿāriḍ dhātī): An attribute that attaches to the subject without mediation or through a part or an equal, and is essential to the subject.
عارض غريب (ʿāriḍ gharīb): An attribute that attaches through a mediation that is more general, more specific, or opposite, and is accidental.
موضوع (mawḍūʿ): The thing whose essential attributes are studied in a given science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the classification in this passage, which of the following is an example of the third type of essential attribute (ʿāriḍ dhātī)?
A) Movement attaching to a human through animal.
B) Laughter attaching to a human through wonder.
C) Heat attaching to water through fire.
D) Intellect attaching to a human directly.

Key Takeaway
A science discusses only the essential attributes of its subject; classifying attributes as essential or accidental depends on the mode of mediation.

Method of Learning
intermediate
12 min
Classification of Essential and Extraneous Accidents
Defines essential and extraneous accidents with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between essential and extraneous accidents and identify their subtypes according to the Hanafi logical classification.

Core Idea
Essential accidents are external but related via a medium; extraneous accidents involve a medium wholly external to the substratum.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih explains the logical categories of accidents ('arad) used in usul al-fiqh. Understanding these categories is crucial for grasping how usul scholars construct propositions about the subject matter of the science, as they form the predicates in usul discussions.

Guided Path
1
Define essential accident
Read the definition of 'arad dhati: it is a state external to the substratum but predicated via a medium that is part of the substratum (or equal/external).
The medium condition distinguishes essential from extraneous.
2
Identify three types of essential accidents
From the text, the medium can be: (1) part of the substratum and more general, (2) external and equal to the substratum, (3) external and more general (though later scholars consider this extraneous).
Examples: man moving via animal; man laughing via wonder; man's motion via body (later classified as extraneous).
3
Define extraneous accident
Read the definition of 'arad gharib: a state external to the substratum predicated via a medium wholly external to the substratum.
4
Identify three types of extraneous accidents
The medium can be: (1) more general than the substratum, (2) more specific, (3) contrary to the substratum.
Examples: white object moving via body; animal laughing via man; water heated via fire.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Early Hanafi scholars (mutaqaddimin) did not require the medium to be more general in the third type of essential accident; later scholars (muta'akkhirin) do. This affects the classification of certain cases.

کا جز ہی نہیں ہے تو پھر بواسطہ جز کے عارض ہونے والی صورت میں یہ تمثیل درست نہیں ہوگی اس لیے بہتر یہ ہے کہ پہلی قسم کی تمثیل میں یوں کہا جائے کہ جیسے علم و قدرت باری تعالیٰ کو لاحق ہیں بلا واسطہ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔

دوسری قسم : عرض ذاتی شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشی پر محمول ہو ایسے امر کے واسطے سے جو معروض کی حقیقت میں داخل ہو کر معروض سے اہم ہو یعنی معروض کا جز ہو اور اس سے عام ہو جیسے حرکت عارض ہو انسان کو اور یوں کہا جائے الانسان متحرک آسمیں انسان معروض اور حرکت عارض ہے بواسطہ حیوان کے۔ اور حیوان انسان سے ائم ہے اور اس کی حقیقت میں داخل ہے یعنی اسکا جز ہے۔ کیونکہ انسان کی حقیقت حیوان ناطق ہے۔

تیسری قسم : عرض ذاتی شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو کئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشنی پرمحمول ہوا ایسے امر کے واسطہ سے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض کے مساوی ہو جیسے محک عارض ہو انسان کو اور کہا جائے الانسان ضاحک اس میں انسان معروض ہے اور محک اس کو عارض ہے تعجب کے واسطہ سے اور یہ تعجب انسان کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر انسان کے مساوی ہے کہا جاتا ہے الانسان متعجب و کل متعجب انسان ۔

عوارض غریبہ کی پہلی قسم : عرض غریب مٹی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر شے پر محمول ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض سے اہم ہو جیسے حرکت عارض ہوا بیض کو بواسطہ جسم کے اور کہا جائے الابیض متحرک۔

دوسری قسم : عرض غریب مٹی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر ٹی پر عارض ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض سے اخص ہو جیسے محک حیوان کو لاحق ہو بواسطہ انسان کے۔

تیسری قسم:۔ عرض غریب شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشٹی کو لاحق ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض کے مباین ہو جیسے حرارت پانی کو عارض ہو بواسطہ آگ کے۔

فائدہ:۔ یہ وجہ حصر بیان کی ہے متاخرین کے مذہب کے مطابق ہے کہ تیسری قسم میں متاخرین نے کہا کہ واسطہ معروض کا جز ہو اور اعم بھی ہو اور شاریخ نے یہی بیان کیا ہے یہ مثال بھی متاخرین کے مذہب کے مطابق دی ہے۔ متقدین کے نزدیک واسطہ کا اہم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔

والمراد بالبحث ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اسمیں شارع نے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی کیفیت کو بیان کیا ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کو قضیہ کا موضوع بنادو اور عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے کسی عرض ذاتی کو معمول بنادو یہ کیفیت بحث ہے مثلاً اصول فقہ کا موضوع کتاب اللہ ہے اس کو قضیہ کا موضوع بنا دو اور عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے کسی عرض ذاتی مثلا قطعی ہونا یا خنی ہونے کو عام خاص وغیرہ کو معمول بنا دو اب عبارت ہوگی الكتاب يفيد القطع ۔ اب الكتاب موضوع ہے يفيد القطع محمول ہے اور قطعی ہونا عارض ہے

دوسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بنا ئیں اور عوارض میں سے کسی کو معمول بنائیں جیسے الامر يفيد القطع اب الامر یہ کتاب اللہ کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یفید القطع یہ عوارض میں سے ایک عرض ہے جو قضیہ کا محمول واقع ہے۔

تیسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ عوارض ذاتیہ کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کو معمول بناؤ مثلاً العام يفيد القطع اب عام خاص ہونا وغیرہ یہ عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے ہیں تو العام یہ موضوع ہے اور قطعی ہونا محمول ہے

چوتھا طریقہ - عوارض ذاتیہ کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کوحمول بناؤ مثلا العام الذي خص عند البعض يفيد الملطن اب عام خص عنہ اعبض یہ عوارض کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یغید الفطن یہ معمول ہے اور عوارض میں سے ایک عارض ہے۔

وجميع مباحث الاصول ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے خلاصہ بیان کیا ہے ماقبل والی بحث کا کہ اصول فقہ میں جتنی مباحث ذکر کی جاتی ہیں وہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کرنے کے لیے ذکر کی جاتی ہیں کیونکہ موضوع دو ہیں ادلہ کے عوارض ان کا مثبت ہوتا ہے اور احکام کے عوارض ان کا ثابت ہوتا ہے یہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں خلاصہ یہ نکلا کہ اصول فقہ میں بحث اثبات وثبوت سے ہوگی اور ان چیزوں سے ہوگی جن کو اثبات و ثبوت میں دخل ہے۔

فان قلت - یہ عبات کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض ایک سوال ذکر کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع اولہ اور احکام ہیں۔ ادلہ میں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول الله اجماع اور قیاس سب داخل ہیں ۔ پھر کیا وجہ ہے کہ اصولی اجماع اور قیاس سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ سے بحث نہیں کرتے یعنی اجماع وقیاس کے حجت ہونے سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ اللہ کے حجت ہونے سے بحث نہیں کرتے۔

جواب (۱):۔ یہ اعترض ہی وارد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بحث ہوتی ہے کہ خاص عام مشترک مجمل متشابه و غیرہ سب کتاب اللہ میں داخل ہیں۔ لیکن یہ جواب کمز رو ہے کیونکہ ایک ہوتا ہے کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ کی کیفیت حجت سے بحث کرنا اور دوسرانفس حجت
It is not part at all; then in the case where the accident occurs through an intermediate part, this example would not be correct. Therefore it is better that in the first type of example one say: like knowledge and power of Allah Most High are attached without mediation. And Allah knows best what is correct.

Second type: Essential accident (arad dhati) is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and is predicated on the thing through something that enters into the essence of the substratum and is more general than the substratum, i.e., it is a part of the substratum and more general than it. Like motion attaches to man, and one says: al-insaan mutaharrik. Here man is the substratum and motion is the accident through the mediation of animal. And animal is more general than man and enters into his essence, i.e., is a part of him, because the essence of man is rational animal.

Third type: Essential accident is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and is predicated on it through something that is external to the essence of the substratum and equal to it. Like laughter attaches to man, and one says: al-insaan dhaahik. Here man is the substratum and laughter is its accident through the medium of wonder. And this wonder is external to the essence of man and equal to man. It is said: al-insaan muta'ajjib, and every muta'ajjib is man.

First type of extraneous accident (arad gharib): It is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and is predicated on the thing through something that is external to the essence of the substratum and more general than it. Like motion attaches to a white object through the medium of body, and one says: al-abyad mutaharrik.

Second type: Extraneous accident is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and attaches to the thing through something external to the essence of the substratum and more specific than it. Like laughter attaches to animal through the medium of man.

Third type: Extraneous accident is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and attaches to the thing through something external to the essence of the substratum and contrary to it. Like heat attaches to water through the medium of fire.

Benefit: This reason for the enumeration is according to the school of the later scholars (muta'akkhirin), that in the third type they said the medium must be a part of the substratum and more general, and the commentator (sharih) has stated this. This example is also given according to the school of the later scholars. According to the earlier scholars (mutaqaddimin), the medium being more general is not necessary.

And the meaning of 'bahth' (discussion): This is the second part of the commentary's text, in which the commentator explained the quality of discussion concerning essential accidents. It is this: make the subject matter of a science the subject of a proposition, and make one of the essential accidents the predicate. This is the quality of discussion. For example, the subject of usul al-fiqh is the Book of Allah; make it the subject of a proposition, and make one of the essential accidents—like being definitive (qat'i) or being speculative (zanni), or general, specific, etc.—the predicate. Then the expression will be: 'al-kitab yufid al-qat'. Now 'al-kitab' is the subject, 'yufid al-qat' is the predicate, and being definitive is an accident.

Second method: make a division of the subject matter the subject, and make one of the accidents the predicate. Like: 'al-amr yufid al-qat'. Now 'al-amr' is a division of the Book of Allah and occurs as the subject of the proposition, and 'yufid al-qat' is one of the accidents occurring as the predicate of the proposition.

Third method: make essential accidents the subject and essential accidents the predicate. For example: 'al-amm yufid al-qat'. Now 'al-amm' etc. are among essential accidents; so 'al-amm' is the subject and being definitive is the predicate.

Fourth method: make a division of essential accidents the subject and essential accidents the predicate. For example: 'al-amm alladhi khuss 'inda al-ba'd yufid al-mutlaq'. Now 'al-amm alladhi khuss 'inda al-ba'd' is a division of accidents and occurs as the subject of the proposition, and 'yufid al-mutlaq' is the predicate and is one of the accidents.

And all discussions of usul: This is the third part of the commentary's text. From here the commentator summarized the preceding discussion: that all discussions mentioned in usul al-fiqh are mentioned to establish its essential accidents. Because the subject matters are two: the accidents of the proofs (adillah) are what establish (muthbit) them, and the accidents of the rulings (ahkam) are what are established (thabit) by them. These are essential accidents. The summary is that discussion in usul al-fiqh will be about affirmation (ithbat) and establishment (thubut), and about those things that have a role in affirmation and establishment.

Now if you say: This is the last part of the text; the purpose is to mention a question and answer it. Objection: The subject matter of usul al-fiqh is proofs and rulings. The proofs include the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). So why is it that the usuli discusses consensus and analogy, but does not discuss the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah? That is, they discuss the authority (hujjiyya) of consensus and analogy, but do not discuss the authority of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.

Answer (1): This objection does not even arise, because discussion does take place regarding the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah — regarding specific, general, common, ambiguous, equivocal, etc., all of which are included in the Book of Allah. But this answer is weak, because there is a difference between discussing the quality of being hujja of the Book and Sunnah, and discussing the very hujja [itself].
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage from the sharh (commentary) of al-Tawdih explains two main topics: (1) the classification of accidents ('arad) in logic, specifically essential (dhati) and extraneous (gharib) accidents, and (2) how these concepts apply to the method of discussion in usul al-fiqh. The commentator first corrects an example for the first type of essential accident, emphasizing that attributes of Allah like knowledge and power are attached without any medium. Then he lays out three types of essential accidents: (a) where the medium is a part of the substratum that is more general (e.g., motion for man via animal), (b) where the medium is external and equal (e.g., laughter for man via wonder), and (c) where the medium is external and more general (but this is actually part of extraneous accidents as per the later scholars). The text then provides three types of extraneous accidents: (a) medium more general than substratum (e.g., motion for white via body), (b) medium more specific (e.g., laughter for animal via man), and (c) medium contrary (e.g., heat for water via fire). A benefit clarifies that the classification with the medium being more general in the third type is according to the later scholars (muta'akkhirin), while earlier scholars (mutaqaddimin) did not require the medium to be more general. The second part of the passage explains the method of constructing propositions in usul al-fiqh: the subject matter of the science (e.g., the Book of Allah) or its divisions can be the subject, and one of its essential accidents (like being definitive, general, etc.) can be the predicate. Four methods are illustrated. The commentator then summarizes that all usul discussions aim to establish the essential accidents of the proofs and rulings. Finally, an objection is raised: why do usulis discuss the authority of ijma and qiyas but not that of Quran and Sunnah? The given answer (that discussions of specific/general etc. constitute discussion) is deemed weak, because there is a difference between discussing the modality of hujjiyya and the essence of hujjiyya. The text ends abruptly, leaving the stronger answer incomplete.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی ('arad dhati): An accident that is external to the essence of the substratum but is predicated on it through something that is either part of the substratum (and more general) or external and equal/specific/contrary.
عرض غریب ('arad gharib): An accident that is external to the essence of the substratum and predicated through a medium that is external to the substratum and either more general, more specific, or contrary.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science, e.g., proofs and rulings in usul al-fiqh; also the subject of a proposition.
محمول (mahmul): The predicate in a proposition; in usul al-fiqh discussions, it is an accident (like being definitive) that is affirmed of the subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of essential accidents ('arad dhati) are mentioned?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Essential accidents are external but predicated via a medium; extraneous accidents use a wholly external medium; the later Hanafi position requires the medium in essential accidents to be a part and more general.

Method of Learning
intermediate
15 min
Method of Discussion in Usul al-Fiqh
Explains the method of constructing propositions in usul al-fiqh and the purpose of usul discussions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the four methods of constructing propositions in usul al-fiqh and explain the purpose of all usul discussions.

Core Idea
All usul discussions aim to establish essential accidents of proofs and rulings.

This part of the commentary explains how usul scholars structure their discussions: by forming propositions where the subject is the subject matter of usul or its divisions, and the predicate is one of its essential accidents. The passage also addresses an objection about why usulis discuss the authority of ijma and qiyas but not of Quran and Sunnah, critiquing a weak answer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four methods of forming propositions
List the four ways: (1) subject matter as subject, essential accident as predicate; (2) division of subject matter as subject, accident as predicate; (3) essential accident as subject, another essential accident as predicate; (4) division of essential accident as subject, another essential accident as predicate.
Each method is a way to discuss properties of the subject matter.
2
Understand the purpose of all usul discussions
The commentator summarizes that all usul research is to establish the essential accidents of the proofs and rulings.
This is the foundation of usul methodology.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection: why do usulis discuss hujjiyya of ijma and qiyas but not of Quran and Sunnah? The text presents a weak answer.
4
Evaluate the given answer
The answer claims that discussion of specific/general etc. counts as discussion of the Book and Sunnah. The commentator deems this weak because it confuses discussing the modality of hujjiyya with the essence of hujjiyya.

کا جز ہی نہیں ہے تو پھر بواسطہ جز کے عارض ہونے والی صورت میں یہ تمثیل درست نہیں ہوگی اس لیے بہتر یہ ہے کہ پہلی قسم کی تمثیل میں یوں کہا جائے کہ جیسے علم و قدرت باری تعالیٰ کو لاحق ہیں بلا واسطہ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔

تیسری قسم : عرض ذاتی شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو کئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشنی پرمحمول ہوا ایسے امر کے واسطہ سے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض کے مساوی ہو جیسے محک عارض ہو انسان کو اور کہا جائے الانسان ضاحک اس میں انسان معروض ہے اور محک اس کو عارض ہے تعجب کے واسطہ سے اور یہ تعجب انسان کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر انسان کے مساوی ہے کہا جاتا ہے الانسان متعجب و کل متعجب انسان ۔

عوارض غریبہ کی پہلی قسم : عرض غریب مٹی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر شے پر محمول ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض سے اہم ہو جیسے حرکت عارض ہوا بیض کو بواسطہ جسم کے اور کہا جائے الابیض متحرک۔

دوسری قسم : عرض غریب مٹی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر ٹی پر عارض ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض سے اخص ہو جیسے محک حیوان کو لاحق ہو بواسطہ انسان کے۔

تیسری قسم:۔ عرض غریب شئی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو ئی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کرشٹی کو لاحق ہو بواسطہ ایسے امر کے جو معروض کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر معروض کے مباین ہو جیسے حرارت پانی کو عارض ہو بواسطہ آگ کے۔

دوسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بنا ئیں اور عوارض میں سے کسی کو معمول بنائیں جیسے الامر يفيد القطع اب الامر یہ کتاب اللہ کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یفید القطع یہ عوارض میں سے ایک عرض ہے جو قضیہ کا محمول واقع ہے۔

تیسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ عوارض ذاتیہ کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کو معمول بناؤ مثلاً العام يفيد القطع اب عام خاص ہونا وغیرہ یہ عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے ہیں تو العام یہ موضوع ہے اور قطعی ہونا محمول ہے

چوتھا طریقہ - عوارض ذاتیہ کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کوحمول بناؤ مثلا العام الذي خص عند البعض يفيد الملطن اب عام خص عنہ اعبض یہ عوارض کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یغید الفطن یہ معمول ہے اور عوارض میں سے ایک عارض ہے۔

وجميع مباحث الاصول ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے خلاصہ بیان کیا ہے ماقبل والی بحث کا کہ اصول فقہ میں جتنی مباحث ذکر کی جاتی ہیں وہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کرنے کے لیے ذکر کی جاتی ہیں کیونکہ موضوع دو ہیں ادلہ کے عوارض ان کا مثبت ہوتا ہے اور احکام کے عوارض ان کا ثابت ہوتا ہے یہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں خلاصہ یہ نکلا کہ اصول فقہ میں بحث اثبات وثبوت سے ہوگی اور ان چیزوں سے ہوگی جن کو اثبات و ثبوت میں دخل ہے۔

فان قلت - یہ عبات کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض ایک سوال ذکر کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع اولہ اور احکام ہیں۔ ادلہ میں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول الله اجماع اور قیاس سب داخل ہیں ۔ پھر کیا وجہ ہے کہ اصولی اجماع اور قیاس سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ سے بحث نہیں کرتے یعنی اجماع وقیاس کے حجت ہونے سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ اللہ کے حجت ہونے سے بحث نہیں کرتے۔

جواب (۱):۔ یہ اعترض ہی وارد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بحث ہوتی ہے کہ خاص عام مشترک مجمل متشابه و غیرہ سب کتاب اللہ میں داخل ہیں۔ لیکن یہ جواب کمز رو ہے کیونکہ ایک ہوتا ہے کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ کی کیفیت حجت سے بحث کرنا اور دوسرانفس حجت
It is not part at all; then in the case where the accident occurs through an intermediate part, this example would not be correct. Therefore it is better that in the first type of example one say: like knowledge and power of Allah Most High are attached without mediation. And Allah knows best what is correct.

Second type: Essential accident (arad dhati) is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and is predicated on the thing through something that enters into the essence of the substratum and is more general than the substratum, i.e., it is a part of the substratum and more general than it. Like motion attaches to man, and one says: al-insaan mutaharrik. Here man is the substratum and motion is the accident through the mediation of animal. And animal is more general than man and enters into his essence, i.e., is a part of him, because the essence of man is rational animal.

Third type: Essential accident is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and is predicated on it through something that is external to the essence of the substratum and equal to it. Like laughter attaches to man, and one says: al-insaan dhaahik. Here man is the substratum and laughter is its accident through the medium of wonder. And this wonder is external to the essence of man and equal to man. It is said: al-insaan muta'ajjib, and every muta'ajjib is man.

First type of extraneous accident (arad gharib): It is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and is predicated on the thing through something that is external to the essence of the substratum and more general than it. Like motion attaches to a white object through the medium of body, and one says: al-abyad mutaharrik.

Second type: Extraneous accident is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and attaches to the thing through something external to the essence of the substratum and more specific than it. Like laughter attaches to animal through the medium of man.

Third type: Extraneous accident is an effect and state of a thing that is external to the essence of the thing and attaches to the thing through something external to the essence of the substratum and contrary to it. Like heat attaches to water through the medium of fire.

Benefit: This reason for the enumeration is according to the school of the later scholars (muta'akkhirin), that in the third type they said the medium must be a part of the substratum and more general, and the commentator (sharih) has stated this. This example is also given according to the school of the later scholars. According to the earlier scholars (mutaqaddimin), the medium being more general is not necessary.

And the meaning of 'bahth' (discussion): This is the second part of the commentary's text, in which the commentator explained the quality of discussion concerning essential accidents. It is this: make the subject matter of a science the subject of a proposition, and make one of the essential accidents the predicate. This is the quality of discussion. For example, the subject of usul al-fiqh is the Book of Allah; make it the subject of a proposition, and make one of the essential accidents—like being definitive (qat'i) or being speculative (zanni), or general, specific, etc.—the predicate. Then the expression will be: 'al-kitab yufid al-qat'. Now 'al-kitab' is the subject, 'yufid al-qat' is the predicate, and being definitive is an accident.

Second method: make a division of the subject matter the subject, and make one of the accidents the predicate. Like: 'al-amr yufid al-qat'. Now 'al-amr' is a division of the Book of Allah and occurs as the subject of the proposition, and 'yufid al-qat' is one of the accidents occurring as the predicate of the proposition.

Third method: make essential accidents the subject and essential accidents the predicate. For example: 'al-amm yufid al-qat'. Now 'al-amm' etc. are among essential accidents; so 'al-amm' is the subject and being definitive is the predicate.

Fourth method: make a division of essential accidents the subject and essential accidents the predicate. For example: 'al-amm alladhi khuss 'inda al-ba'd yufid al-mutlaq'. Now 'al-amm alladhi khuss 'inda al-ba'd' is a division of accidents and occurs as the subject of the proposition, and 'yufid al-mutlaq' is the predicate and is one of the accidents.

And all discussions of usul: This is the third part of the commentary's text. From here the commentator summarized the preceding discussion: that all discussions mentioned in usul al-fiqh are mentioned to establish its essential accidents. Because the subject matters are two: the accidents of the proofs (adillah) are what establish (muthbit) them, and the accidents of the rulings (ahkam) are what are established (thabit) by them. These are essential accidents. The summary is that discussion in usul al-fiqh will be about affirmation (ithbat) and establishment (thubut), and about those things that have a role in affirmation and establishment.

Now if you say: This is the last part of the text; the purpose is to mention a question and answer it. Objection: The subject matter of usul al-fiqh is proofs and rulings. The proofs include the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). So why is it that the usuli discusses consensus and analogy, but does not discuss the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah? That is, they discuss the authority (hujjiyya) of consensus and analogy, but do not discuss the authority of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.

Answer (1): This objection does not even arise, because discussion does take place regarding the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah — regarding specific, general, common, ambiguous, equivocal, etc., all of which are included in the Book of Allah. But this answer is weak, because there is a difference between discussing the quality of being hujja of the Book and Sunnah, and discussing the very hujja [itself].
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage from the sharh (commentary) of al-Tawdih explains two main topics: (1) the classification of accidents ('arad) in logic, specifically essential (dhati) and extraneous (gharib) accidents, and (2) how these concepts apply to the method of discussion in usul al-fiqh. The commentator first corrects an example for the first type of essential accident, emphasizing that attributes of Allah like knowledge and power are attached without any medium. Then he lays out three types of essential accidents: (a) where the medium is a part of the substratum that is more general (e.g., motion for man via animal), (b) where the medium is external and equal (e.g., laughter for man via wonder), and (c) where the medium is external and more general (but this is actually part of extraneous accidents as per the later scholars). The text then provides three types of extraneous accidents: (a) medium more general than substratum (e.g., motion for white via body), (b) medium more specific (e.g., laughter for animal via man), and (c) medium contrary (e.g., heat for water via fire). A benefit clarifies that the classification with the medium being more general in the third type is according to the later scholars (muta'akkhirin), while earlier scholars (mutaqaddimin) did not require the medium to be more general. The second part of the passage explains the method of constructing propositions in usul al-fiqh: the subject matter of the science (e.g., the Book of Allah) or its divisions can be the subject, and one of its essential accidents (like being definitive, general, etc.) can be the predicate. Four methods are illustrated. The commentator then summarizes that all usul discussions aim to establish the essential accidents of the proofs and rulings. Finally, an objection is raised: why do usulis discuss the authority of ijma and qiyas but not that of Quran and Sunnah? The given answer (that discussions of specific/general etc. constitute discussion) is deemed weak, because there is a difference between discussing the modality of hujjiyya and the essence of hujjiyya. The text ends abruptly, leaving the stronger answer incomplete.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی ('arad dhati): An accident that is external to the essence of the substratum but is predicated on it through something that is either part of the substratum (and more general) or external and equal/specific/contrary.
بحث (bahth): Discussion or investigation in a science; specifically, the method of forming propositions to establish essential accidents.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science, e.g., proofs and rulings in usul al-fiqh; also the subject of a proposition.
محمول (mahmul): The predicate in a proposition; in usul al-fiqh discussions, it is an accident (like being definitive) that is affirmed of the subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many methods of forming propositions in usul al-fiqh are mentioned in the passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
All usul discussions aim to establish essential accidents of proofs and rulings; the four methods of forming propositions are tools for this purpose, and the objection about discussing hujjiyya reveals the need for precision.

Method of Learning

8 min
Four Methods of Framing Propositions in Usul al-Fiqh
Describes four ways to form propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four ways to formulate propositions about the subject matter of usul al-fiqh and apply them to generate valid propositions.

Core Idea
The subject of usul al-fiqh can be combined with its essential accidents in four distinct propositional forms.

This passage demonstrates the method of constructing the issues (masa'il) of usul al-fiqh by combining the subject (mawdu') with its essential accidents (awāriḍ dhātiyya) as predicates or subjects. Understanding this helps us see how each topic in usul al-fiqh is framed.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Subject (mawdu') and Essential Accidents (awāriḍ dhātiyya)
The subject of usul al-fiqh is the proofs (adilla) of Islamic law. Essential accidents are properties like being definitive, probable, general, or specific. Identify which elements in a proposition serve as subject and which as predicate.
2
Apply Method 1: Subject from the science's subject, predicate from accidents
Take the subject of the science (e.g., 'the Book of Allah') and make it the subject of a proposition. Take an accident (e.g., being definitive) as the predicate. Example: 'The Book of Allah gives definitiveness' (الكتاب يفيد القطع).
Here 'the Book' is the subject, 'gives definitiveness' is the predicate.
3
Apply Method 2: A division of the subject as subject, an accident as predicate
Take a subdivision of the science's subject (e.g., 'the command') as the subject and an accident as predicate. Example: 'The command gives definitiveness' (الأمر يفيد القطع).
'The command' is a division of the Book's legislative speech.
4
Apply Methods 3 and 4: Accidents as subject with other accidents as predicate
Method 3: Take an essential accident itself (e.g., 'the general') as subject and another accident as predicate. Example: 'The general gives definitiveness'. Method 4: Take a division of an accident (e.g., 'the general that has been specified') as subject and an accident as predicate.
These show that even the accidents themselves can become subjects of investigation.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الترويح لحل التوضيح والتلويح
اور وہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کو قضیہ کا موضوع بنادو اور عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے کسی عرض ذاتی کو معمول بنادو یہ کیفیت بحث ہے مثلاً اصول فقہ کا موضوع کتاب اللہ ہے اس کو قضیہ کا موضوع بنا دو اور عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے کسی عرض ذاتی مثلا قطعی ہونا یا خنی ہونے کو عام خاص وغیرہ کو معمول بنا دو اب عبارت ہوگی الكتاب يفيد القطع ۔ اب الكتاب موضوع ہے يفيد القطع محمول ہے اور قطعی ہونا عارض ہے دوسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بنا ئیں اور عوارض میں سے کسی کو معمول بنائیں جیسے الامر يفيد القطع اب الامر یہ کتاب اللہ کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یفید القطع یہ عوارض میں سے ایک عرض ہے جو قضیہ کا محمول واقع ہے۔ تیسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ عوارض ذاتیہ کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کو معمول بناؤ مثلاً العام يفيد القطع اب عام خاص ہونا وغیرہ یہ عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے ہیں تو العام یہ موضوع ہے اور قطعی ہونا محمول ہے چوتھا طریقہ - عوارض ذاتیہ کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کوحمول بناؤ مثلا العام الذي خص عند البعض يفيد القطع اب عام خص عنہ اعبض یہ عوارض کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یغید الفطن یہ معمول ہے اور عوارض میں سے ایک عارض ہے۔
وجميع مباحث الاصول ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے خلاصہ بیان کیا ہے ماقبل والی بحث کا کہ اصول فقہ میں جتنی مباحث ذکر کی جاتی ہیں وہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کرنے کے لیے ذکر کی جاتی ہیں کیونکہ موضوع دو ہیں ادلہ کے عوارض ان کا مثبت ہوتا ہے اور احکام کے عوارض ان کا ثابت ہوتا ہے یہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں خلاصہ یہ نکلا کہ اصول فقہ میں بحث اثبات وثبوت سے ہوگی اور ان چیزوں سے ہوگی جن کو اثبات و ثبوت میں دخل ہے۔
فان قلت - یہ عبات کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض ایک سوال ذکر کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع اولہ اور احکام ہیں۔ ادلہ میں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول الله اجماع اور قیاس سب داخل ہیں ۔ پھر کیا وجہ ہے کہ اصولی اجماع اور قیاس سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ سے بحث نہیں کرتے یعنی اجماع وقیاس کے حجت ہونے سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ اللہ کے حجت ہونے سے بحث نہیں کرتے۔ جواب (۱):۔ یہ اعترض ہی وارد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بحث ہوتی ہے کہ خاص عام مشترک مجمل متشابه و غیرہ سب کتاب اللہ میں داخل ہیں۔ لیکن یہ جواب کمز رو ہے کیونکہ ایک ہوتا ہے کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ کی کیفیت حجت سے بحث کرنا اور دوسرانفس حجت ہونے سے بحث کرنا ۔ تو اصول فقہ میں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ کی کیفیت حجت سے بحث ہوتی ہے کہ کس کیفیت سے استنباط کیا جائے اور ان کے نفس حجت ہونے سے بحث نہیں ہوتی جبکہ اعتراض دوسری جہت سے ہے۔ جواب (۲): قلت سے شارع نے مذکورہ اعتراض کا جواب دیا کہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت اسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا حجت ہونا بدیہی ہے اور اصولیین بحث کرتے ہیں نظری و کسی سے خلاصہ یہ کہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت کا حجت ہوتاہد یہی تھا اور اجماع وقیاس کا حجت ہونا نظری تھا اس لیے اصولیین حجیت اجماع و قیاس سے بحث کرتے ہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ کتاب اللہ کی بعض وہ قسمیں جو نظری ہیں مثلاً قراءات شاذہ کا حجت ہونا اور سنت کی وہ قسمیں جو نظری ہیں مثلاً خبر واحد کا حجت ہونا تو اصولیین ان سے بھی بحث کرتے ہیں۔
فَيُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الأَدِلَّةِ المَذْكُورَةِ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا ) الْفَاءِ فِي قَوْلِهِ فَيُبْحَثُ مُتَعَلَّقَ بِحَدٌ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ أَى إِذَا كَانَ حَدٌ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ هَذَا يَجِبُ أَنْ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الأَدِلَّةِ وَالأحْكَامِ وَمُتَعَلَّقَاتِهِما وَالْمُرَادُ بِالأحْوَالِ الْعَوَارِضُ الذَّاتِيَّةُ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا عَطْفٌ عَلَى الأُدِلَّةِ وَالضَّمِيرُ فِي قَوْلِهِ بِهَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الأَدِلَّةِ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا هُوَ الَّا دِلَّهُ الْمُخْتَلَفُ فِيهَا كَاسْتِصْحَابِ الْحَالِ وَالاسْتِحْسَانِ وَأدِلَّةِ المُقَلدِ وَالْمُسْتَفْتِي وَأَيْضًا مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالأدِلَّةِ الأَرْبَعَةِ مِمَّا لَهُ مَدْخَلٌ فِي كَوْنِهَا مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلْحُكْمِ كَالْبَحْثِ عَنْ الْاجْتِهَادِ وَنَحْوِهِ . وَاعْلَمُ أَنَّ الْعَوَارِضَ الدَّانِيَّةَ لِلادِلَّةِ ثَلَاثَةُ أَقْسَامٍ مِنْهَا الْعَوَارِضُ النَّانِيَّةُ الْمَبْحُوتُ عَنْهَا وَهِيَ كَوْنُهَا مُقْبِتَةٌ لِلأحْكَامِ وَمِنْهَا مَا لَيْسَتْ بِمَبْعُوثٍ عَنْهَا لَكِنُ لَهَا مَدْخَلٌ فِي لُحُوقِ مَا هِيَ مَبْحُوتُ عَنْهَا كَكَوْنِهَا عَامَّةً أَوْ مُشْتَرَكَةً أَوْ خَبَرَ وَاحِدٍ وَأَمْثَالَ ذَلِكَ وَمِنْهَا مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ كَكَونِهَا قَدِيمًا أَوْ حَادِثًا أَوْ غَيْرَهَا فَالْقِسْمُ الْأَوَّلُ يَقَعُ مَحْمُولَاتٍ فِى الْقَضَايَا الَّتِي هِيَ مَسَائِلُ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ وَالْقِسْمُ الثَّانِي يَقَعُ أوْصَافًا وَأَبُودًا لِمَوْضُوع تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا كَقَوْلِنَا الْخَبَرُ الَّذِى يَرْوِيهِ وَاحِدٌ يُوجِبُ
Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. And it is that you make the subject of the science the subject of a proposition, and from the essential accidents you make some accident the predicate. This is the mode of investigation. For example, the subject of usul al-fiqh is the Book of Allah. Make it the subject of a proposition, and from the essential accidents, like being definitive or probable, general or specific, etc., make it the predicate. So the phrase becomes: 'The Book gives definitiveness.' Here 'the Book' is the subject, 'gives definitiveness' is the predicate, and definitiveness is an accident. The second method is that you make some division of the subject of the science a subject, and from the accidents make something a predicate, like: 'The command gives definitiveness.' Here 'the command' is a division of the Book of Allah and is the subject of the proposition, and 'gives definitiveness' is one of the accidents that is the predicate of the proposition. The third method is that you make the essential accidents the subject and the essential accidents the predicate, e.g., 'The general gives definitiveness.' Here 'general/specific' etc. are among the essential accidents, so 'the general' is the subject and definitiveness is the predicate. The fourth method: you make some division of the essential accidents the subject and the essential accidents the predicate, e.g., 'The general that has been specified according to some gives [؟].' Here 'general specified by some' is a division of the accidents and is the subject of the proposition, and 'gives [؟]' is the predicate and is one of the accidents. And all topics of usul: This is the third part of the commentary's phrase. From here, the commentator summarizes the previous discussion: that all the topics mentioned in usul al-fiqh are mentioned to affirm its essential accidents, because the subject (mawdu') is two: the accidents of the proofs (adilla) are what they affirm, and the accidents of the rulings (ahkam) are what are affirmed by them. These are essential accidents. The summary is that discussion in usul al-fiqh will be about affirmation and being affirmed, and about those things that have bearing on affirmation and being affirmed. Then there is a question: This is the last part of the phrase, to mention an objection and answer it. Objection: The subject of usul al-fiqh is the proofs and the rulings. The proofs include the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus, and analogy. So why do usuli scholars discuss consensus and analogy but not the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah? That is, they discuss the hujja status of consensus and analogy, but do not discuss the hujja status of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. Answer (1): This objection does not even arise, because discussion occurs about the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah—like specific, general, ambiguous, unclear, etc.—all are included in the Book of Allah. But this answer is weak, because one thing is discussing the quality of being hujja of the Book and Sunnah, and another is discussing their very being hujja. So in usul al-fiqh, discussion occurs about the quality of being hujja of the Book and Sunnah—i.e., by what quality deduction is made—and not about their very being hujja, whereas the objection is about the latter aspect. Answer (2): The commentator answered the mentioned objection that the hujja status of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah is intuitive (badihi), and usuli scholars discuss only the theoretical (nazari). Summary: The hujja status of the Book and Sunnah was intuitive, and the hujja status of consensus and analogy was theoretical, so usuli scholars discuss the hujja status of consensus and analogy. This is also the reason that some divisions of the Book that are theoretical, like the hujja status of anomalous readings (qira'at shadhdha), and divisions of the Sunnah that are theoretical, such as the hujja status of solitary reports (khabar wahid), are also discussed by usuli scholars. Therefore, discussion in it is about the states of the mentioned proofs and what relates to them. The 'fa' in his saying 'fayubhathu' is connected to the definition of this science: i.e., if the definition of usul al-fiqh is this, then discussion must be in it about the states of the proofs and rulings and their related matters. By 'states' is meant essential accidents. 'And what relates to them' is coordinate to 'proofs', and the pronoun in 'biha' refers to the proofs. 'What relates to them' are the disputed proofs like istishab al-hal, istihsan, the proofs of the muqallid and the mustafti, and also what relates to the four proofs that has bearing on their being affirming of the ruling, like discussion about ijtihad and the like. Know that the essential accidents of the proofs are three categories: from them are the essential accidents that are investigated, which is their being affirming of rulings; from them are what are not investigated but have bearing on the attachment of what is investigated, like their being general or shared or solitary report and the like; and from them are what are not like that, such as being pre-eternal or temporal or other. So the first category occur as predicates in the propositions that are the issues of this science; the second category occur as descriptions and states of the subject of those propositions, like our saying: 'A tradition narrated by one person makes obligatory...'
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of usul al-fiqh, explaining its subject matter and the types of discussions within it. The author first outlines four ways to formulate propositions about the science's subject, showing that the essential accidents (awāriḍ dhātiyya) can serve as predicate or subject in different combinations. Then he clarifies that all topics in usul al-fiqh aim to affirm these essential accidents. A key point is that the proofs (adilla) have accidents that they affirm, while rulings (aḥkām) have accidents that are affirmed by them. The passage then addresses an important objection: why do usuli scholars discuss consensus and analogy but not the Qur'an and Sunnah as proof? The first answer (weak) says they do discuss the Qur'an and Sunnah but in terms of specific vs. general etc. The stronger answer is that the hujja status of Qur'an and Sunnah is self-evident (badīhī), so no discussion is needed, whereas consensus and analogy are theoretical (naẓarī). However, subcategories like anomalous readings or solitary reports are also discussed because they are not self-evident. The final part classifies essential accidents of proofs into three: those directly investigated (being affirmative of rulings), those that have bearing on the investigation (e.g., being general or specific), and those irrelevant (like being created or eternal). The first type become predicates in the science's issues, the second become attributes of the subject.

Key Terms
عوارض ذاتية (awāriḍ dhātiyya): Essential accidents: properties that are necessary attributes of the subject for the purpose of the science, such as being definitive or probable for a proof.
قضية (qaḍiyya): Proposition: a statement consisting of a subject and predicate that is either true or false. In usul, propositions form the issues (masa'il) of the science.
موضوع (mawḍūʿ): Subject: that which is being studied in a discipline. For usul al-fiqh, it is the proofs of fiqh and the rulings derived from them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which method is used in the proposition 'The command gives definitiveness'?
A) Method 1: subject from science's subject
B) Method 2: a division of the subject as subject
C) Method 3: accident as subject
D) Method 4: a division of an accident as subject

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh frames its issues by combining the subject proofs or their essential accidents in four distinct propositional forms.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
The Hujjiyya of Proofs and the Three Categories of Essential Accidents
Addresses an objection and classifies essential accidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the hujjiyya of the Qur'an and Sunnah is not discussed in usul al-fiqh, and classify essential accidents of proofs into three categories.

Core Idea
The hujjiyya of primary proofs is self-evident; only theoretical proofs and qualities of proofs are investigated.

This passage addresses a common objection: why do usuli scholars discuss consensus and qiyas but not the Qur'an and Sunnah? The key is that the hujjiyya (proof status) of the Qur'an and Sunnah is intuitive (badihi), while that of consensus and qiyas is theoretical (nazari). The passage also classifies essential accidents into three types, clarifying what is directly investigated and what is indirectly relevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection and Its Two Aspects
The objection distinguishes between discussing the 'quality' of being hujja (e.g., how to derive from it) and the 'very fact' of being hujja. The usuli discusses the quality, not the fact, for primary sources.
The first answer given is weak; the strong answer uses the badihi/nazari distinction.
2
Understand the Badihi vs Nazari Distinction
Badihi means self-evident, requiring no proof. Nazari means requiring theoretical investigation. The hujjiyya of Qur'an and Mutawatir Sunnah is badihi; therefore not discussed. But for subcategories like shadhdh readings or khabar wahid, it is nazari, so they are discussed.
This explains why ijma and qiyas are discussed: their hujjiyya is nazari.
3
Learn the Three Categories of Essential Accidents
First category: directly investigated accidents (e.g., being affirmative of rulings). Second: not directly investigated but have bearing (e.g., being general, specific, solitary). Third: irrelevant accidents (e.g., being created or eternal).
The first category becomes predicate; the second becomes description of subject.
4
Apply the Categories to a Proposition
Example: 'A solitary report (khabar wahid) makes obligatory' – here 'solitary report' is a second category accident (not directly investigated but bearing), and 'makes obligatory' is a first category accident (directly investigated).
This shows how the framework works in practice.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الترويح لحل التوضيح والتلويح
اور وہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کو قضیہ کا موضوع بنادو اور عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے کسی عرض ذاتی کو معمول بنادو یہ کیفیت بحث ہے مثلاً اصول فقہ کا موضوع کتاب اللہ ہے اس کو قضیہ کا موضوع بنا دو اور عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے کسی عرض ذاتی مثلا قطعی ہونا یا خنی ہونے کو عام خاص وغیرہ کو معمول بنا دو اب عبارت ہوگی الكتاب يفيد القطع ۔ اب الكتاب موضوع ہے يفيد القطع محمول ہے اور قطعی ہونا عارض ہے دوسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ علم کے موضوع کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بنا ئیں اور عوارض میں سے کسی کو معمول بنائیں جیسے الامر يفيد القطع اب الامر یہ کتاب اللہ کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یفید القطع یہ عوارض میں سے ایک عرض ہے جو قضیہ کا محمول واقع ہے۔ تیسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ عوارض ذاتیہ کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کو معمول بناؤ مثلاً العام يفيد القطع اب عام خاص ہونا وغیرہ یہ عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے ہیں تو العام یہ موضوع ہے اور قطعی ہونا محمول ہے چوتھا طریقہ - عوارض ذاتیہ کی کسی قسم کو موضوع بناؤ اور عوارض ذاتیہ کوحمول بناؤ مثلا العام الذي خص عند البعض يفيد القطع اب عام خص عنہ اعبض یہ عوارض کی قسم ہے اور قضیہ کا موضوع واقع ہے اور یغید الفطن یہ معمول ہے اور عوارض میں سے ایک عارض ہے۔
وجميع مباحث الاصول ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے خلاصہ بیان کیا ہے ماقبل والی بحث کا کہ اصول فقہ میں جتنی مباحث ذکر کی جاتی ہیں وہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کرنے کے لیے ذکر کی جاتی ہیں کیونکہ موضوع دو ہیں ادلہ کے عوارض ان کا مثبت ہوتا ہے اور احکام کے عوارض ان کا ثابت ہوتا ہے یہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں خلاصہ یہ نکلا کہ اصول فقہ میں بحث اثبات وثبوت سے ہوگی اور ان چیزوں سے ہوگی جن کو اثبات و ثبوت میں دخل ہے۔
فان قلت - یہ عبات کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض ایک سوال ذکر کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع اولہ اور احکام ہیں۔ ادلہ میں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول الله اجماع اور قیاس سب داخل ہیں ۔ پھر کیا وجہ ہے کہ اصولی اجماع اور قیاس سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ سے بحث نہیں کرتے یعنی اجماع وقیاس کے حجت ہونے سے بحث کرتے ہیں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ اللہ کے حجت ہونے سے بحث نہیں کرتے۔ جواب (۱):۔ یہ اعترض ہی وارد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بحث ہوتی ہے کہ خاص عام مشترک مجمل متشابه و غیرہ سب کتاب اللہ میں داخل ہیں۔ لیکن یہ جواب کمز رو ہے کیونکہ ایک ہوتا ہے کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ کی کیفیت حجت سے بحث کرنا اور دوسرانفس حجت ہونے سے بحث کرنا ۔ تو اصول فقہ میں کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ کی کیفیت حجت سے بحث ہوتی ہے کہ کس کیفیت سے استنباط کیا جائے اور ان کے نفس حجت ہونے سے بحث نہیں ہوتی جبکہ اعتراض دوسری جہت سے ہے۔ جواب (۲): قلت سے شارع نے مذکورہ اعتراض کا جواب دیا کہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت اسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا حجت ہونا بدیہی ہے اور اصولیین بحث کرتے ہیں نظری و کسی سے خلاصہ یہ کہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت کا حجت ہوتاہد یہی تھا اور اجماع وقیاس کا حجت ہونا نظری تھا اس لیے اصولیین حجیت اجماع و قیاس سے بحث کرتے ہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ کتاب اللہ کی بعض وہ قسمیں جو نظری ہیں مثلاً قراءات شاذہ کا حجت ہونا اور سنت کی وہ قسمیں جو نظری ہیں مثلاً خبر واحد کا حجت ہونا تو اصولیین ان سے بھی بحث کرتے ہیں۔
فَيُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الأَدِلَّةِ المَذْكُورَةِ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا ) الْفَاءِ فِي قَوْلِهِ فَيُبْحَثُ مُتَعَلَّقَ بِحَدٌ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ أَى إِذَا كَانَ حَدٌ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ هَذَا يَجِبُ أَنْ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الأَدِلَّةِ وَالأحْكَامِ وَمُتَعَلَّقَاتِهِما وَالْمُرَادُ بِالأحْوَالِ الْعَوَارِضُ الذَّاتِيَّةُ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا عَطْفٌ عَلَى الأُدِلَّةِ وَالضَّمِيرُ فِي قَوْلِهِ بِهَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الأَدِلَّةِ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا هُوَ الَّا دِلَّهُ الْمُخْتَلَفُ فِيهَا كَاسْتِصْحَابِ الْحَالِ وَالاسْتِحْسَانِ وَأدِلَّةِ المُقَلدِ وَالْمُسْتَفْتِي وَأَيْضًا مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالأدِلَّةِ الأَرْبَعَةِ مِمَّا لَهُ مَدْخَلٌ فِي كَوْنِهَا مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلْحُكْمِ كَالْبَحْثِ عَنْ الْاجْتِهَادِ وَنَحْوِهِ . وَاعْلَمُ أَنَّ الْعَوَارِضَ الدَّانِيَّةَ لِلادِلَّةِ ثَلَاثَةُ أَقْسَامٍ مِنْهَا الْعَوَارِضُ النَّانِيَّةُ الْمَبْحُوتُ عَنْهَا وَهِيَ كَوْنُهَا مُقْبِتَةٌ لِلأحْكَامِ وَمِنْهَا مَا لَيْسَتْ بِمَبْعُوثٍ عَنْهَا لَكِنُ لَهَا مَدْخَلٌ فِي لُحُوقِ مَا هِيَ مَبْحُوتُ عَنْهَا كَكَوْنِهَا عَامَّةً أَوْ مُشْتَرَكَةً أَوْ خَبَرَ وَاحِدٍ وَأَمْثَالَ ذَلِكَ وَمِنْهَا مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ كَكَونِهَا قَدِيمًا أَوْ حَادِثًا أَوْ غَيْرَهَا فَالْقِسْمُ الْأَوَّلُ يَقَعُ مَحْمُولَاتٍ فِى الْقَضَايَا الَّتِي هِيَ مَسَائِلُ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ وَالْقِسْمُ الثَّانِي يَقَعُ أوْصَافًا وَأَبُودًا لِمَوْضُوع تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا كَقَوْلِنَا الْخَبَرُ الَّذِى يَرْوِيهِ وَاحِدٌ يُوجِبُ
Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. And it is that you make the subject of the science the subject of a proposition, and from the essential accidents you make some accident the predicate. This is the mode of investigation. For example, the subject of usul al-fiqh is the Book of Allah. Make it the subject of a proposition, and from the essential accidents, like being definitive or probable, general or specific, etc., make it the predicate. So the phrase becomes: 'The Book gives definitiveness.' Here 'the Book' is the subject, 'gives definitiveness' is the predicate, and definitiveness is an accident. The second method is that you make some division of the subject of the science a subject, and from the accidents make something a predicate, like: 'The command gives definitiveness.' Here 'the command' is a division of the Book of Allah and is the subject of the proposition, and 'gives definitiveness' is one of the accidents that is the predicate of the proposition. The third method is that you make the essential accidents the subject and the essential accidents the predicate, e.g., 'The general gives definitiveness.' Here 'general/specific' etc. are among the essential accidents, so 'the general' is the subject and definitiveness is the predicate. The fourth method: you make some division of the essential accidents the subject and the essential accidents the predicate, e.g., 'The general that has been specified according to some gives [؟].' Here 'general specified by some' is a division of the accidents and is the subject of the proposition, and 'gives [؟]' is the predicate and is one of the accidents. And all topics of usul: This is the third part of the commentary's phrase. From here, the commentator summarizes the previous discussion: that all the topics mentioned in usul al-fiqh are mentioned to affirm its essential accidents, because the subject (mawdu') is two: the accidents of the proofs (adilla) are what they affirm, and the accidents of the rulings (ahkam) are what are affirmed by them. These are essential accidents. The summary is that discussion in usul al-fiqh will be about affirmation and being affirmed, and about those things that have bearing on affirmation and being affirmed. Then there is a question: This is the last part of the phrase, to mention an objection and answer it. Objection: The subject of usul al-fiqh is the proofs and the rulings. The proofs include the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus, and analogy. So why do usuli scholars discuss consensus and analogy but not the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah? That is, they discuss the hujja status of consensus and analogy, but do not discuss the hujja status of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. Answer (1): This objection does not even arise, because discussion occurs about the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah—like specific, general, ambiguous, unclear, etc.—all are included in the Book of Allah. But this answer is weak, because one thing is discussing the quality of being hujja of the Book and Sunnah, and another is discussing their very being hujja. So in usul al-fiqh, discussion occurs about the quality of being hujja of the Book and Sunnah—i.e., by what quality deduction is made—and not about their very being hujja, whereas the objection is about the latter aspect. Answer (2): The commentator answered the mentioned objection that the hujja status of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah is intuitive (badihi), and usuli scholars discuss only the theoretical (nazari). Summary: The hujja status of the Book and Sunnah was intuitive, and the hujja status of consensus and analogy was theoretical, so usuli scholars discuss the hujja status of consensus and analogy. This is also the reason that some divisions of the Book that are theoretical, like the hujja status of anomalous readings (qira'at shadhdha), and divisions of the Sunnah that are theoretical, such as the hujja status of solitary reports (khabar wahid), are also discussed by usuli scholars. Therefore, discussion in it is about the states of the mentioned proofs and what relates to them. The 'fa' in his saying 'fayubhathu' is connected to the definition of this science: i.e., if the definition of usul al-fiqh is this, then discussion must be in it about the states of the proofs and rulings and their related matters. By 'states' is meant essential accidents. 'And what relates to them' is coordinate to 'proofs', and the pronoun in 'biha' refers to the proofs. 'What relates to them' are the disputed proofs like istishab al-hal, istihsan, the proofs of the muqallid and the mustafti, and also what relates to the four proofs that has bearing on their being affirming of the ruling, like discussion about ijtihad and the like. Know that the essential accidents of the proofs are three categories: from them are the essential accidents that are investigated, which is their being affirming of rulings; from them are what are not investigated but have bearing on the attachment of what is investigated, like their being general or shared or solitary report and the like; and from them are what are not like that, such as being pre-eternal or temporal or other. So the first category occur as predicates in the propositions that are the issues of this science; the second category occur as descriptions and states of the subject of those propositions, like our saying: 'A tradition narrated by one person makes obligatory...'
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of usul al-fiqh, explaining its subject matter and the types of discussions within it. The author first outlines four ways to formulate propositions about the science's subject, showing that the essential accidents (awāriḍ dhātiyya) can serve as predicate or subject in different combinations. Then he clarifies that all topics in usul al-fiqh aim to affirm these essential accidents. A key point is that the proofs (adilla) have accidents that they affirm, while rulings (aḥkām) have accidents that are affirmed by them. The passage then addresses an important objection: why do usuli scholars discuss consensus and analogy but not the Qur'an and Sunnah as proof? The first answer (weak) says they do discuss the Qur'an and Sunnah but in terms of specific vs. general etc. The stronger answer is that the hujja status of Qur'an and Sunnah is self-evident (badīhī), so no discussion is needed, whereas consensus and analogy are theoretical (naẓarī). However, subcategories like anomalous readings or solitary reports are also discussed because they are not self-evident. The final part classifies essential accidents of proofs into three: those directly investigated (being affirmative of rulings), those that have bearing on the investigation (e.g., being general or specific), and those irrelevant (like being created or eternal). The first type become predicates in the science's issues, the second become attributes of the subject.

Key Terms
بديهي (badīhī): Self-evident, requiring no proof. The hujjiyya of Qur'an and mutawatir Sunnah is badihi.
نظري (naẓarī): Theoretical, requiring investigation. The hujjiyya of ijma, qiyas, khabar wahid is nazari.
حجية (hujjiyya): The quality of being a valid proof (hujja) that must be followed. The text distinguishes between badihi and nazari hujjiyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which category of essential accidents does 'being general' (ʿumūm) belong to?
A) Category 1: directly investigated accidents
B) Category 2: not directly investigated but have bearing
C) Category 3: irrelevant accidents
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The scope of usul al-fiqh is limited to theoretical investigation; self-evident matters like the hujjiyya of primary proofs are excluded.
