مَنْسُوبَةٌ إلَى الصّحَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ الْغَايَةُ فِى ذَلِكَ الْعِلْمِ فَعُلِمَ أَنَّهُمْ لَمْ يُهْمِلُوا رِعَايَةَ مَعْنَى يُوجِبُ الْوَحْدَةَ وَأَنْ لَيْسَ لِأحَدٍ أَنْ يَصْطَلِحَ عَلَى أَنَّ الْفِقْهَ وَالْهَنْدَسَةَ عِلْمٌ وَاحِدٌ مَوْضُوعُهُ فِعْلُ الْمُكَلَّفِ وَالْمِقْدَارُ ثُمَّ أَنَّهُ فِيمَا أَوْرَدَ مِنْ الْمِثَالَيْنِ مُنَافِضٌ نَفْسَهُ ؛ لأنَّ مَوْضُوعَ الْأُصُولِ أَشْيَاء كَثِيرَةٌ ، إِذْ مَحْمُوَلَاتُ مَسَائِلِهِ لَيْسَتْ أَعْرَاضًا ذَاتِيَّةٌ لِمَفهومِ الدَّلِيلِ ، بَلْ لِلْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ عَلَى
الانْفِرَادِ أَو التَّشَارُكِ بَيْنَ اثْنَيْنِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ ، وَكَذَا التَّصَوُّرُ وَالتَّصْدِيقُ فِي الْمَنْطِقِ . ترجمہ :۔ اور اس میں نظر ہے کیونکہ اگر مراد لیا جائے اختلاف مسائل سے محض ان مسائل کا کیٹر ہونا تو پھر ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ بیشک وہ ثابت کرتا ہے اختلاف علم کو اور ظاہر ہے کہ بیشک علم واحد کے مسائل کثیر ہوتے ہیں لازمی طور پر اور اگر مراد لیا جائے مسائل کا عدم تناسب تو ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ بیشک موضوعات کا محض کثیر ہونا ثابت کرتا ہے اس (عدم تناسب ) کو سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ لازم آتا ہے یہ اگر نہ ہوں موضوعات کثیرہ متناسبہ (پینھم ) حالا تک قوم نے صراحت کی ہے کہ بیشک اشیاء کثیر ہ سوائے اس کے نہیں وہ موضوع ہوتی ہیں ایک علم کا تناسب کی شرط کیسا تھ اور وجہ تناسب ان کا مشترک ہونا ہے ذاتی میں جیسا کہ مخط اور سطح اور جسم تعلیمی علم ہندسہ کے لیے کیونکہ یہ مشترک ہیں جنس میں اور وہ مقدار ہے یعنی وہ کم متصل جو قار الذات ہو یا عرضی میں جیسا کہ بدن انسانی اور اس کے اجزاء اور غذائیں اور ادویات اور ارکان اور مزاج وغیرہ ان کو جب موضوع بنالیا جائے علم طب کا تو بیشک یہ مشترک ہیں ان کے منسوب ہونے میں صحت کی طرف وہ جو غایت اور مقصود ہے اس علم میں پس معلوم ہوا کہ نہیں مہمل چھوڑا انہوں نے ایسے معنی کی رعایت کو جو ثابت کرے وحدت کو ۔ اور بیشک نہیں ہے جائز ہر ایک کے لئے یہ کہ اصطلاح قائم کرلے اس بات پر کہ فقہ اور ہندسہ ایک علم ہیں اور اس کا موضوع فعل مکلف اور مقدار ہے۔ پھر بیشک جس میں اس نے دو مثالیں ذکر کی ہیں وہ خود اپنے معارض ہیں کیونکہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع اشیاء کثیرہ ہیں کیونکہ اس کے مسائل کے محمولات نہیں ہیں اعراض ذاتیہ دلیل کے مفہوم کیلئے بلکہ کتاب وسنت اور اجماع و قیاس منفرد ہو کر اور مشترک ہو کر ہر دو کے درمیان یا کثیر کے درمیان اور اسی طرح تصور و تصدیق منطق کیلئے ۔
شاریخ کی طرف سے تعدد موضوع کے بطلان پر دلیل کارد
تشریح: وفیہ نظر : منصف نے علم واحد کے موضوع کے تعدد کے ابطال پر جو دلیل پیش کی تھی اس کا حاصل دو مقدمے تھے .

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج
پہلا مقدمہ تھا کہ موضوعات کا اختلاف مسائل کے اختلاف کو ستلزم ہے اور دوسرا مقدمہ تھا کہ مسائل کا اختلاف علم کے اختلاف
کوستلزم ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا موضوعات کا اختلاف مسائل کے اختلاف کو مستلزم ہے اس سے تمہاری کیا مراد ہے؟ اس لیے کہ اس کے دو معنے ہو سکتے ہیں (۱) مسائل کا اختلاف بمعنی کثرت مسائل کے ہو (۲) مسائل کا اختلاف بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل ہو ۔ اب بتاؤ کہ کونا معنی مراد ہے؟ بالمعنی الاول مراد ہے یا بالمعنی الثانی مراد ہے اگر آپ کثرت مسائل بالمعنی الاول مراد لیتے ہیں تو مقدمہ اولی سو فیصد مسلم ہے کہ اختلاف موضوع مستلزم ہے اختلاف مسائل بمعنی کثرت مسائل کو لیکن دوسرا مقدمہ تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ اختلاف مسائل اختلاف علم کو ستلزم ہو اس لئے کہ ہر علم کے ہزاروں مسائل ہیں کوئی علم بھی ایسا نہیں ہے ج کا صرف ایک ھی مسئلہ ہو لھذا کثرت مسائل کثرت علم کوستلزم نہیں ہے اور اگر اختلاف بالمعنی الثانی مراد ہے پھر مقدمہ اولی کو ہم علی الاطلاق تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ موضوعات کا اختلاف مسائل کے اختلاف کومستلزم ہوتا ہے بلکہ اسمیں تفصیل ہے کہ اختلاف موضوع کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ موضوعات میں کثرت ہو لیکن آپس میں متناسب نہ ہوں (۲) دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ موضوعات میں کثرت ہو اور آپس میں متناسب بھی ہوں۔ اگر موضوعات میں تعدد اور آپس میں کوئی مناسبت نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں موضوعات کا اختلاف اختلاف مسائل بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل گوستلزم ہوگا۔ اور اگر مسائل آپس میں مناسب ہوں تو پھر یہ قطعا اختلاف مسائل بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل کو تلزم نہیں ہے اور جمہور بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں کہ موضوعات میں تعدد جائز ہے بشرطیکہ ان میں تناسب ہو اور یہ اختلاف مسائل بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل گوستلزم نہیں ہے کہ تم یہ کہو کہ یہ اختلاف علم کو ستلزم ہے۔
تناسب کی صورتیں :۔ تناسب کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) ان کا امر ذاتی میں اشتراک ہو (۲) امر عرضی میں اشتراک ہوامر ذاتی میں اشتراک کی مثال جیسے علم ھندسہ کا موضوع تین چیزیں ہیں۔ خط سطح اور جسم تعلیمی لیکن یہ تینوں امر ذاتی میں مشترک ہیں اور وہ ہے مقدار یعنی کم متصل قار الذات جسکے اجزاء مجتمع فی الوجود ہوں۔ امر عرضی میں اشتراک کی مثال ۔ جیسے علم طلب کا موضوع بدن انسانی ہے اور اجزاء بدنی جیسے ناک کان دل وغیرہ ہیں علم طب میں ان سے بھی بحث ہوتی ہے ایسے ہی دوائیں ہیں غذا ئیں ہیں اور ارکان ہیں یعنی صفراء کا غالب ہوتا بدن میں یا سوداء کا غالب ہونا یا بلغم کا غالب ہونا اور ایسے ہی علم طب میں مزاجوں سے بھی بحث کی جاتی ہے الغرض علم طب میں یہ متعدد چیزیں زیر بحث ہیں لیکن یہ سب امر عرضی میں مشترک ہیں اور وہ امر عرضی ہے صحت باقی صحت امر عرضی کیوں ہے؟ اس لیے کہ صحت علم طب کی غرض و غایت ہے اور شئی کی غرض و غایت
This is a commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. (They are) attributed to health, which is the ultimate goal in that science. So it is known that they did not neglect to observe a meaning that necessitates unity, and that no one has the right to conventionally agree that jurisprudence and geometry are one science whose subject is the act of the responsible person and magnitude. Then he, in what he presented from the two examples, contradicts himself, because the subject of usul is many things, since the predicates of its problems are not essential accidents of the concept of evidence, but rather (they relate) to the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and analogy, individually or jointly between two or more, and similarly, conceptualization and asservation in logic. Translation: There is consideration in it because if by difference of problems is meant merely their multiplicity, then we do not concede that it proves the difference of sciences. And it is evident that the problems of a single science are necessarily many. If by difference is meant lack of proportionality among the problems, then we do not concede that mere multiplicity of subjects proves that lack, unless (the subjects) are many and non-proportional... The people have explicitly stated that many things can be subjects of one science provided there is proportionality. The condition of proportionality is that they share a common essential attribute, as line, surface, and solid body are common in the genus of magnitude for geometry; or a common accidental attribute, as the human body and its parts, foods, medicines, elements, and temperaments are common in being subservient to health, which is the goal of medicine. So it is known that they did not neglect observing a meaning that necessitates unity. And no one has the right to conventionally make fiqh and geometry one science. Then he contradicts himself in the two examples, because the subject of usul is many things, as the predicates of its problems are not essential accidents of the concept of evidence... The commentator's refutation of the argument against multiplicity of subject. Explanation: And there is consideration: The author presented an argument against the multiplicity of subject in a single science, which consisted of two premises. The first premise: difference of subjects necessitates difference of problems. The second premise: difference of problems necessitates difference of science. Question: What do you mean by difference of subjects necessitating difference of problems? Two meanings are possible: (1) difference meaning multiplicity of problems, (2) difference meaning lack of proportionality among problems. If you mean the first, then the first premise is definitely accepted, but the second premise is not accepted because every science has thousands of problems; no science has only one problem. So multiplicity of problems does not necessitate multiplicity of science. If you mean the second, then we do not accept the first premise absolutely; rather, there is detail: difference of subjects has two forms: (1) subjects are many but not proportional, (2) subjects are many and proportional. If they are many and not proportional, then it necessitates lack of proportionality among problems. But if they are proportional, then it does not necessitate lack of proportionality. The majority hold that multiplicity of subjects is permissible provided there is proportionality, and it does not necessitate lack of proportionality among problems, so it does not necessitate difference of science. There are two forms of proportionality: (a) sharing in an essential attribute, e.g., geometry has three subjects: line, surface, and solid body, which share the essential attribute of magnitude (continuous quantity with coexisting parts). (b) sharing in an accidental attribute, e.g., medicine has subjects: human body, bodily parts, foods, medicines, elements (dominance of yellow bile, black bile, phlegm), and temperaments; they all share the accidental attribute of health, which is the goal of medicine. So health is accidental because it is the goal and purpose of medicine.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the unity of a science and the refutation of an objection that multiple subject matters require multiple sciences. The author (commentator) begins by stating that the people (scholars) did not neglect to observe a meaning that necessitates unity, meaning that subjects of a science are unified by a common attribute. No one has the right to arbitrarily agree that fiqh and geometry are one science because their subjects (act of mukallaf and magnitude) are fundamentally different. He then points out a contradiction in the objector's use of examples: the subject of usul al-fiqh is multiple (Book, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), and its problems are not essential accidents of a single concept. The author then details the argument: if 'difference of problems' means multiplicity, then multiplicity is natural in any science and does not necessitate a different science. If it means lack of proportionality, then mere multiplicity of subjects does not cause that unless the subjects are non-proportional. The condition for having multiple subjects in one science is proportionality, which can be either in an essential attribute (like magnitude for geometry) or in an accidental attribute (like health for medicine). The passage clarifies that the unity of a science is preserved by a common unifying meaning, not by having a single subject.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawḍūʿ): The subject matter or object of study of a science, that which the science investigates.
مسائل (masāʾil): The specific problems or propositions that are investigated in a science, which are predicates of the subject.
تناسب (tanāsub): Proportionality or common attribute that unites multiple subject matters into a single science, either essential (jins) or accidental (ghaya).
ذاتي (dhātī): Essential; an attribute that is intrinsic to the subjects, such as the genus of magnitude for geometry.
عرضي (ʿaraḍī): Accidental; an attribute that is extrinsic but related to the science's purpose, such as health for medicine.
غاية (ghāya): The ultimate goal or purpose of a science; in medicine it is health.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for multiple subject matters to belong to a single science?
A) They must be identical in every respect.
B) They must be from the same genus exclusively.
C) They must be proportional either in essence or accidentally.
D) They must be unrelated to each other.

Key Takeaway
Multiple subject matters can be part of one science if they share a common attribute, either essential (like genus) or accidental (like goal), ensuring proportionality.

Two Meanings of al-Haythiyya in Subject Definitions
Definitional discussion on the function of 'haythiyya' in science subjects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the two meanings of 'haythiyya' in defining a science's subject, and distinguish which meaning is operative in examples from medicine and astronomy.

Core Idea
Al-haythiyya either compounds with the subject or specifies which accidents are studied—knowing which is critical for defining a science.

When scholars define a science, they often say 'the subject of X is Y from the aspect of Z.' But what does 'from the aspect of' really mean? This passage from al-Tawdih unpacks two distinct interpretations: one treats the aspect as part of the subject itself, the other as a pointer to the essential properties under investigation. Mastering this distinction is essential for correctly delineating the scope of any science in the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Note the two distinct meanings of 'ḥaythiyya' that the author presents.
Pay special attention to the examples from ilāhiyyāt (divine science), ṭibb (medicine), and hay'a (astronomy).
2
Identify the first meaning
The first meaning treats ḥaythiyya as part of the subject. The subject becomes a compound: 'the existent inasmuch as it is existent'. The science then investigates the essential accidents of that compound subject, not the aspect itself.
Example: al-ilāhiyyāt studies unity and multiplicity as accidents of existence.
3
Identify the second meaning
The second meaning treats ḥaythiyya as a specification (bayān) of which essential accidents are studied. The subject remains simple (e.g., 'the human body'), and the aspect tells us which of its many accidents are investigated.
Example: medicine studies health and sickness, not the accidents of 'body-as-healthy'.
4
Analyze the examples given
The author states that for medicine and astronomy, the second meaning is intended. Verify this: in medicine, we research health and sickness directly (the aspects), not the accidents of a compound 'body-inasmuch-as-it-becomes-sick'. Similarly for astronomy.
Ask yourself: what would change if the first meaning were applied? The objects of investigation would be different.
5
Apply the distinction to a new science
Consider the definition of fiqh: 'knowledge of practical shar‘i rulings derived from detailed evidences'. What would be its subject? Could 'al-haythiyya' play a role? Decide which meaning fits and why.
This step consolidates your understanding by transferring the concept to Islamic legal theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا أَنَّهُ قَدْ يُذْكَرُ الْحَيْثِيَّةُ فِى الْمَوْضُوعَاتِ وَلَهَا مَعْنَيَان أَحَدُهُمَا أَنَّ الشَّيْء مَعَ تِلْكَ الْحَيْنِيَّةِ مَوْضُوعٌ كَمَا يُقَالُ الْمَوْجُودُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَوْجُودٌ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلْعِلْمِ الْإِلَهِي فَيُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الَّتِي تَلْحَقُهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَوْجُودٌ كَالْوَحْدَةِ وَالْكَثَرَةِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا ، وَلَا يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ تِلْكَ الْحَيْثِيَّة ؛ لأنَّ الْمَوْضُوعَ مَا يُبْحَثُ عَنْ أَعْرَاضِهِ لَا مَا يُبْحَثُ عَنْهُ أَوْ عَنْ أَجْزَائِهِ وَثَانِيهِمَا أَنَّ الْحَيْنِيَّةَ تَكُونُ بَيَانًا لِلْأعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا فَإِنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلشَّيْء أَعْرَاضٌ ذَاتِيَّةٌ مُتَنَوّعَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْحَثُ فِي عِلْمٍ عَنْ نَوْعٍ مِنْهَا فَالْحَيْثِيَّةُ بَيَانُ ذَلِكَ النَّوْعِ فَقَوْلُهُمْ مَوْضُوعُ الطَّبٌ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُ وَيَمْرَضُ وَمَوْضُوعُ الْهَيْئَةِ أَجْسَامُ الْعَالَمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ لَهَا شَكَلايُرَادُ بِهِ الْمَعْنَى الثَّانِي لَا الْأَوَّلُ إذْ فِي الطِّبِّ يُبْحَث عَنُ الصَّحَّةِ وَالْمَرَض وَفِي الْهَيْئَةِ عَنْ الشَّكل فَلَوْ كَانَ الْمُرَادُ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ يَجبُ أَن يُبْحَثُ فِي الطَّبْ وَالْهَيْئَةِ عَنْ أَعْرَاضِ لَاحِقَةٍ لأَجْلِ الْحَيْثِيَّتَيْنِ وَلَا يُبْحَثُ عَنْ الْحَيْتَيْن وَالْوَاقِعُ خِلافٌ ذَلِكَ .
And among these discussions is that sometimes 'al-haythiyya' (the aspect) is mentioned in the subjects (of sciences). It has two meanings: one is that the thing together with that aspect is the subject, as it is said: 'the existent inasmuch as it is existent is the subject of the divine science', so in it one investigates the essential accidents that attach to it inasmuch as it is existent, such as unity, multiplicity, and the like. One does not investigate that aspect itself, because the subject is that whose accidents are investigated, not that which is investigated about itself or its parts. The second is that the aspect becomes an explanation of the essential accidents that are investigated; for a thing can have various essential accidents, and in a given science only one type is investigated, so the aspect explains that type. Thus their statement: 'the subject of medicine is the human body inasmuch as it becomes healthy or sick' and 'the subject of astronomy is the bodies of the world inasmuch as they have shape' – by it the second meaning is intended, not the first. For in medicine one investigates health and sickness, and in astronomy one investigates shape. If the first meaning were intended, then in medicine and astronomy one would have to investigate accidents that follow from the two aspects, and not investigate the aspects themselves, but the reality is otherwise.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion about the role of 'haythiyya' (aspect/consideration) in defining the subject of a science. The author of al-Tawdih is explaining that when scholars say 'the subject of science X is Y from the aspect of Z', the phrase 'from the aspect of' can mean two different things. First, it could be part of the subject itself, so the subject is 'Y-qua-Z', and the science investigates the essential accidents of that composite subject. Second, it could be merely a specification: the subject is still Y, but the aspect indicates which of Y's many essential accidents are actually studied. The author argues that the common usage in medicine (body inasmuch as it becomes healthy/sick) and astronomy (bodies inasmuch as they have shape) corresponds to the second meaning, because those sciences actually investigate health/sickness and shape, not the accidents of 'body-as-healthy' or 'body-as-shaped'. This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope and boundaries of a science. The passage also implies that if the first meaning were taken, then the subject would be a compound (e.g., body-with-the-aspect), and the science would need to investigate the accidents of that compound, but in reality the objects of investigation are the aspects themselves. Thus, the correct interpretation is the second meaning, where the aspect is just an indicator of which essential properties are studied.

Key Terms
الحيثية (al-haythiyya): The aspect or consideration under which a subject is studied in a science; it qualifies the subject and may be understood either as part of the subject or as a specification of which accidents are investigated.
الأعراض الذاتية (al-a‘rāḍ al-dhātiyya): Essential accidents that are consequent upon the essence of a thing (e.g., unity and multiplicity for existence); they are the proper objects of investigation in a science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second meaning of 'min haythu' discussed in the passage, what function does the haythiyya serve?
A) It is part of the subject itself.
B) It is a specification of which essential accidents are studied.
C) It indicates the final cause of the science.
D) It is the efficient cause of investigation.

Key Takeaway
The term 'min haythu' in subject definitions can either compound with the subject or specify the accidents studied; identifying which meaning is intended is crucial for accurately delimiting a science's scope.

Two Meanings of Haythiyyah in Subject Matters
Explains two meanings of haythiyyah in subject definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two meanings of 'haythiyyah' in defining a science's subject and apply the correct meaning to given examples.

Core Idea
The haythiyyah either forms part of the subject or merely indicates which accidents to investigate.

This passage from al-Tarweeh explains a crucial distinction in Islamic epistemology: how to understand the 'min haythu' phrase when defining a science's subject matter. You will learn two meanings of haythiyyah and see examples from theology, medicine, and astronomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Meanings
Read the passage and list the two meanings of haythiyyah as stated: (1) the haythiyyah is part of the subject, (2) the haythiyyah is a statement of the type of accidents investigated.
The author distinguishes these explicitly at the beginning.
2
Analyze the First Meaning (Integral)
In the first meaning, the aspect is included in the subject definition. The science then investigates the essential accidents that follow from that aspect, not the aspect itself. Example: Theology's subject is 'al-mawjud min haythu innahu mawjud' – existence is part of the subject, so accidents like unity and causality are studied.
The subject itself (existence) is not investigated because that would be circular.
3
Analyze the Second Meaning (Indicative)
In the second meaning, the haythiyyah is not part of the subject but indicates which type of accidents are to be investigated. Example: Medicine's subject is 'the human body from the aspect of health and sickness' – health and sickness are the actual topics studied, not a part of the body's essence.
The aspect itself is the focus of investigation, confirming it is not part of the subject.
4
Apply the Distinction
Given a new subject definition, determine whether the haythiyyah is integral or indicative by checking if the aspect itself is investigated in that science. If it is investigated, it is indicative; if not, it is integral.
Use the rule: 'if the aspect is part of the subject, it is not investigated; if it is investigated, it is not part of the subject'.

Source Text

بَيَانًا لِلْأعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا فَإِنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلشَّيْء أَعْرَاضٌ ذَاتِيَّةٌ مُتَنَوّعَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْحَثُ فِي عِلْمٍ عَنْ نَوْعٍ مِنْهَا فَالْحَيْثِيَّةُ بَيَانُ ذَلِكَ النَّوْعِ فَقَوْلُهُمْ مَوْضُوعُ الطَّبٌ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يَصِحُ وَيَمْرَضُ وَمَوْضُوعُ الْهَيْئَةِ أَجْسَامُ الْعَالَمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ لَهَا شَكَلايُرَادُ بِهِ الْمَعْنَى الثَّانِي لَا الْأَوَّلُ إذْ فِي الطِّبِّ يُبْحَث عَنُ الصَّحَّةِ وَالْمَرَض وَفِي الْهَيْئَةِ عَنْ الشَّكل فَلَوْ كَانَ الْمُرَادُ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ يَجبُ أَن يُبْحَثُ فِي الطَّبْ وَالْهَيْئَةِ عَنْ أَعْرَاضِ لَاحِقَةٍ لأَجْلِ الْحَيْثِيَّتَيْنِ وَلَا يُبْحَثُ عَنْ الْحَيْتَيْن وَالْوَاقِعُ خِلافٌ ذَلِكَ .
ترجمہ:۔ اور ان مباحث میں سے یہ بھی ہے کہ کبھی ذکر کیا جاتا ہے (قید ) حیثیت کو موضوعات میں اور اس کے دو معنی ہیں ان دو میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ بے شک شئی اس قید حیثیت کے ساتھ موضوع ہو جیسا کہا جاتا ہے کہ الموجود من حیث انہ موجود موضوع ہے علم الہی کا پس بحث کی جائیگی اس ( علم الہی ) میں ان اعراض ذاتیہ سے جو لاحق ہوتے ہیں اس کو اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ موجود ہیں جیسے اس کا واحد ہونا اور کثیر ہونا اور اس کی مثل اور نہیں بحث کی جاتی اس میں اس حیثیت سے کیونکہ موضوع وہ ہوتا ہے کہ بحث کی جاتی ہے اس کے اعراض سے نا کہ وہ کہ جس سے بحث کی جائے یا اس کے اجزاء سے بحث کی جائے اور ان دو میں سے دوسرا معنی یہ ہے کہ بیشک حیثیت مجوث عنها اعراض ذاتیہ کا بیان ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ ایک ہی شئی کیلئے مختلف اعراض ذاتیہ ہوں اور سوائے اس کے نہیں بحث کی جاتی ہے ایک علم میں ان (اعراض ) کی ایک نوع سے پس حیثیت بیان ہوگی اسی نوع کا پس ان کا قول کہ علم طب کا موضوع بدن انسانی ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ صحیح ہوتا ہے اور مریض ہوتا ہے اور علم حیت کا موضوع اجسام عالم ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ اس کیلئے ایک شکل ہے مراد لیا جائیگا اس سے دوسرا معنی نا کہ پہلا معنی کیونکہ علم طب میں بحث کی جاتی ہے صحت اور مرض سے اور علم حیت میں شکل سے پس اگر مراد وہ اول ( معنی ) ہو تو واجب ہے یہ کہ بحث کی جائے علم طب میں اور ھیت میں ان اعراض سے جو ان کو لاحق ہوتے ہیں ان دو حیثیتوں کی وجہ سے اور نہ بحث کی جائے ان حیثیتوں سے حالانکہ واقعہ اس کے خلاف ہے۔ کبھی حیثیت محیث لہ سمیت علم کا موضوع بنتی ہے اور بھی موضوع کے عوارض کی جہت کیلئے بیان واقع ہوتی ہے تشریح ومنها انه قد تذکر : ۔ یہاں سے صاحب تو ضیح رحمۃ اللہ علیہ بحث ثانی کو ذکرفرمارہے ہیں یہ بحث
الترويج لحل التوضيح والتنويج حیثیت سے متعلق ہے فرماتے ہیں کہ عمومی طور پر موضوعات میں جو حیثیت ذکر کی جاتی ہے اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں (1) حیثیت اس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ شئی محیث لہ حیثیت سمیت علم کا موضوع بنتی ہے یعنی حیثیت موضوع کا جزء واقع ہوتی ہے (۲) حیثیت وہ اعراض جو مجوث عنما ہیں ان کی نوع کا بیان ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ جائز ہے کہ اس موضوع کے عوارض ذاتیہ متعدد انواع کے ہوں لہذا یہ حیثیت بیان کر دے گی کہ اس علم میں فلان نوع سے بحث ہے تو یہ حیثیت صرف اس موضوع کے عوارض ذاتیہ کی جہت کو بیان کر رہی ہے۔ قسم اول کی توضیح بالمثال :- جیسے علم الہی کا موضوع الموجود من حیث انہ موجود ہے اس میں موضوع کے اندر جو حیثیت ہے یہ موضوع کی جزء ہے یعنی جو عوارض موجود کو لاحق ہوں گے موجود ہونے کی حیثیت سے جیسے وحدت کا ہونا علیت کا ہونا اور معلولیت کا ہونا اور کثرت کا ہونا وغیرہ اس قسم کے جتنے بھی عوارض ہیں ان کو دخل ہے موجود میں بخلاف حادث ہونا اور جو ہر ہوتا عرض ہونا وغیرہ ان کو دخل نہیں ہے موجود ہونے میں چونکہ یہ قسم موضوع کی جزء بن رہی ہے لہذا علم الہی میں خود موجود سے بحث نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ قاعدہ اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ علم میں خود موضوع اور موضوع کے اجزاء سے بحث نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہوتی ہے نیز اس سے بحث کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس کو زیر بحث لایا جائے تو اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی اس کو مسئلہ کا معمول بنا کر موضوع کیلئے ثابت کیا جائیگا مثلا یوں کہیں گے الموجود موجود اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں لغویت ہے قسم ثانی کی توضیح بالمثال : جیسے علم طب کا موضوع ہے بدن انسانی من حيث الصحة والمرض اب یہ صحت اور مرض بیان ہے اس بات کا کہ علم طب میں بدن کے جو عوارض مبحوث عنھا ہوں گے وہ اس حیثیت سے ہوں گے کہ جو بدن کو عارض ہوتے ہیں من حیث الصحة والمرض۔ دوسری مثال: جیسے علم حیت کا موضوع ہے اجسام عالم من حیث انتشکل اب یہ تشکل حیثیت ہے جو بیان ہے اس بات کا علم قیمت میں جو عوارض مبحوث عنھا ہیں وہ جسم کو عارض ہوتے ہیں من حیث المتشکل یہ دوسری قسم حیثیت بیانیہ ہے جب یہ بیانیہ ہے تو خود صحت اور مرض کے احوال سے علم طب میں بحث ہوگی اور علم صیت میں خود تشکل سے بھی بحث ہوگی کیونکہ یہ موضوع کا جز نہیں ہے باقی اس بات پر کیا دلیل ہے کہ یہ حیثیت بیانیہ ہے جو نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ جز ہوتی تو پھر مجوث عنھا نہیں ہونی چاہیے حالانکہ ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ علم طب میں خود صحت و مرض سے بحث ہوتی ہے اور علم ھیت میں خود شکل سے بحث ہوتی ہے اب اگر جز ہوتی تو مبحوث عنھا نہ ہوتی کیونکہ قاعدہ ہے کہ کسی علم میں اس کے موضوع اور موضوع کے اجزاء سے بحث نہیں ہوتی۔
An explanation of the essential properties that are investigated: it is possible for a thing to have various essential properties, and only one type of them is investigated in a science. So the 'haythiyyah' (aspect) is the statement of that type. Thus their saying: 'The subject of medicine is the human body from the aspect that it becomes healthy and sick, and the subject of astronomy is the bodies of the world from the aspect that they have a shape' is intended with the second meaning, not the first. For in medicine, health and sickness are investigated, and in astronomy, shape. If the first meaning were intended, then it would be necessary to investigate in medicine and astronomy the accidents that follow due to the two aspects, and not to investigate the aspects themselves, but the reality is contrary to that.
Translation: Among these discussions is that sometimes the restriction of 'haythiyyah' is mentioned in subjects, and it has two meanings. The first meaning: the thing is the subject with this restriction, as it is said: 'Al-mawjud min haythu innahu mawjud (the existent qua existent) is the subject of theology.' So in theology, investigation takes place into the essential properties that are consequent to it from the aspect that it exists, such as its being one, many, etc., and not from other aspects because the subject is that whose accidents are investigated, not that about which investigation is made or its parts. The second meaning: the 'haythiyyah' is a statement of the essential properties that are investigated, because it is possible for one thing to have diverse essential properties, and in a science only one type of them is investigated. Thus the 'haythiyyah' will be a statement of that type. So their saying: 'The subject of medicine is the human body from the aspect that it becomes healthy and sick, and the subject of astronomy is the bodies of the world from the aspect that they have a shape' is taken in the second meaning, not the first. Because in medicine, health and sickness are investigated, and in astronomy, shape. If the first meaning were intended, then it would be necessary to investigate in medicine and astronomy the accidents that are consequent to them due to the two aspects, and not to investigate the aspects themselves, but the reality is contrary to that. Sometimes the 'haythiyyah' together with what it is an aspect of becomes the subject of a science, and sometimes it is a statement for the direction of the subject's accidents. Explanation: And among them is that it is sometimes mentioned... Here the author of al-Tawdih, may Allah have mercy on him, mentions the second discussion. This discussion is related to 'haythiyyah'. He says: Generally, the 'haythiyyah' mentioned in subjects has two types: (1) The 'haythiyyah' indicates that the thing with what it is an aspect of becomes the subject of the science, meaning the 'haythiyyah' becomes a part of the subject. (2) The 'haythiyyah' is a statement of the type of accidents that are investigated. Because it is possible that the subject's essential properties are of multiple types, so this 'haythiyyah' will clarify that in this science, such and such type is investigated. Thus this 'haythiyyah' is only indicating the direction of the subject's essential properties. Clarification of the first type by example: Like the subject of theology is al-mawjud min haythu innahu mawjud. In this, the 'haythiyyah' within the subject is part of the subject, meaning the accidents that will attach to al-mawjud from the aspect of its existence, such as being one, being a cause, being an effect, multiplicity, etc., all such accidents have entry into al-mawjud. Unlike being temporal, being a substance, being an accident, etc., these have no entry into existence. Since this type becomes part of the subject, in theology investigation is not about al-mawjud itself because the rule and principle is that in a science, the subject itself and its parts are not investigated; rather, its essential properties are investigated. Also, investigating it has no benefit because if it were investigated, the form would be: making it a subject of the problem and then proving it for the subject, e.g., they would say 'al-mawjud exists', and it is obvious that this is tautological. Clarification of the second type by example: Like the subject of medicine is the human body from the aspect of health and sickness. Now this 'health and sickness' is a statement of the fact that in medicine, the accidents that are investigated concerning the body will be those that occur to it from the aspect of health and sickness. Another example: The subject of astronomy is the bodies of the world from the aspect that they have shape. Now this 'shape' is a 'haythiyyah' which is a statement of the fact that in astronomy, the accidents that are investigated occur to the body from the aspect of having shape. This second type is expressive 'haythiyyah'. When it is expressive, then in medicine, investigation will be into the states of health and sickness themselves, and in astronomy, investigation will be into shape itself because it is not a part of the subject. As for the proof that this 'haythiyyah' is expressive and not part, the proof is that if it were part, then it would not be investigated, but we see that in medicine, health and sickness themselves are investigated, and in astronomy, shape itself is investigated. If it were part, it would not be investigated because the rule is that in any science, its subject and the parts of the subject are not investigated.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion from Usul al-Fiqh concerning the term 'haythiyyah' (aspect or consideration) as used to define the subject matter (mawdu') of a science. The author distinguishes two meanings. The first meaning: the 'haythiyyah' is an integral part of the subject itself. In this case, the subject is defined by that aspect, and the science investigates the essential accidents that follow from that aspect, not the aspect itself. For example, in theology, the subject is 'al-mawjud min haythu innahu mawjud' (the existent qua existent). Here, 'existence' is part of the subject definition. The accidents investigated are those that necessarily attach to existence, such as unity or causality. The subject itself (existence) is not investigated because that would be circular. The second meaning: the 'haythiyyah' is merely indicative of which type of accidents are to be investigated. It is not part of the subject's definition. For example, in medicine, the subject is 'the human body from the aspect of health and sickness.' Here, 'health and sickness' are not part of the body's essence, but they indicate that in medicine we only study accidents related to health and illness. Similarly, in astronomy, the aspect of 'shape' indicates that we investigate shape-related accidents. The key evidence for the second meaning is that if it were part of the subject, then we would not investigate health and sickness themselves in medicine, but we do. This distinction helps define the scope of each science.

Key Terms
حيثية (haythiyyah): The aspect or consideration from which a subject is studied; used in defining the subject matter (mawdu') of a science.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science, defined along with a haythiyyah to specify which accidents are investigated.
عراض ذاتية (a'radh dhatiyyah): Essential accidental properties that necessarily attach to the subject and are the focus of investigation in a science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes the first meaning of 'haythiyyah' from the second?
A) In the first meaning, the haythiyyah is part of the subject; in the second, it is not.
B) In the first meaning, the haythiyyah is derived from ijma; in the second, from qiyas.
C) The first meaning applies only to medicine; the second only to theology.
D) The first meaning indicates that the subject itself is investigated; the second indicates that its parts are investigated.

Key Takeaway
The haythiyyah in a subject definition can either be integral (part of the subject) or indicative (pointing to the accidents to be studied), determined by whether the aspect itself is investigated.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
Two Types of Haythiyya in Defining a Science's Subject Matter
Explaining two types of haythiyya with examples and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of haythiyya in defining a science's subject matter and apply the classification to any given definition.

Core Idea
The haythiyya is either part of the subject or a declaration of the accidents to be studied — a distinction proven by whether it is itself investigated.

In Hanafi usul, precisely defining a science's subject matter is essential to delimit its scope. The term 'haythiyya' (aspect) plays a central role in such definitions, but its function can vary. This passage from al-Talwih clarifies two distinct roles: the haythiyya may be an intrinsic part of the subject, or it may merely indicate the types of essential accidents (al-awarid al-dhatiyya) that the science investigates. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion about what is actually studied in a given field.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of haythiyya
The author states that haythiyya either (1) constitutes part of the subject or (2) declares the type of accidents to be investigated. Locate this classification in the opening lines of the Urdu explanation.
The two divisions are clearly marked with numerals in the text.
2
Analyse the first type: haythiyya as part of the subject
Examine the example of theology: 'the existent qua existent'. Here the haythiyya 'qua existent' is part of the subject itself. Therefore the science investigates accidents that necessarily attach to existence (e.g., causality, unity), not existence itself. Discussing existence would be tautological.
Rule: the subject and its parts are not discussed in the science; only its essential accidents are.
3
Analyse the second type: haythiyya as declarative of accidents
Examine the examples of medicine ('human body insofar as it is healthy and ill') and geometry ('bodies of the world insofar as they are shaped'). Here the haythiyya (health/disease, shape) is not part of the subject but indicates which accidents are to be studied. Crucially, these haythiyyas themselves are discussed in the respective sciences.
This contrasts with the first type: the haythiyya is itself a topic of investigation.
4
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The author provides a proof: if the haythiyya were part of the subject, it could not be investigated. But in medicine and geometry, the haythiyya is indeed discussed. Therefore it cannot be part of the subject; it must be declarative.
This is an inductive argument based on observable practice in the sciences.
5
Appreciate the potential objection and its refinement
The passage ends with a likely objection: one might argue that in theology the haythiyya is not part of the subject but a restriction. Though the text cuts off, the Hanafi response is implied: if it were merely a restriction, existence itself could be discussed, which is absurd. This demonstrates the critical refinement typical in usul al-fiqh.
This step shows how usul scholars sharpen definitions through objections.

کو دخل ہے موجود میں بخلاف حادث ہونا اور جو ہر ہوتا عرض ہونا وغیرہ ان کو دخل نہیں ہے موجود ہونے میں چونکہ یہ قسم موضوع کی جزء بن رہی ہے لہذا علم الہی میں خود موجود سے بحث نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ قاعدہ اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ علم میں خود موضوع اور موضوع کے اجزاء سے بحث نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہوتی ہے نیز اس سے بحث کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس کو زیر بحث لایا جائے تو اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی اس کو مسئلہ کا معمول بنا کر موضوع کیلئے ثابت کیا جائیگا مثلا یوں کہیں گے الموجود موجود اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں لغویت ہے قسم ثانی کی توضیح بالمثال : جیسے علم طب کا موضوع ہے بدن انسانی من حيث الصحة والمرض اب یہ صحت اور مرض بیان ہے اس بات کا کہ علم طب میں بدن کے جو عوارض مبحوث عنھا ہوں گے وہ اس حیثیت سے ہوں گے کہ جو بدن کو عارض ہوتے ہیں من حیث الصحة والمرض۔ دوسری مثال: جیسے علم حیت کا موضوع ہے اجسام عالم من حیث انتشکل اب یہ تشکل حیثیت ہے جو بیان ہے اس بات کا علم قیمت میں جو عوارض مبحوث عنھا ہیں وہ جسم کو عارض ہوتے ہیں من حیث المتشکل یہ دوسری قسم حیثیت بیانیہ ہے جب یہ بیانیہ ہے تو خود صحت اور مرض کے احوال سے علم طب میں بحث ہوگی اور علم صیت میں خود تشکل سے بھی بحث ہوگی کیونکہ یہ موضوع کا جز نہیں ہے باقی اس بات پر کیا دلیل ہے کہ یہ حیثیت بیانیہ ہے جو نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ جز ہوتی تو پھر مجوث عنھا نہیں ہونی چاہیے حالانکہ ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ علم طب میں خود صحت و مرض سے بحث ہوتی ہے اور علم ھیت میں خود شکل سے بحث ہوتی ہے اب اگر جز ہوتی تو مبحوث عنھا نہ ہوتی کیونکہ قاعدہ ہے کہ کسی علم میں اس کے موضوع اور موضوع کے اجزاء سے بحث نہیں ہوتی۔

قَوْلُهُ ) وَمِنْهَا أَنَّهُ قَدْ يَذْكُرُ الْحَيْنِيَّةُ) الْمَبْحَثُ الثَّانِي فِي تَحْقِيقِ الْحَيْنِيَّةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ فِي الْمَوْضُوعِ حَيْثُ يُقَالُ مَوْضُوعُ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ هُوَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء حَيْثُ كَذَا وَلَفُظْ حَيْثُ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلْمَكَانِ أَسْتَعِيرَ لِجِهَةِ الشَّيْء وَاعْتِبَارِهِ يُقَالُ الْمَوْجُودُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَوْجُودٌ أَى مِنْ هَذِهِ الْجِهَةِ وَبِهَذَا الْاعْتِبَارِ فَالْحَيْثِيَّةُ الْمَذْكُورَةُ فِي الْمَوْضُوعِ قَدْ لَا تَكُونُ مِنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ كَقَوْلِهِمْ مَوْضُوعُ الْعِلْمِ الْإِلَهِيِّ الْبَاحِثِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ الْمُجَرَّدَةِ هُوَ الْمَوْجُودُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَوْجُودٌ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّهُ يُبْحَثُ عَنْ الْعَوَارِضِ الَّتِي تَلْحَقُ الْمَوْجُودَ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَوْجُودٌ لَا مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ جَوْهَرٌ أَوْ عَرَضٌ أَوْ حِسْمٌ أَوْ مُجَرَّدٌ ، وَذَلِكَ كَالْعِيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ وَالْوُجُوبِ رَ الْإِمْكَانِ وَالْقِدَمِ وَالْحُدُوثِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ وَلَا يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ حَيْثِيَّةِ الْوُجُودِ ، إِذْ لَا مَعْنَى لِإِثْبَاتِهَا لِلْمَوْجُودِ وَقَدْ تَكُونُ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ كَقَوْلِهِمْ مَوْضُوعُ عِلْمِ الطَّبَ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ مِنْ حَيْثُ يَصِحُ وَيَمُرَضُ وَمَوْضُوعُ الْعِلْمِ الطَّبِيعِيِّ الْجِسْمُ مِنْ حَيْثُ يَتَحَرَّكَ وَيَسْكُنُ وَالصَّحَّةُ وَالْمَرَضُ مِنْ الأعْرَاضِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الطَّبٌ وَكَذَا الحَرَكَةُ وَالسُّكُونُ فِي الطَّبِيعِيِّ فَذَهَبَ الْمُصَنِّفُ إلَى أَنَّ الْحَيْنِيَّةَ فِي الْقِسْمِ الأَوَّل جُزء مِنْ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، وَفِي الثَّانِي بَيَانٌ لِلْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ إذْ لَوْ كَانَتْ جُزْءًا مِنَ الْمَوْضُوعِ كَمَا فِي الْقِسْمِ الْأَوَّلِ لَمَا صَحٌ أَنْ يُبْحَثُ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ وَتُجْعَلَ مِنْ مَحْمُووَلَاتِ مَسَائِلِهِ ، إِذْ لَا يُبْحَثُ فِى الْعِلْمِ عَنْ أَجْزَاء الْمَوْضُوعِ ، بَلْ عَنْ أَعْرَاضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ وَلِقَائِلِ أَنْ يَقُولَ لَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهَا فِي الْأَوَّلِ جُزْء مِنُ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، بَلْ قَيْدٌ لِمَوْضُوعِيَّتِهِ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ الْبَحْتَ يَكُونُ عَنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الَّتِي
Altarweeh li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is about haythiyya. They say: Generally, in subjects, the haythiyya mentioned is of two types: (1) haythiyya indicates that the thing, with its haythiyya, becomes the subject of the science, meaning the haythiyya is part of the subject. (2) haythiyya is an expression of the type of accidents that are investigated. Because it is permissible that the essential accidents of this subject are of multiple types, so this haythiyya will indicate which type is discussed in this science. So this haythiyya only indicates the direction of the essential accidents of the subject. First type exemplified: Like the subject of theology is 'the existent qua existent'. In this, the haythiyya within the subject is part of the subject, i.e., the accidents that attach to the existent by virtue of existence, such as unity, causality, effect, multiplicity, etc. All such accidents enter into 'existent', unlike being contingent, being an accident, etc. They do not enter into 'existent'. Since this type becomes part of the subject, therefore in theology the existent itself is not discussed, because the rule is that in a science the subject itself and its parts are not discussed, but rather its essential accidents. Also there is no benefit in discussing it, because if it were made a subject of investigation, it would be like saying 'the existent is existent', which is tautological. Second type exemplified: Like the subject of medicine is the human body from the perspective of health and disease. This health and disease indicate that the accidents discussed in medicine are those that occur to the body with respect to health and disease. Another example: Like the subject of geometry is the bodies of the world from the perspective of shape. This shape is a haythiyya indicating that the accidents discussed in geometry are those that occur to the body by virtue of shape. This second type is declarative haythiyya. Since it is declarative, the states of health and disease themselves are discussed in medicine, and shape itself is discussed in geometry, because it is not part of the subject. As for the proof that this haythiyya is declarative and not part of the subject, it is that if it were part, then it should not be investigated, whereas we see that in medicine health and disease themselves are discussed, and in geometry shape itself is discussed. If it were part, it would not be investigated because the rule is that in a science the subject and its parts are not discussed.

He said: 'And among them is that he may mention the haythiyya.' The second investigation concerns the verification of the haythiyya mentioned in the subject, where it is said that the subject of this science is such-and-such a thing 'insofar as' (haythu) 'so and so'. The word 'haythu' is originally for place, but is metaphorically used for 'aspect of a thing' and 'consideration of it'. It is said: 'the existent insofar as it is existent', meaning from this aspect and with this consideration. So the haythiyya mentioned in the subject may not be among the accidents investigated in the science, as when they say: the subject of theology, which investigates the states of abstract existents, is the existent insofar as it is existent, meaning that it investigates the accidents that attach to the existent by virtue of being existent, not by virtue of being substance, accident, body, or abstract. That is like causality, being an effect, necessity, possibility, pre-eternity, temporality, etc. And it does not investigate the haythiyya of existence itself, because there is no meaning to proving it for the existent. And it may be among the accidents investigated in the science, as when they say: the subject of medicine is the human body insofar as it is healthy and ill, and the subject of natural science is the body insofar as it moves and rests. Health and disease are among the accidents investigated in medicine, and likewise motion and rest in natural science. So the author (al-Musannif) holds that the haythiyya in the first division is part of the subject, and in the second it is a declaration of the essential accidents investigated in the science. For if it were part of the subject as in the first division, it would not be correct to investigate it in the science and make it one of the predicates of its problems, because in a science one does not investigate the parts of the subject, but rather its essential accidents. And one might object: We do not grant that in the first division it is part of the subject; rather it is a restriction for its being a subject, meaning that the investigation is about the accidents that...
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion from the hashiya (Talwih) on the concept of haythiyya (aspect/consideration) in defining the subject matter of a science. The commentator (Taftazani) clarifies the two possible roles of haythiyya: (1) It can be part of the subject itself, as in theology where 'existent qua existent' means the aspect of existence is intrinsic to the subject, so the accidents discussed are those that attach to existence itself, like unity, causality, etc. (2) It can be merely declarative, indicating which types of accidents are to be discussed, as in medicine where 'health and disease' are not part of the subject (the human body) but indicate that the accidents studied are those related to health and disease. The argument is rational: if haythiyya were part of the subject, it could not be discussed as an accident; but in sciences like medicine and geometry, the very thing indicated by the haythiyya (health/disease, shape) is discussed, proving it is not part of the subject. The commentary also addresses a potential objection: one might argue that in the first division (theology), the haythiyya is not part of the subject but a restriction. This shows the rigour of Hanafi usul in defining the boundaries of a science.

Key Terms
الحيثية (al-haythiyya): The aspect or consideration from which a subject is studied, either as part of the subject or as a declaration of the accidents to be investigated.
العوارض الذاتية (al-awarid al-dhatiyya): Essential accidents that attach to the subject by virtue of its essence, not by external factors.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science, defined with its haythiyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second type of haythiyya, such as 'human body insofar as it is healthy and ill' in medicine, why is the haythiyya not considered part of the subject?
A) Because health and disease are not real accidents.
B) Because health and disease are discussed in medicine, and if they were part of the subject they could not be discussed.
C) Because the human body is not the true subject of medicine.
D) Because the author did not include it in his classification.

Key Takeaway
The haythiyya in a science's definition either constitutes part of the subject (and is not discussed) or declares the accidents to be studied (and is discussed), a distinction determined by whether the haythiyya itself appears among the questions of the science.

Method of Learning
advanced
8 min
The Haythiyya: Part of the Subject or Qualification?
Analyzing whether 'haythiyya' is part of subject or qualification for accidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of 'haythiyya' in defining a science's subject and evaluate the dispute over whether it is part (juz') or qualification (qayd).

Core Idea
The 'haythiyya' in a science's definition either specifies the subject's parts or qualifies which accidents are studied — a subtle distinction with major implications.

This lesson dives into a foundational debate in Islamic philosophy of science: when we say 'the subject of X science is Y from the aspect of Z', is 'from the aspect of Z' part of Y itself, or merely a qualification telling us which properties of Y will be investigated? The answer determines whether two sciences can share the same subject essentially. We will follow the argument between the author (al-musannif) and an objector.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions of haythiyya
The passage distinguishes two cases: (a) haythiyya not among the accidents investigated (e.g., theology's 'existent qua existent'), (b) haythiyya among the accidents (e.g., medicine's 'human body from aspect of health/sickness'). Recognize each from the examples.
In case (a), the haythiyya itself is not studied; in case (b), it is.
2
Understand the author's classification
Al-musannif holds that in case (a) haythiyya is part (juz') of the subject; in case (b) it is a statement of the essential accidents. His reasoning: if it were part in (b), we would be investigating parts of the subject, which sciences do not do.
This preserves the principle that sciences investigate accidents of the subject, not its parts.
3
Analyze the objector's counterargument
The objector argues that in both cases haythiyya is a qualification (qayd) for subjecthood, not a part. This means the research is about accidents attaching to the subject from that specific aspect.
Under this view, investigating haythiyya does not mean investigating parts of the subject.
4
Trace the consequence of each view
Under the author's view, two sciences (e.g., theology and natural philosophy) might share the same subject essentially if the haythiyya is part of the subject. The objector's view avoids this by making haythiyya a qualification, allowing distinct sciences to study the same thing under different aspects.
The passage highlights that the objector's view prevents 'sharing same subject essentially and with the same consideration'.
5
Evaluate which view is more consistent
Consider the implications for how we define the boundaries of sciences. The passage does not give a final tarjih, so weigh the logical arguments of both sides.
This is an open methodological issue in usul al-fiqh.

مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ جَوْهَرٌ أَوْ عَرَضٌ أَوْ جِسْمٌ أَوْ مُجَرَّدٌ ، وَذَلِكَ كَالْعِلِّيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ وَالْوُجُوبِ وَالْإِمْكَانِ وَالْقِدَمِ وَالْحُدُوثِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ وَلَا يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ حَيْثِيَّةِ الْوُجُودِ ، إِذْ لَا مَعْنَى لِإِثْبَاتِهَا لِلْمَوْجُودِ وَقَدْ تَكُونُ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ كَقَوْلِهِمْ مَوْضُوعُ عِلْمِ الطِّبِّ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ مِنْ حَيْثُ يَصِحُّ وَيَمْرَضُ وَمَوْضُوعُ الْعِلْمِ الطَّبِيعِيِّ الْجِسْمُ مِنْ حَيْثُ يَتَحَرَّكُ وَيَسْكُنُ وَالصِّحَّةُ وَالْمَرَضُ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الطِّبِّ وَكَذَا الْحَرَكَةُ وَالسُّكُونُ فِي الطَّبِيعِيِّ فَذَهَبَ الْمُصَنِّفُ إلَى أَنَّ الْحَيْثِيَّةَ فِي الْقِسْمِ الأَوَّل جُزْء مِنْ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، وَفِي الثَّانِي بَيَانٌ لِلْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَتْ جُزْءًا مِنَ الْمَوْضُوعِ كَمَا فِي الْقِسْمِ الْأَوَّلِ لَمَا صَحَّ أَنْ يُبْحَثَ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ وَتُجْعَلَ مِنْ مَحْمُولَاتِ مَسَائِلِهِ ، إِذْ لَا يُبْحَثُ فِى الْعِلْمِ عَنْ أَجْزَاء الْمَوْضُوعِ ، بَلْ عَنْ أَعْرَاضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَقُولَ لَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهَا فِي الْأَوَّلِ جُزْء مِنُ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، بَلْ قَيْدٌ لِمَوْضُوعِيَّتِهِ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ الْبَحْثَ يَكُونُ عَنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الَّتِي تَلْحَقُهُ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ وَبِذَلِكَ الْاعْتِبَارِ وَعَلَى هَذَا لَوْ جَعَلْنَا الْحَيْثِيَّةَ فِي الْقِسْمِ الثَّانِي أَيْضًا قَيْدًا لِلْمَوْضُوعِ عَلَى مَا هُوَ ظَاهِرُ كَلَامِ الْقَوْمِ لَا بَيَانًا لِلْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ عَلَى مَا ذَهَبَ إلَيْهِ المُصَنِّفُ لَمْ يَكُنُ الْبَحْثُ عَنْهَا فِى العِلْمِ بَحْثًا عَنْ أَجْزَاءِ المَوْضُوعِ وَلَمْ يَلْزَمْنَا مَا لَزِمَ الْمُصَنِّفَ مِنْ تَشَارُكِ الْعِلْمَيْنِ فِي مَوْضُوعِ وَاحِدٍ بِالذَّاتِ وَالِاعْتِبَارِ
His saying 'and among them is that he may mention al-haythiyya' — the second investigation is in the verification of the haythiyya mentioned in the subject where it is said 'the subject of this science is that thing from such-and-such an aspect.' The word 'haythu' is originally used for place, metaphorically borrowed for the aspect of a thing and its consideration. It is said 'the existent from the aspect that it exists' i.e., from this aspect and with this consideration. So the haythiyya mentioned in the subject is sometimes not among the accidents investigated in the science, as in their saying 'the subject of theology, which investigates the states of abstract existents, is the existent from the aspect that it exists' meaning that it investigates the accidents that attach to the existent from the aspect that it exists, not from the aspect that it is substance or accident or body or abstract. That includes causality, effectuality, necessity, possibility, eternity, origination, and the like. It does not investigate the haythiyya of existence itself, since there is no meaning to affirming it for the existent. And sometimes it is among the accidents investigated in the science, as in their saying 'the subject of medicine is the human body from the aspect that it is healthy and sick' and 'the subject of natural science is the body from the aspect that it moves and rests.' Health and sickness are among the accidents investigated in medicine, similarly movement and rest in natural science. The author held that the haythiyya in the first division is part of the subject, and in the second it is a statement of the essential accidents investigated in the science, for if it were part of the subject as in the first division, it would not be valid to investigate it in the science and make it among the predicates of its problems, since in the science one does not investigate the parts of the subject, but rather its essential accidents. An objector may say: we do not accept that in the first it is part of the subject; rather it is a qualification for its being a subject, meaning that the research is about the accidents that attach to it from that aspect and with that consideration. On this basis, if we made the haythiyya in the second division also a qualification for the subject, as is apparent from the statements of the scholars, not a statement of the essential accidents as the author held, then the investigation of them in the science would not be an investigation of the parts of the subject, and we would not be required to accept what the author was forced to accept, namely that two sciences share the same subject essentially and with the same consideration.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a dispute about the nature of 'haythiyya' (the aspect/respect) mentioned in the definition of a science's subject matter. The author (al-musannif) divides cases into two: first, where the haythiyya is not itself among the accidents investigated (e.g., theology: subject is 'the existent qua existent' — the aspects of causality, necessity, etc. are studied, not the aspect of existence itself); second, where the haythiyya is among the accidents (e.g., medicine: subject is 'human body from aspect of health/sickness'; health/sickness are the accidents studied). The author claims that in the first case, the haythiyya is part of the subject; in the second, it is a statement of the essential accidents. His reasoning: if it were part in both, then we would be investigating parts of the subject — which is not done in a science (sciences investigate accidents of the subject, not its parts). An objector counters: even in the first case, the haythiyya is not a part but a qualification (qayd) for subjecthood. That is, the research is about accidents attaching from that specific aspect. If we apply this understanding to the second case as well (following the apparent meaning of scholars' statements, not the author's view), then investigating the haythiyya does not constitute investigating parts of the subject, and we avoid the problem of two sciences (like medicine and theology) sharing the same subject essentially and with the same consideration. The passage clarifies a subtle distinction in how to define a science's subject, emphasizing that the phrase 'min haythu' functions either to limit the scope of investigation (qualification) or to specify the essential accidents themselves.

Key Terms
الْحَيْثِيَّة (al-haythiyya): The aspect or respect indicated by the phrase 'min haythu' in defining the subject matter of a science
الْمَوْضُوع (al-mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science; that which the science investigates its essential accidents
الْأَعْرَاض الذَّاتِيَّة (al-aʿrāḍ al-dhātiyya): Essential accidents that belong to the subject and are investigated in the science
الْجُزْء (al-juzʾ): A part of the subject; that which constitutes the essence of the subject
الْقَيْد (al-qayd): A qualification that restricts the subject to a certain aspect, without being part of its essence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (al-musannif), how does the role of 'haythiyya' differ between the two divisions?
A) In both divisions, it is a part of the subject.
B) In the first division, it is a statement of essential accidents; in the second, it is a part of the subject.
C) In the first division, it is a part of the subject; in the second, it is a statement of essential accidents.
D) In both divisions, it is a qualification (qayd).

Key Takeaway
The haythiyya in a science's definition is either a part of the subject or a qualification, and this distinction affects whether two sciences can share the same subject essentially.

The Two Types of Haythiyya and Their Role in Subject Definition
Dispute over the nature of haythiyya in subject definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute over the nature of haythiyya and apply the commentator's refinement to the problem of overlapping scientific subjects.

Core Idea
Treating haythiyya as a condition (qayd) in both divisions avoids subject overlap and keeps discussion on accidental attributes.

The definition of a science's subject often includes a qualifier (haythiyya) that specifies the aspect under which the subject is studied. This passage from a Hanafi commentary debates whether that qualifier is an integral part of the subject, a description of the attributes to be studied, or a mere condition restricting the subject. The commentator offers a refined view that resolves a critical problem: two sciences (e.g., medicine and natural science) would otherwise share the same subject essentially. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions of haythiyya
The musannif divides haythiyya into two kinds: (1) one that is part of the subject itself (e.g., 'existent qua existent' in theology) and (2) one that describes the accidental attributes to be studied (e.g., 'human body qua healthy/sick' in medicine). Distinguish these examples and their implications.
In theology, the subject is existent; the aspect 'qua existent' seems to be part of the subject's definition. In medicine, the subject is the human body; the aspect 'qua healthy/sick' describes the attributes discussed.
2
State the musannif's position
The musannif argues that in the first division the haythiyya is a part of the subject, while in the second it is a description of the accidental attributes. This leads to the possibility that two sciences (e.g., medicine and natural science) could share the same subject essentially if the haythiyya is not properly distinguished.
The musannif's view is explicit in the text: 'haythiyya in the first division is a part of the subject, and in the second division it is a description of the accidental attributes.'
3
Present the commentator's alternative
The commentator proposes that in both divisions the haythiyya should be treated as a condition (qayd) for the subject, neither part of the subject nor a description of attributes. This aligns with the apparent view of earlier scholars (al-qawm).
The commentator says: 'if we make the haythiyya in the second division also a condition for the subject... we would not be required what the author required.'
4
Analyze the advantages of the commentator's view
Under the commentator's view: (a) discussion in a science remains about accidental attributes of the subject, not its parts; and (b) the problem of two sciences sharing the same subject essentially and in consideration is avoided (e.g., medicine and natural science both study the body but under different aspects).
The commentator explicitly states these advantages: 'discussion about it in the science would not be a discussion about the parts of the subject, and we would not be faced with the objection... of two sciences sharing one subject.'
5
Apply the analysis to examples
Apply both views to the examples given: theology (ilm al-ilahi) where subject is existent with haythiyya as condition, and medicine where body is subject with haythiyya as condition. Show how the commentator's view makes each science focus on distinct attributes without subject overlap.
In theology, the condition 'qua existent' restricts discussion to attributes that attach by virtue of existence (possible, necessary, etc.). In medicine, the condition 'qua healthy/sick' restricts discussion to health-related attributes. Natural science uses the condition 'qua moving/resting'.

موضوع بدن انسانی ہے من حیث المرض والصحہ یہاں حیث بیان واقع ہے اب یہ صحت و مرض بیان ہے اس چیز کا کہ علم طب میں بدن کے جو عوارض مبحوث عنہا ہوں گے وہ اس حیثیت سے ہوں گے جو بدن کو عارض ہوتے ہیں من حیث الصحة و المرض اور جیسے علم حیت کا موضوع اجسام عالم ہیں من حیث المتشکل یہ تشکل حیثیت ہے اور یہ بیان ہے اس
The commentary for solving al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. It follows from that haythiyya and with that consideration. And based on this, if we make the haythiyya in the second division also a condition for the subject, as is apparent from the speech of the earlier scholars, not a description of the accidental attributes as the author went to, then the discussion about it in the science would not be a discussion about the parts of the subject, and we would not be required what the author required of two sciences sharing one subject essentially and in consideration. Translation: The second discussion is an investigation of the haythiyya that is mentioned in the subject. It is said that the subject of a science is a thing 'from the aspect of such-and-such'. The word 'hayth' is coined for the meaning of place (location). It is used metaphorically for the direction and consideration of a thing. It is said 'al-mawjud min haythu huwa mawjud' i.e., from that direction and with that consideration. And the haythiyya that is mentioned in the subject sometimes is not among the accidental attributes discussed in the science, like their saying: the subject of divine science, which discusses the states of abstract existents, is existent from the aspect that it exists. With this meaning, discussion is about the attributes that attach to the existent from the aspect that it exists, not from the aspect that it is a substance or an accident or a body or abstract. And these are, for example, causality and effect, necessary and possible, eternal and originated, and the like. And there is no discussion in it about the aspect of existence because there is no meaning to proving existence for the existent. And sometimes the haythiyya is among the accidental attributes discussed in the science, like their saying: the subject of medicine is the human body from the aspect that it is healthy or sick, and the subject of natural science is the body from the aspect that it moves or is stationary. Health and sickness in medicine are among the accidental attributes discussed, and similarly motion and rest in natural science. Thus the author proceeded to the point that verily the haythiyya in the first division is a part of the subject, and in the second division it is a description of the accidental attributes of the science discussed, because if it were a part of the subject as in the first division, then it would not be correct that discussion occurs in the science concerning it, and that it is included among the matters of the science, because discussion in a science is not about the parts of the subject but about its accidental attributes. And one may say: we do not accept that the haythiyya in the first division is a part of the subject; rather, it is a condition for its being a subject. The meaning is that discussion occurs about the attributes that attach to it from that aspect and consideration. And based on this, if we make the haythiyya in the second division a condition for the subject, as the speech of the earlier scholars apparently shows, not a description of the accidental attributes, following what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) went to, then discussion about it in the science would not be a discussion about the parts of the subject, and we would not be faced with the objection that the author faced of two sciences sharing one subject essentially and in consideration. Explanation: His statement 'and among them is that indeed the haythiyya is mentioned': In this phrase, the commentator clarified the text. In the text, the author used the phrase 'among them is that indeed the haythiyya is mentioned'. So in this phrase the author indicated the connection to what preceded: that among the discussions related to the subject, the second discussion is about the word 'haythiyya' which is mentioned in subjects. The linguistic investigation of 'hayth': And the word 'hayth': From here the linguistic investigation of the word 'hayth' is explained: that in language it is used for place, e.g., 'haythu tajlisu ajlis' meaning 'wherever you sit, I sit'. Metaphorically, 'hayth' means direction and consideration. Thus, 'al-mawjud min haythu huwa mawjud' i.e., the existent from the direction and consideration that it exists. The haythiyya is sometimes a part of the subject and sometimes a description of the accidental attributes. 'Fa al-haythiyya al-madhkura': In this phrase, the text is explained. The summary is that when the word 'hayth' is mentioned in the subject, sometimes the haythiyya is not from the accidental attributes of the subject, and sometimes it is from the accidental attributes. That is, in the first case, discussion will be about the attributes that attach to the subject by means of this aspect, and there will be no discussion about attributes that do not attach by means of this aspect. For example, the subject of divine science is existent from the aspect of being existent. So in it, discussion will be about the states of existents that attach by means of existence, such as existence being originated, possible, unity, multiplicity, cause, effect; these things attach to the existent by means of existence. But contrary to the existent's being a substance, accident, body, or abstract from matter: these are not discussed because although they attach to the existent, they do not do so by means of existence. And sometimes the haythiyya is an actual description of the types, such as the subject of medicine is the human body from the aspect of sickness and health; here 'hayth' is a description. Now this health and sickness are a description of that which the accidental attributes discussed in medicine will be that which affect the body from the aspect of health and sickness. And similarly, the subject of natural science is bodies from the aspect of motion and rest; this motion and rest are the haythiyya and it is a description of that...
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is a discussion (dispute) in the commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih regarding the nature of 'hayth' (aspect) in the definition of a science's subject. The author (musannif) of the matn held that in the first type (e.g., theology: existent qua existent), the hayth is part of the subject itself, while in the second type (e.g., medicine: human body qua healthy/sick), the hayth is a description of the accidental attributes to be studied. The commentator argues that if one adopts the view of the earlier scholars (al-qawm) that in both types the hayth is a condition (qayd) for the subject rather than a part or a description of attributes, then two advantages follow: (1) the discussion in the science remains about accidental attributes of the subject, not its parts, preserving the proper object of inquiry; and (2) the problem of two sciences sharing the same subject essentially and in consideration (e.g., medicine and natural science both studying the body) is avoided. The commentator then provides linguistic background: 'hayth' literally means place, metaphorically used for direction/consideration. He illustrates with examples from theology (ilm al-ilahi) and medicine/ natural science to show how the haythiyya functions either as a restricting condition or as a description of attributes. The passage is a classic example of Hanafi usul methodology where the definition of a science's subject matter is rigorously analyzed to differentiate fields of inquiry.

Key Terms
حيث (hayth): Literally place; in usul it refers to the aspect or consideration by which a subject is defined.
حيثية (haythiyya): The aspect or consideration mentioned in the definition of a science's subject.
قيد (qayd): A condition or restriction that defines the scope of the subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the advantage of treating the haythiyya in both divisions as a qayd (condition) for the subject rather than as a description of accidental attributes?
A) It allows the science to discuss the parts of the subject.
B) It avoids two sciences sharing the same subject essentially and in consideration.
C) It makes the haythiyya a part of the subject.
D) It removes the need for examples.

Key Takeaway
A haythiyya in subject definitions is best interpreted as a condition (qayd) that restricts the subject, ensuring each science studies distinct accidental attributes and avoiding overlap.

Resolving Self-Predication in Subject Definition
Resolving self-predication in subject definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the self-predication objection in defining a science's subject and apply the Hanafi resolution using the concept of haythiyya (aspect).

Core Idea
The aspect (haythiyya) qualifies the investigation, not the existence of attributes, thereby avoiding self-predication.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, defining the subject (mawdu') of a science requires care to avoid logical fallacies. One such fallacy is self-predication (taqaddum al-shay' 'ala nafsihi) where an attribute appears to be both the means and the object of investigation. This lesson unpacks the objection and the Hanafi resolution through the concept of 'aspect' (haythiyya), distinguishing between restriction on attribution and restriction on investigation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Self-Predication Objection
The objection arises when we define a science's subject by its essential attributes and then restrict investigation via an aspect (haythiyya). If the aspect acts as a mediator, then the attribute under investigation (e.g., health in medicine) would be both mediated (posterior) and mediator (prior), leading to self-predication.
2
Analyze the Famous Response
The famous response distinguishes between the essence of the attribute (e.g., health itself) and its possibility (e.g., possibility of health). The aspect is identified with the possibility, not the essence, so two different things are involved, avoiding self-predication.
This response maintains a separation between mediator and mediated.
3
Examine the Investigative Response (Tahqiq)
The investigative response corrects the understanding of restriction. The aspect is not a restriction on the attribution itself but on the mode of investigation. The attributes are not required to attach via the aspect; rather, the aspect is a perspective for inquiry.
This resolves the objection more fundamentally by redefining the role of haythiyya.
4
Distinguish Between Two Types of Restriction
There are two possible meanings: restricting the establishment of attributes (via aspect) vs. restricting the investigation of attributes (using aspect). The correct Hanafi view is the latter, which avoids self-predication completely.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the commentary of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih.
