Unity of Science Despite Diverse Essential Attributes
Addresses the objection that diverse essential attributes would fragment a single science into many.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that diverse essential attributes of a single subject remain in one science if they share a common genus, and distinguish when they may form separate sciences.

Core Idea
Diverse essential attributes unify under a common genus; otherwise, sciences split.

A key challenge in defining a science is how a single subject can accommodate multiple types of essential attributes without fragmenting into separate disciplines. This passage from a classic usul text presents an objection against the use of essential attributes as the basis for distinguishing sciences, along with a nuanced response that introduces the concept of a common genus (jins) as a unifying factor. Understanding this principle is crucial for grasping the Hanafi methodology of classifying legal subject matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector argues that if a single subject (e.g., the act of the mukallaf in fiqh) has essential attributes of multiple types (obligation, prohibition, recommendation), then each type could be made a separate science, destroying the unity of the original science.
This objection targets the use of attributes (a'rad) for scientific distinction.
2
Understand the answer: genus condition
The author responds that diverse types of attributes lead to separate sciences only if they do not share a common genus (jins). If they share a genus, they remain part of one science. Example: In grammar, marfu'at and mansubat share the genus of i'rab, so they are not separate sciences.
The genus condition preserves unity.
3
Apply to fiqh
The act of the mukallaf has attributes of obligation, prohibition, recommendation, etc. All these share the genus of legal prescription (hukm shar'i). Therefore, fiqh remains one science, not fragmented.
This shows the answer in action.
4
Analyze the compulsory reply
The author then offers an ad hominem: even if one insists on subject-based distinction (as the objector implies), the subject of fiqh can be viewed from different restrictions (e.g., obligation vs. permissibility), leading to multiple subjects, which would cause the same fragmentation problem for the objector. Thus, the objector's own criterion fails.
This reply shows the consistency and robustness of the Hanafi position.
5
Derive the usul rule
The principle extracted: The unity of a science is determined by whether its diverse essential attributes share a common genus. If they do, the science remains one; if not, separate sciences may be formed.
This rule guides the classification of Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض ثالث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگرشئی واحد کو علوم متعددہ کا موضوع بنایا جائے اور تمایز معمولات کی وجہ سے ہو تو پھر علم کے واحد ہونے کا کوئی معیار باقی نہیں رہے گا مثال کے طور پر جب ایک شئی کے اعراض مختلف الانواع ہوں اور ایک شخص کہے کہ میں نوع کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو مستقل علم بناتا ہوں اور دوسری نوع کے عوارض کو مستقل علم بناتا ہوں تو پھر وہ علم واحد تو نہ رہا بلکہ متعدد علوم بن گئے جیسے علم فقہ کا موضوع مکلف کا فعل ہے اور اس کے اعراض ذاتیہ مختلف الانواع ہیں اس کے کچھ عوارض وجوب کی نوع سے ہیں کچھ حرمت کی نوع سے ہیں اور کچھ ندب کی نوع سے اب کوئی یہ کہے کہ وہ عوارض جو و جوب کی نوع سے ہیں ان کو مستقل علم بنا تا ہوں اور جو عوارض حرمت کی نوع سے ہیں ان کو دوسرا علم بنا تا ہوں پھر علم فقہ ایک تو نہ رہا بلکہ علوم کا ڈھیر لگ گیا۔ جواب: یہ ہے کہ جب ایک موضوع کے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع ہوں تو ہر نوع کو الگ علم تب شمار کیا جائیگا جب سب انواع کسی ایک جنس میں شریک نہ ہوں اگر ایک جنس میں شریک ہوں تو الگ علم شمار کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جیسا کہ کلمہ علم النحو کا موضوع ہے اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع ہیں لیکن سب اعراب کی جنس میں شریک ہیں لہذا اب کسی کو حق حاصل نہیں ہے کہ مرفوعات کو الگ علم شمار کرے اور منصوبات کو الگ علم شمار کرے ہاں جب ایک جنس میں شریک نہ ہوں تو پھر اختیار حاصل ہے جواب الزامی: آپ نے کہا کہ علوم میں اتحاد و اختلاف کا مدار موضوع پر ہے کہ موضوع ایک ہو تو تو علم بھی ایک موضوع مختلف ہوں تو علم بھی مختلف اب اگر موضوع مختلف ہو یعنی ایک علم کا موضوع مقید ہو دوسرے علم کا موضوع مطلق ہو یا ایک علم میں ایک قید سے مقید ہو اور دوسرے علم میں دوسری قید سے مقید ہو اب ہم کہتے ہیں تمایز علمین میں اگر موضوع کا اعتبار کریں تو یہ اعتراض آپ پر بھی وارد ہوتا ہے کیونکہ فقہ کا موضوع فعل مکلف ہے اب فقہ کے موضوع کئی ہو سکتے ہیں پہلا فعل مکلف من حیث الوجوب دوسرا موضوع مقید ہو بقید الاباحت اور تیسرا موضوع مقید ہو بقید الندب ایسے ہی کراہت کے متعلق مسائل الگ علم ہیں یہ کئی علوم میں تقسیم ہو گیا کیونکہ موضوع ایک نہ رہا نما ہو جوا بکم فہو جوا بنا۔
The outcome of the third objection is that if a single thing is made the subject of multiple sciences and distinction is due to attributes, then no standard for the unity of a science remains. For example, when the attributes of one thing are of different types, and a person says: I make the essential attributes of one type an independent science, and the attributes of another type an independent science, then that science is no longer one but becomes multiple sciences. Like the subject of fiqh is the act of the mukallaf, and its essential attributes are of different types: some attributes are from the type of obligation, some from the type of prohibition, and some from the type of recommendation. Now if someone says: I make the attributes of obligation an independent science, and the attributes of prohibition another science, then fiqh is no longer one but becomes a heap of sciences. Answer: When the essential attributes of one subject have different types, each type is considered a separate science only if all types do not share a common genus. If they share a common genus, there is no need to count them as separate sciences. For example, the word (kalimah) is the subject of grammar; its essential attributes have different types, but all share the genus of i'rab (inflection). So no one has the right to count marfu'at as a separate science and mansubat as another. Yes, when they do not share a common genus, then there is choice. Compulsory reply: You said that the basis of unity and difference of sciences is the subject: if the subject is one, the science is one; if subjects differ, sciences differ. Now if the subject differs, i.e., the subject of one science is restricted, the subject of another is absolute, or one is restricted by one restriction and another by another restriction, then we say: If we consider the subject in the distinction of two sciences, this objection also applies to you, because the subject of fiqh is the act of the mukallaf. Now the subject of fiqh can be multiple: first, the act of the mukallaf from the perspective of obligation; second, the subject restricted by the restriction of permissibility; third, the subject restricted by the restriction of recommendation. Similarly, matters of dislike are a separate science. Thus it becomes divided into many sciences because the subject is no longer one. So what is your answer? That is our answer.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage addresses the third objection against using essential attributes as the basis for distinguishing sciences. The objector argues that if a single subject has multiple types of essential attributes (e.g., obligation, prohibition, recommendation in fiqh), then one could split each type into separate sciences, destroying the unity of a science. The author responds by introducing a key condition: the diverse types of essential attributes must not share a common genus. If they do (like all types of i'rab in grammar), they remain part of one science. The author then provides a compulsory reply: even if one insists on subject-based distinction, the subject of fiqh can be viewed from different perspectives (obligation, permissibility, etc.), leading to multiple subjects and thus multiple sciences — a problem for the opponent as well.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): A common genus that unites diverse types of essential attributes under one science.
نوع (naw'): A type or species of essential attribute within a science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, when can diverse essential attributes of a single subject be made into separate sciences?
A) Always, because they are different types
B) Never, because the subject is one
C) Only when they do not share a common genus
D) Only with the permission of the founder of the science

Key Takeaway
The unity of a science is preserved when its diverse essential attributes share a common genus; otherwise, they may form distinct sciences.

12 min
The Necessity of Diverse Essential Attributes for a Unitary Entity
Logical proof of diverse essential attributes for a unitary entity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the logical argument that a real unitary entity must have diverse essential attributes and critically evaluate the objection that multiplicity does not imply diversity.

Core Idea
A truly unitary entity's multiple essential attributes must be diverse in type, not just numerically multiple.

This passage presents a philosophical proof central to Hanafi usul al-fiqh: that a real unitary entity (like the divine essence) cannot acquire attributes from parts or externals, so its many attributes must arise from its essence itself. The argument further shows that these attributes are necessarily diverse in kind, not merely multiple. Understanding this reasoning sharpens your ability to analyze essential properties in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis and the entity
Recognize that the thesis to be proved is that a real unitary entity (wahid haqiqi), with no parts or multiplicity, possesses diverse essential attributes (a'radh dhatiyya mutanawwi'a). The entity itself is the subject.
2
Eliminate impossible sources of attributes
Consider how attributes could attach: either due to a part of the entity, or due to something separate from it. Since the entity has no parts, the first is impossible. Since it is truly unitary and cannot depend on an external cause, the second is also impossible. Therefore attributes must attach due to the essence itself.
3
Apply the dilemma: regress or essence
Now for any attribute, either it attaches because of another attribute (leading to infinite regress, tasalsul, which is impossible) or it attaches because of the essence itself. If it attaches via the essence, it is an essential attribute. For multiple attributes, either each is essential (giving diversity) or some attach via other attributes. But infinite regress is barred, so eventually all must be essential.
4
Address the objection: multiplicity vs. diversity
An objector says: even if many essential attributes are granted, they could all be of the same type (e.g., multiple powers), and the desired conclusion is diversity of types (tanawwu'), not mere multiplicity. The response: attributes in a single locus are necessarily diverse because attributes of the same type differ only by their locus; here the locus is one, so if they were of the same type they would be identical, not multiple. Hence multiplicity in one locus forces diversity in type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ، ( وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا اسْتَدَلَّ عَلَى ثُبوتِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمُتَنَوِّعَةِ لِشَيْءٍ. وَاحِدٍ بِأنَّ الوَاحِدَ الْحَقِيقِى الَّذِي لَا كَثرَةَ فِي ذَاتِهِ بِوَجْهِ مِنَ الْوُجُوهِ يَعْصِفُ بِصِفَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ ، وَإِنْ كَانَ بَعْضُهَا حَقِيقِيًّا كَالْقُدْرَةِ وَبَعْضُهَا إِضَافِيًّا كَالْخَلْقِ وَبَعْضُهَا سَلْبِيًّا كَالتَّجَرُّدِ عَنْ الْمَادَّةِ وَالْمُتَّصِفُ بِصِفَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ مُتَّصِفٌ بِأَعْرَاض ذَاتِيَّةٍ مُتَنَوِّعَةٍ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا شَيْءٍ مِنْ تِلْكَ الصِّفَاتِ لَاحِقًا لَهُ لِجُزْئِهِ لِعَدَمِ الْجُزْء لَهُ وَلا لِلْمُبَايُنِ لِامْتِنَاعِ احْتِيَاجِ الْوَاحِدِ الْحَقِيقِي فِي صِفَاتِهِ إِلَى أَمْرٍ مُتَفَصِلٍ وَكَانَ يَنبَغِي أَنْ يَتَعَرَّضَ لِهَذَا أَيْضًا وَحِينَئِذٍ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لُحُوقَ كُلِّ مِنْهَا لِصِفَةٍ أُخْرَى فَيَلْزَمُ التَّسَلُسُلُ فِى الْمَبَادِى أَعْنِي الصَّفَاتِ الَّتِي كُلُّ مِنْهَا مَبْدَأُ لِصِفَةٍ أُخْرَى ، وَهُوَ مُحَالٌ لِبُرْهَانِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ فِي الْكَلَامِ أَوْ يَكُونُ بَعْضُهَا لِذَاتِهِ فَيَثْبُتُ عَرَضُ ذَاتِي وَحِينَئِذٍ فَالْبَعْضُ الْآخَرُ لَا يَجُوزُ أَن يَكُونَ لِجُزنِهِ لِمَا مَرَّ فَهُوَ إمَّا لِذَاتِهِ فَيَقْبتُ عَرَضٌ ذَاتِيٌّ آخَرُ ، وَهُوَ الْمَطْلُوبُ أَوْ لِغَيْرِهِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَن يَكُونَ الْغَيْرُ مُبَايِنًا لِمَا مَرَّ ، بَلْ يَكُونُ صِفَةٌ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ وَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَنتَهِيَ إِلَى مَا يَكُونُ لُحُوقُهُ لِذَاتِهِ وَإِلَّا لَزِمَ التَّسَدُسُلُ فِي الْمَبَادِءِ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَنتَهِيَ إِلَى الْعَرَضِ الذَّاتِي الْأَوَّلِ فَلا يَلْزَمُ تَعَدُّدُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ وَلَوْ سُلّمَ فَاللَّازِمُ تَعَدُّدُهَا ، وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَطْلُوبِ وَالْمَطْلُوبُ تَنَوُّعُهَا ، وَهُوَ غَيْرُ لَازِمٍ قُلْنَا اللَّاحِقُ بِوَاسِطَةِ الْعَرَضِ الذَّاتِيِّ الْأَوَّلِ أَيْضًا عَرَضْ ذَاتِي فَيَلْزَمُ التَّعَدُّدُ وَالصِّفَاتُ الْمُتَعَدِّدَةُ فِي مَحَلِّ وَاحِدٍ مُتَنَوِّعَةٌ لَا مَحَالَةَ ضَرُورَةَ
أَنَّ اخْتِلَافَ أَشْخَاصِ نَوْعٍ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الصِّفَاتِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَحَلِّ قَوْلُهُ ) وَلِأَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ) عَطْفٌ عَلَى مَضْمُونِ الْكَلَامِ السَّابِقِ أَى ، وَإِنْ كَانَ لِغَيْرِهِ فَهُوَ بَاطِلٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَسْتَلْزِمُ التَّسَلْسُلَ وَ لأَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ اسْتِكْمَالُ الْوَاحِدِ الْحَقِيقِي فِي صِفَاتِهِ بِالْغَيْرِ ، وَهُوَ مُحَالٌ ؛ لأنَّهُ يُوجِبُ النُّقْصَانَ فِي ذَاتِهِ وَالِاحْتِيَاجَ فِي كَمَالَاتِهِ
His statement: 'And we only said that it is proved that essential attributes of a single thing are diverse because a real unitary entity, which has no multiplicity in its essence in any way, is characterized by many attributes, even if some are real like power, some are relational like creation, and some are negative like immateriality. And that which is characterized by many attributes is characterized by diverse essential attributes necessarily, because none of those attributes attaches to it due to a part (since it has no part) nor due to something separate (because it is impossible for a real unitary entity to need an external thing for its attributes). And he ought to have addressed this also. Then either the attachment of each of them is due to another attribute, resulting in infinite regress in the principles—meaning the attributes each being a principle for another attribute—and that is impossible due to the known proof in theology; or some of them are due to its essence, so an essential attribute is established. Then the other part cannot be due to its part as previously, so it is either due to its essence, so another essential attribute is established—and that is what is sought—or due to something else, and that something else cannot be separate as previously, but must be an attribute of its attributes, and it must terminate at that which attaches due to its essence, otherwise infinite regress would follow. If it is said that it may terminate at the first essential attribute so no multiplicity of essential attributes would follow, and even if multiplicity is granted, what is required is diversity, not multiplicity, and diversity does not necessarily follow. We say: that which attaches via the first essential attribute is also an essential attribute, so multiplicity follows, and multiple attributes in a single locus are necessarily diverse, because the difference of individuals of a single type of attributes is only due to difference of locus. His statement: 'And because it follows' is conjoined to the content of the previous statement, meaning: And if it is due to something else, it is invalid because it entails infinite regress, and because it would require the real unitary entity to complete its attributes by something else, which is impossible because it would imply deficiency in its essence and need in its perfections.'
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a proof that a real unitary entity (like the divine essence, though the text is abstract) necessarily has diverse essential attributes. The proof proceeds by noting that such an entity has no parts (so attributes cannot arise from parts) and cannot depend on external things (so attributes cannot come from outside). Therefore, each attribute either arises from another attribute (leading to infinite regress, which is impossible) or arises from the essence itself. If multiple attributes arise from the essence, they are essential attributes, but they may be multiple (ta'addud) but not necessarily diverse (tanawwu'). The text then argues that even if they are multiple, because they inhere in a single locus, they must be diverse—since the only way two attributes can be of the same type is if they differ by locus. Thus the attributes of a single unitary entity are necessarily diverse in type (not just numerically multiple). This is a classical kalām argument about the attributes of God, applied here to illustrate the concept of essential attributes in the philosophy of science.

Key Terms
واحد حقیقی (wahid haqiqi): An entity that is one in essence with no parts or multiplicity.
عارض ذاتی (aaridh dhati): An attribute that attaches to the essence itself, not through a part or external cause.
تسلسل (tasalsul): An endless chain of causes, considered impossible in this argument.
تنوع (tanawwu'): Attributes of different types, not just multiple instances of the same type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if a real unitary entity's attributes were all due to another attribute (infinite regress)?
A) The entity would have parts.
B) Infinite regress is impossible, so this scenario is invalid.
C) The attributes would all be relational.
D) The attributes would be diverse anyway.

Key Takeaway
A real unitary entity must have diverse essential attributes because attributes cannot arise from parts or externals, and multiple attributes in one locus are necessarily diverse in type.

Refuting Circularity in the Definition of Quran: Mahiyyah vs. Tashkhis
Refuting circularity by distinguishing essential definition from specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ta'rif al-mahiyyah (essential definition) and tashkhis (specification), and apply this distinction to refute the objection of circularity in the Hanafi definition of the Quran.

Core Idea
A definition can be a specification (tashkhis) of a homonym, not an essence (mahiyyah), thus avoiding circularity.

In this passage, the author responds to a classic objection raised by Ibn Hajib: that the Hanafi definition of the Quran as 'what is transmitted in the musahif' is circular, because defining 'mus'haf' requires the Quran. The author clarifies that this definition is not an essential definition (ta'rif al-mahiyyah) but rather a specification (tashkhis) that identifies which meaning of the homonymous term 'Quran' is intended. This distinction is crucial for understanding how Hanafi usul al-fiqh handles definitions and avoids logical fallacies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Understand Ibn Hajib's claim that the definition of Quran involves circularity because it uses 'mus'haf', which itself is defined by 'Quran'. This is a standard logical critique.
Circularity (dawr) renders a definition invalid if it is intended as an essential definition.
2
Recognize the distinction between mahiyyah and tashkhis
The author argues that the Hanafi definition is not an essential definition capturing the 'whatness' of the Quran, but rather a specification that picks out a particular meaning among multiple possibilities.
Tashkhis does not require capturing the essence; it merely identifies the intended referent.
3
Analyze the homonymy of 'Quran'
The word 'Quran' is mushtarak (homonymous): it can refer to the eternal speech of Allah (an attribute) or to the recited text (al-maqru'). The definition specifies the latter.
Homonyms require specification to avoid ambiguity; this is a common usul tool.
4
See how tashkhis avoids circularity
Since mus'haf is known by custom ('urf), it does not need definition. The definition merely says: 'the Quran (recited) is the one written in what is customarily called a mus'haf'. No circularity arises.
Customary knowledge breaks the potential circular dependency.
5
Note the practical consequence
The Hanafi definition of Quran stands as valid and is used for deriving rulings, unlike alternative definitions that might be vulnerable to this objection.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the acceptance of the standard Hanafi definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَأَجَبْت عَنْ هَذَا بِقَوْلِى ) وَلَا دَوْرَ ؛ لِأَنَّ الْمُصْحَفَ مَعْلُومٌ أَيْ فِي الْعُرْفِ قَلا يَحْتَاجُ إلَى تَعْرِيفِهِ بِقَوْلِهِ الَّذِى كُتِبَ فِيهِ الْقُرْآنُ ثُمَّ أَرَدْت تَحْقِيقًا فِي هَذَا الْمَوْضِعِ لِيُعْلَمَ أَنَّ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفَ أَى نَوْعٍ مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ التَّعْرِيفَاتِ فَإِنَّ إِثْمَامَ الْجَوَابِ مَوْقُوت[؟] عَلَى هَذَا فَقُلْت ( وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيفُ مَاهِيَّةِ الْكِتَابِ ) بَلْ تَشْخِيصُهُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ كِتَابٍ تُرِيدُ ، ( وَلَا الْقُرْآنِ) فَإِنَّ عُلَمَاء نَا قَالُوا هُوَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا إِلَخُ فَلَا يَخُلُو إِمَّا أَنْ عَرَّفُوا الْكِتَابَ بِهَذَا أَوْ عَرَّفُوا الْقُرْآنَ بِهَذَا ، فَإِنْ عَرَّفُوا الْكِتَابَ بِهَذَا فَلَيْسَ تَعْرِيفًا لِمَاهِيَّةِ الْكِتَابِ ، بَلْ تَشْخِيصَهُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيَّ كِتَابٍ تُرِيدُ وَإِنْ عَمَّلُوا الْقُرْآنَ بِهَذَا فَلَيْسَ تَعْرِيفًا لِمَاهِيَّةِ الْقُرْآنِ أَيْضًا ، بَلْ تَشْخِيصَهُ ) لأنَّ الْقُرْآنَ اسْمٌ يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْكَلَامِ الْأَزَلِيّ وَعَلَى الْمَقْرُوءٍ فَهَذَا تَعْيِينُ أَحَدٍ مُحْتَمَلَيْهِ ، وَهُوَ الْمَقْرُوءُ) فَإِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ لَفَةٌ مُشْتَرَى[؟] يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْكَلَامِ الْأَزَلِيِّ الَّذِى هُوَ صِفَةٌ لِلْحَقِّ عَزَّ وَعَلَا وَيُطْلَقُ أَيْضًا عَلَى مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ ، وَهُوَ الْمَقْرُوءٍ فَكَأَنَّهُ قِيلَ أَيْ الْمَعْنَيَيْنِ تُرِيدُ ، فَقَالَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا إِلَخْ أَى نُرِيدُ الْمَقْرُوءِ فَعَلَى هَذَا لَا يَلْزَمُ الدَّورُ وَإِنَّمَا يَلْزَمُ الدَّورُ إِنْ أُرِيدَ تَعْرِيفُ مَاهِيَّةِ الْقُرْآنِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ عُرْف مَاهِيَّةَ الْقُرْآنِ بِالْمَكْتُوبِ فِى الْمُصْحَفِ فَلا بُدَّ مِنْ مَعْرِفَةِ مَاهِيَّةِ الْمُصْحَفِ فَلَا يَكْفِي حِينَئِذٍ مَعْرِفَةُ الْمُصْحَفِ بِبَعْضِ الْوُجُوهِ كَالْإِشَارَةِ وَنَحْوِهَا ، ثُمَّ مَعْرِفَةُ مَاهِيَّةِ الْمُصْحَفِ مَوْقُوفَةٌ عَلَى مَعْرِفَةِ مَاهِيَّةِ الْقُرْآنِ ..
ترجمہ:۔ پس ہم رکھتے ہیں کتاب کو دو قسموں پر قسم اول اولہ شرعیہ (کے بیان ) میں ہے اور وہ (ادلہ ) چار ارکان پر (مشتمل) ہیں رکن اول کتاب یعنی قرآن میں ہے اور وہ ( قرآن ) وہ ہے جو نقل کیا گیا ہو ہماری طرف مصاحف کے دوستوں کے درمیان تو اتر کے ساتھ پس خارج ہو گئیں باقی تمام کتابیں اور احادیث قدسیہ اور نبویہ اور قراءات شاذہ ۔ اور تحقیق اعتراض کیا ابن حاجب نے کہ بیشک یہ تعریف دوری ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی مانقل فی المصاحف کے ساتھ پس اگر سوال کیا جائے کہ مصحف کیا ہے؟ پس ضروری ہے کہ کہا جائے وہ ہے جس میں لکھا گیا ہو قرآن۔ پس میں نے جواب دیا اس اعتراض کا اپنے اس قول کے ساتھ اور نہیں لازم آتا) دور کیونکہ مصحف معلوم ہے یعنی عرف میں پس نہیں ہے احتیاجی اس کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اس کے قول الذی کتب فیہ القرآن کے ساتھ ۔ پھر میں نے ارادہ کیا تحقیق کرنے کا اس جگہ میں کہ بے شک یہ تعریف تعریفات کی قسموں میں سے کونسی قسم ہے ہی کیونکہ جواب کا مکمل ہونا موقوف ہے اسی پر پس میں نے کہا اور نہیں ہے یہ تعریف ماہیت کتاب کی بلکہ کتاب کی تشخیص کی ہے ائی کتاب ترید کے جواب میں اور نہ ہی قرآن کی ماہیت کی) کیونکہ ہمارے علماء نے کہا ہیکہ وہ مانقل الیتا الخ ہے پس نہیں ہے خالی یا تو انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے کتاب کی اس طرح یا انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی یہ پس اگر انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے کتاب کی یہ تو پھر نہیں ہے یہ تعریف کتاب کی ماہیت کی بلکہ اس (کتاب) کی تشخیص کی ہے ای کتاب ترید کے جواب میں اور اگر انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی یہ پس نہیں ہے یہ تعریف قرآن کی ماہیت کی بھی بلکہ اس کی تشخیص کی ہے کیونکہ قرآن کا طلاق کیا جاتا ہے کلام از لی پر اور کلام مقر و پر پس یہ (تعریف) متعین کرتا ہے اس کے دو احتمالوں میں سے ایک کو اور وہ کلام مقرو ہے کیونکہ قرآن ایسا لفظ ہے جو مشترک ہے بولا جاتا ہے اس کلام الہی پر وہ جو صفت ہے حق تعالیٰ عزوجل کی۔ اور نیز بولا جاتا ہے اس پر بھی جس پر وہ دلالت کرتا ہے اور وہ کلام مقرر ہے پس گویا کہ کہا گیا دو معنوں میں سے کونسے معنی کا تو ارادہ کرتا ہے پس کہا کہ مانقل الینا آخر تک یعنی ہم ارادہ کرتے ہیں کلام مقر و کا پس اس تفصیل پر نہیں لازم آتا دور اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ لازم آتا ہے دور اگر مرا دلیا جائے ماہیت قرآن کی تعریف کیونکہ اگر تعریف کی جائے ماہیت قرآن کی المکتوب فی المصاحف کے ساتھ پس ضروری ہوگی ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت اور نہیں ہے ممکن اس وقت ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت بعض وجوہ کے ساتھ جیسا کہ اشارہ اور اس کی مثل ہے پھر ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت موقوف ہے ماہیت قرآن کی معرفت پر ۔ کتاب (تنقیح) میں اقسام مذکورہ کا بیان فتضع الكتاب : ماتن نے یہاں سے کتاب کی اقسام یا اجزاء کتاب کو بیان کیا ہے کہ کتاب دو قسموں پر مشتمل ہے تم اول ادلہ شرعیہ یعنی کتاب اللہ سنت رسول مہ وغیرہ کے بیان میں ہے اور قسم ثانی احکام کے بیان میں ہے تو پہلے کتاب اللہ کی تعریف کی ہے کتاب اللہ اور قرآن اس کو کہتے ہیں جو مصحف کے دوستوں کے درمیان لکھا ہوا ہے اور تو اتر کے ساتھ ہم تک پہنچا ہے پھر فوائد و قیود ذکر کرتے ہیں کہ بین رفتی المصاحف کی قید سے احادیث قدسیہ اور مطلق احادیث خارج ہوگئیں کیونکہ وہ مکتوب نی المصاحف نہیں ہیں اور قراآت شازہ تواتر کی قید سے خارج ہو گئیں لیکن اس تعریف پر علامہ ابن حاجب نے اعتراض کیا ہے۔
I responded to this with my statement: 'And there is no circularity, because the mus'haf is known, i.e., in custom, so there is no need to define it with his statement 'that in which the Quran is written.' Then I intended to achieve verification in this place so that it may be known what type of definition this definition is, for the completion of the answer depends on this. So I said: 'And this is not a definition of the essence (mahiyyah) of the book, but rather its specification (tashkhis) in answer to 'which book do you mean?' and nor of the Quran, for our scholars said: 'It is what has been transmitted to us...' etc. So it is either that they defined the book with this, or they defined the Quran with this. If they defined the book with this, then it is not a definition of the essence of the book, but rather its specification in answer to 'which book do you mean?' And if they defined the Quran with this, then it is not a definition of the essence of the Quran either, but rather its specification, because the Quran is a name applied to the eternal speech and to the recited text. So this is a determination of one of its two possibilities, which is the recited text. For the Quran is a homonym: it is applied to the eternal speech which is an attribute of Allah, Most High, and also applied to what indicates it, which is the recited text. So it is as if it was said: 'Which of the two meanings do you intend?' So he said: 'What has been transmitted to us...' etc., meaning we intend the recited text. So on this basis, circularity does not arise. Circularity would only arise if the definition of the essence (mahiyyah) of the Quran was intended, because if the essence of the Quran were defined by 'written in the mus'haf', then knowledge of the essence of the mus'haf would be necessary, and in that case knowledge of the mus'haf by some aspects like pointing and the like would not suffice. Then knowledge of the essence of the mus'haf depends on knowledge of the essence of the Quran.'
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a response to Ibn Hajib's objection that the definition of the Quran as 'what is transmitted in the musahif' is circular because to define mus'haf one would need the Quran. The author clarifies that the definition is not of the essence (mahiyyah) but rather a specification (tashkhis). Customarily, mus'haf is known, so no definition is needed. Moreover, the word 'Quran' is homonymous, applying both to the eternal attribute of Allah and to the recited text. The definition specifies the latter. Thus, no circularity occurs; it is only problematic if one attempts an essential definition. The Urdu commentary reinforces this, explaining the two divisions of the book (Kitab), the first being evidences, and the definition of the Quran with its exclusions (e.g., hadith qudsi, shadhdh recitations).

Key Terms
تعريف الماهية (ta'rif al-mahiyyah): A definition that captures the essence (whatness) of a thing, listing its essential properties.
تشخيص (tashkhis): Specification; identifying a particular instance or meaning among multiple possibilities.
دور (dawr): Circularity in definition; a logical fallacy where the definiendum and definiens are mutually dependent.
مشترك (mushtarak): Homonym; a term with multiple distinct meanings (here: eternal speech and recited text).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the definition of Quran as 'what is transmitted in musahif' does not lead to circularity?
A) Because the Quran and mus'haf are synonyms.
B) Because mus'haf is known by custom and the definition is a specification of the recited Quran.
C) Because the definition is of the essence of the Quran, which is independent of mus'haf.
D) Because Ibn Hajib's objection is based on a false premise.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran is a valid tashkhis (specification) of the homonym 'Quran', not a mahiyyah definition, and thus avoids circularity because mus'haf is known by custom.

Hadd vs Rasm: Refuting the Circularity Objection in Defining the Qur'an
Objection and response regarding circular definition of Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distinction between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition), and apply it to refute the charge of circularity (dawr) in the Hanafi definition of the Qur'an.

Core Idea
The definition 'what is transmitted to us in the Mushafs' is a rasm, not a hadd, so no circularity arises.

A common logical objection to the Hanafi definition of the Qur'an is that it is circular, since it defines Qur'an by Mushaf and Mushaf by Qur'an. In this passage, the commentator presents two Hanafi responses, the second of which relies on a fundamental distinction between two types of definitions: hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). Understanding this distinction is crucial for appreciating how Hanafi usul avoids logical pitfalls and grounds its definitions in 'urf (custom) rather than essentialist requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Ibn Hajib argues that defining 'Qur'an' as 'what has been transmitted to us in the Mushafs' is circular: understanding Qur'an requires knowing Mushaf, and knowing Mushaf requires knowing Qur'an. Understand his reasoning.
Circularity (dawr) is considered invalid in logic because it makes understanding contingent on itself.
2
Examine the first response
The commentator's first response is that Mushaf is well-known by custom ('urf) and requires no definition, so understanding Mushaf does not depend on understanding Qur'an. This breaks the circle.
This is a simpler, pragmatic rebuttal based on convention.
3
Analyze the second response - the hadd/rasm distinction
Definitions are of two kinds: hadd (essential definition) specifies the genus and differentia, revealing the essence; rasm (descriptive definition) merely distinguishes the defined from others using known properties. For hadd, all parts must be known essentially; for rasm, conventional understanding suffices.
Key differences: hadd answers 'what is it in essence?', rasm answers 'which one do you mean?'.
4
Apply the distinction to the definition of Qur'an
The definition 'what has been transmitted to us' is a rasm, not a hadd. It only distinguishes the revealed Qur'an from the eternal attribute. Since rasm does not require essential knowledge of its parts, Mushaf does not need to be defined essentially; its customary meaning is sufficient. Hence, no circularity.
If it were a hadd, circularity would arise, but it is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہ تعریف دور پر مشتمل ہے اس لئے کہ اس تعریف میں توقف الشئی علی نفسہ لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ قرآن کی تعریف کو سمجھنا موقوف ہے مصحف کی تعریف پر اور اگر مصحف کے بارے میں پوچھا جائے تو کہا جائیگا ما کتب فیہ القرآن تو قرآن کا سمجھنا موقوف ہوا مصحف پر اور مصحف کا سمجھنا موقوف ہوا قرآن پر تو قرآن کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف ہو گیا اس لئے کہ شی کے موقوف علیہ کا موقوف علیہ مئی کا موقوف علیہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ دور ہے اور دور باطل ہے تو مستلزم دور بھی باطل ہے اس اعتراض کے ماتن نے جواب دیئے۔
جوابات اعتراضات ابن حاجب
جواب (1):۔ یہ بھی جواب ہے کہ یہاں دور لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے کہ قرآن کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے مصحف پر اور مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہے کیونکہ مصحف عرف میں مشہور ہے اور مشہور کی تعریف نہیں ہوتی ۔
جواب (۲):۔ یہ تحقیقی جواب ہے لیکن اس سے پہلے بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں ۔
مقدمہ: تعریف دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس سے مقصود معرف کی ماہیت کو بیان کرنا ہوگا یا مقصود صرف معرف کو ماعدا سے جدا کرنا ہوگا یعنی تعین تشخیص مقصود ہوگی مثلا زید معرف ہے اور اس کی ماہیت حیوان ناطق ہے اور تشخیص کے بارے کہا جائیگا کہ فلاں جگہ رہتا ہے ایسا رنگ ہے اتنا قد ہے وغیرہ ذالک تو اگر مقصود ماہیت کو بیان کرنا ہو تو یہ حد ہے اور اگر تعریف تشخیص مقصود ہو تو یہ تعریف رسم ہے۔
حد اور رسم میں فرق: حد اور رسم میں کئی فرق ہیں (۱) حد میں سوال ما حقیقیہ سے ہوگا اور رسم کے بارے میں سوال اسی شئی سے ہوگا مثلا انسان کی تعریف حقیقی کریں گے تو سوال ہوگا ما الانسان اور اگر ماعدا سے امتیاز مقصود ہو تو کہیں گے ای بی الانسان (۲) حد کیلئے جنس و فصل کو ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے اور رسم کیلئے جنس و فصل کو ذکر کرنا ضروری نہیں۔ (۳) حد میں صرف اشارہ کافی نہیں ہو تا رسم میں صرف اشارہ کافی ہوتا ہے۔ حد میں ضروری ہے کہ حد کے جتنے اجزاء ہیں ان کی حقیقت بھی معلوم ہو اور رسم میں تمام اجزاء کی حقیقت معلوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
اس تمہید کے بعد یہ سمجھیں کہ قرآن کی جو یہ تعریف کی گئی ہے یہ تعریف حد کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے بلکہ رسم کے قبیل سے ہے اس کے بارے میں سوال اسی شئی سے ہوتا ہے یعنی مانقل الینا الخ اگر کتاب کی تعریف ہو تو ای کتاب ترید کے سوال کے جواب میں یہ تعریف واقع ہوگی اور اگر تعریف قرآن کی ہو تو اسی شئی سے سوال ہو گا کیونکہ قرآن کا اطلاق کلام ازلی پر بھی ہوتا ہے اور کلام لفظی ( مانقل الیتا الخ) پر بھی ہوتا ہے جو ہم پڑھتے ہیں اب اگر یہ قرآن کی تعریف ہے تو سوال ہو گا ای قرآن ترید جواب میں کہا جائیگا مانقل الینا الخ یعنی ہماری مراد کلام لفظی ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تعریف رسم کے قبیل سے ہے اور رسم کیلئے اشارہ اور عرف کافی ہے اور تمام اجزاء کی تعریف ضروری نہیں ہے تو مصحف کی تعریف بھی ضروری نہیں ہے اب اگر ما نقل الیتا الخ والی تعریف حد ہوتی تو پھر دور لازم آتا کیونکہ پھر مصحف کی حقیقت معلوم کرنا پڑتی تو اب جب یہ تعریف رسم ہے تو قرآن کا سمجھنا تو مصحف پر موقوف ہے لیکن مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں تو توقف اشئی علی نفسہ لازم نہیں آتا۔
Objection: This definition includes circularity because understanding the definition of Qur'an depends on the definition of Mushaf, and if asked about Mushaf, one says 'that in which the Qur'an is written,' so understanding Qur'an depends on Mushaf and understanding Mushaf depends on Qur'an, thus understanding Qur'an depends on itself, because the thing upon which something depends, if that itself depends on the original thing, circularity occurs, and circularity is invalid, so the definition implying circularity is also invalid. The author (matn) gave responses to this objection. 
Responses to Ibn Hajib's objections:
Response (1): This is a response that circularity does not occur here because understanding Qur'an depends on Mushaf, but understanding Mushaf does not depend on Qur'an, since Mushaf is well-known in custom and the well-known does not require definition.
Response (2): This is a research-based response. But before that, understand a premise by way of introduction: A definition is either intended to explain the essence of the defined thing or only to distinguish it from others, i.e., identification and distinction. For example, Zayd is the defined, his essence is 'rational animal,' and for identification one says he lives in such a place, has such color, such height, etc. So if the intention is to explain the essence, it is hadd (logical definition), and if the intention is identification and distinction, it is rasm (descriptive definition).
Difference between hadd and rasm: Several differences: (1) In hadd, the question is 'what is it in essence?' while in rasm, the question is 'which thing do you mean?' For example, for a real definition of man, one asks 'what is man?' and if distinction from others is intended, one says 'which man?' (2) For hadd, mentioning genus and differentia is necessary; for rasm, it is not necessary. (3) In hadd, mere indication is not sufficient; in rasm, mere indication is sufficient. In hadd, it is necessary to know the reality of all its parts; in rasm, it is not necessary to know the reality of all parts.
After this introduction, understand that the definition given for Qur'an is not of the type of hadd but of rasm. The question regarding it is 'which thing do you mean?' i.e., 'what is transmitted to us...' If it were a definition of a book, the question would be 'which book do you intend?' and this definition would be given in response. If it is a definition of Qur'an, the question would be 'which Qur'an do you intend?' because the term 'Qur'an' applies both to the eternal speech and to the verbal speech (what is transmitted to us) that we recite. Now if this is a definition of Qur'an, the question would be 'which Qur'an do you mean?' and in response one would say 'what is transmitted to us...' meaning we intend the verbal speech. So it becomes clear that this definition is of the type of rasm, and for rasm, indication and custom are sufficient, and definition of all parts is not necessary. Thus, definition of Mushaf is also not necessary. If the definition 'what is transmitted to us' were hadd, then circularity would occur because then one would have to know the reality of Mushaf. But since this definition is rasm, understanding Qur'an depends on Mushaf, but understanding Mushaf does not depend on Qur'an, so dependence of a thing on itself does not occur.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage presents an objection attributed to Ibn Hajib against the standard Hanafi definition of the Qur'an, along with two responses. The objection claims circularity: understanding 'Qur'an' requires understanding 'Mushaf', and understanding 'Mushaf' requires understanding 'Qur'an', leading to a vicious circle (دور). The commentator (the author of Altarweeh) first clarifies that circularity does not arise because 'Mushaf' is a term known by custom ('urf) and requires no definition—it is self-evident. Then a more detailed response follows, distinguishing between two types of definition: hadd (essential definition, giving genus and differentia) and rasm (descriptive definition, merely identifying the thing). The definition of the Qur'an as 'that which has been transmitted to us in the Mushafs' (مانقل الينًا) is a rasm, not a hadd. In a rasm, the goal is simply to distinguish the defined from other things, not to give its essence. Therefore, the definition does not require an explanation of what a Mushaf is in its essence; it suffices that the term 'Mushaf' is conventionally understood. Hence, no circularity arises. This is a standard Hanafi usul al-fiqh discussion on the nature of definitions and the technical definition of the Qur'an. The discussion is rational (dalil aqli) and shows how Hanafi usul avoids the logical pitfall of circularity by using the classification of definitions into hadd and rasm.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Logical circularity where the definition of a term depends on itself.
حد (hadd): Essential definition that gives the genus and differentia of a thing.
رسم (rasm): Descriptive definition that identifies a thing without giving its essence, often using known properties or conventional understanding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to Ibn Hajib's objection, why does the definition of Qur'an as 'what has been transmitted to us in the Mushafs' not involve circularity?
A) Because the definition is a hadd, and hadd does not require knowledge of the defined term.
B) Because the definition is a rasm, and Mushaf is known by custom, so no essential definition is needed.
C) Because the term 'Mushaf' is defined in the same way as 'Qur'an', resolving the circle.
D) Because the definition includes a condition that breaks the circle.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Qur'an is valid as a rasm; the hadd/rasm distinction prevents the charge of circularity.

Structure of a Hanafi Usul Work: Two Parts and Four Pillars
Explanation of the book's structure: two parts and four pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main divisions of a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text and explain the arrangement of the four evidences and the appendices.

Core Idea
The Hanafi usul text divides into evidences and rulings, with the first part built on four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.

In this passage from Al-Talwih, the commentator explains the overarching structure of a standard Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. Understanding this structure is essential because it reveals the logical flow from sources to rulings. The author places the book's main purposes into two divisions, with the first division dedicated to the four primary evidences, arranged in order of priority, and the two supporting chapters on tarjih and ijtihad appended to the last evidence, Qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main divisions
According to the text, the book's main purposes are divided into two parts. Determine what those two parts are (evidences and rulings).
The passage explicitly mentions 'the states of evidences and rulings' as the subject matter.
2
Recognize the four pillars of the first division
List the four sources of evidence (adillah) that form the pillars of the first division: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
They are presented in a specific order.
3
Understand the ordering principle
Why are the four evidences arranged in this sequence? The text says 'giving precedence to the prior in essence and honor'.
The Quran is first because it is the most fundamental and noble source.
4
Locate the appendices
The chapters on tarjih (preponderance) and ijtihad are placed as a completion and appendage to the pillar of Qiyas. Identify what they complete.
Tarjih and ijtihad are methods for resolving conflicts and deriving rulings from qiyas.
5
Distinguish the main from preliminary
The preliminary discussion of definition and subject matter is outside the two divisions. Note why it is excluded.
Because it is not among the main purposes (maqasid) of the book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلویح
قَوْلُهُ فَتَضَعُ تَفْرِيحٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ فَيَبْحَثُ عَنْ كَذَا وَكَذَا يَعْنِي بِسَبَبٍ أَنْ الْبَحْتَ فِى هَذَا الْفَنْ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ نَضَعُ الْكِتَابَ أَيْ مَقَاصِدَهُ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ وَإِلَّا فَبَحْتُ التَّعْرِيفِ وَالْمَوْضُوعِ أَيْضًا مِنْ الْكِتَابِ مَعَ أَنَّهُ خَارِجٌ عَن الْقِسْمَيْنِ لِكَوْنِهِ غَيْرَ دَاخِلٍ فِى الْمَقَاصِدِ وَالْقِسْمُ الْأَوَّلُ مُرَتِّبٌ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَرْكَانِ فِي الْأَدِلَّةِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْكِتَابُ ثُمَّ السُّنةَ ثُمَّ الْإِجْمَاعُ ثُمَّ الْقِيَاسُ تَقْدِيمًا للإقدَامِ بِالذَّاتِ وَالشَّرَفِ . وَأَمَّا بَابَا التَّرْجِيحِ وَالِاجْتِهَادِ فَكَأَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُمَا تَتِمَّةٌ وَتَذْيِلا لِرُكُنِ الْقِيَاسِ .
Talwih: His statement 'so we place' is an explication of his statement 'he investigates such and such', meaning that because research in this art is only about the states of evidences and rulings, we place the book (i.e., its purposes) into two divisions. Otherwise, the discussion of definition and subject matter is also part of the book, though it is outside the two divisions because it is not included among the purposes. The first division is arranged upon four pillars concerning the four evidences: the Book (Quran), then the Sunnah, then Consensus (Ijma), then Analogy (Qiyas), giving precedence to the prior in essence and honor. As for the two chapters of tarjih (preponderance) and ijtihad, it is as if he made them a completion and appendage to the pillar of Qiyas.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage from Al-Talwih (a super-commentary on Al-Tawdih) explains the structure of the standard Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. The author (Taftazani) comments on the matn's statement 'fa-nada'u' (so we place) in relation to the previous phrase 'yabhathu 'an kadha wa kadha' (he investigates such and such). The point is that since the science of usul al-fiqh is about the states of evidences and rulings, the book's main purposes are divided into two parts. There is also preliminary discussion of definitions and subject matter, but that is not part of the main purposes. The first main part is organized into four pillars corresponding to the four sources of evidence: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. They are arranged in order of priority—the Quran first because it is prior in time (aqdam) and in honor (ashraf). The two chapters on tarjih (preponderance between conflicting evidences) and ijtihad are treated as an appendix to the pillar of Qiyas, indicating that they are related to the application and resolution of analogical reasoning. This reflects the standard Hanafi arrangement where qiyas is the last of the four evidences, and the rules for preferring one evidence over another and the methodology of ijtihad are placed after it.

Key Terms
الأدلة الأربعة (al-adillah al-arba'ah): The four sources of evidence in Hanafi usul: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of giving preponderance to one evidence over another when they conflict.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent reasoning to derive rulings from sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text from Talwih, how are the chapters on tarjih and ijtihad treated in the book's structure?
A) As a fifth pillar alongside the four evidences.
B) As a separate part independent of the four pillars.
C) As a completion and appendage to the pillar of Qiyas.
D) As part of the preliminary discussion of definitions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul text is structured in two parts: evidences and rulings, with the first part built upon four pillars (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), and tarjih/ijtihad appended to Qiyas.

The Four Sources of Usul al-Fiqh and the Role of Ijtihad and Tarjih
Explaining the book's division and the four sources of the first part

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four primary sources in the first part of a Hanafi usul work and explain why ijtihad and tarjih are considered preludes to qiyas rather than independent sources.

Core Idea
The first part of usul works has only four sources; ijtihad and tarjih are tools, not independent divisions.

This passage from a sharh on a Hanafi usul matn explains the book's structure. The author clarifies that the book's main objectives are divided into two parts: the sources (adillah) and the rulings (ahkam). Within the first part, only four sources are counted: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. Chapters on ijtihad and tarjih are included under qiyas as preludes, not as separate sections. Understanding this classification is essential for grasping the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Main Divisions
The commentator states the book is divided into two parts: first part (al-awwal) deals with sources, second part deals with rulings. Note that introductory material is excluded from these divisions because it is auxiliary.
The term 'objectives' (maqāṣid) refers only to the core content.
2
List the Four Sources of the First Part
The first part contains exactly four components: Kitab Allah, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. This is the standard Hanafi list of primary sources.
Order reflects rank: Quran first, then Sunnah, then consensus, then analogy.
3
Understand the Objection and Response About Ijtihad and Tarjih
A hypothetical objection claims that chapters on ijtihad and tarjih are also in the first part, making six components. The commentator responds that these are merely preludes (tamah) to qiyas and are subsumed under it.
This shows that procedural discussions are not independent sources but methodological tools.
4
Apply the Classification
When studying usul texts, distinguish between primary sources (adillah) and secondary discussions (tarjih, ijtihad, etc.). This helps in understanding the hierarchy and the scope of each source.
Hanafis treat ijtihad and tarjih as part of the methodology for applying qiyas.

The book is divided into two parts: first part is the sources (al-awwal) and second part is rulings (ahkam). By 'book' is meant the objectives of the book. This is the second part of the commentary, answering an implicit question: The author said 'we divide the book into two parts: first part is the sources and second part is the rulings.' The question is: the introduction includes definitions and subject matter, so it is also part of the book; why didn't the author mention it? The answer: In 'we divide the book' there is an omitted genitive, i.e., 'we divide the objectives of the book into two parts'. The introduction and subject matter are aids to the objectives, not part of the objectives. Another question: The commentator said 'by book is meant the objectives of the book', and objectives are two: sources and rulings. The objection: the book contains letters and words, not proofs; how can it be said that the objectives are mentioned? Answer: This is figurative: the indicator is used to mean the indicated, because the letters indicate meanings. The first part: the third part of the commentary—the commentator intends to explain the division of the first part; it has four components: Kitab Allah, Sunnah of the Messenger, Ijma, and Qiyas. Order and precedence: the fourth part of the commentary; the commentator answers an implicit question: Why was this order placed? Because Kitab Allah is superior in rank, so it is placed first in mention to conform to natural order. Ijtihad and Tarjih are preludes to Qiyas. ... This is the last part of the commentary; the commentator answers an implicit question: Question: You said the first part explains four components; we do not accept; rather, two more chapters are mentioned there: the chapters of Ijtihad and Tarjih, so the components are six, not four. Answer: Because these two chapters are preludes to Qiyas and are mentioned under Qiyas; they are not independent divisions, so no objection.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the structure of the matn. The commentator clarifies that the book's two-part division refers to its main objectives: the sources (first part) and the rulings (second part). Introductory matters are not counted among these objectives. The first part has four core sources: the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. The ordering by rank is justified. When an objection is raised that chapters on ijtihad and tarjih make the first part six components, the commentator responds that these are merely preludes to analogy and not independent, thus preserving the fourfold division. This is typical Hanafi usul methodology: prioritizing sources by strength and incorporating procedural tools as subsets of analogy.

Key Terms
مقاصد (maqāṣid): The main objectives or purposes of the book, i.e., the sources and rulings, excluding introductory material.
اول (awwal): The first part of the book dealing with the four foundational sources: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
تمہ (tamah): Prelude or preface; here, ijtihad and tarjih are described as preludes to qiyas, not independent sections.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul books divide the subject into two parts: four primary sources and rulings; ijtihad and tarjih are methodological tools within qiyas, not independent sources.

Avoiding Circularity (Dawr) in Defining Mushaf
Discusses circularity in defining Mushaf via Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition of Mushaf leads to circularity and distinguish between an essential definition and a distinguishing description.

Core Idea
Defining Mushaf essentially via Quran causes circularity; a distinguishing definition by custom avoids it.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, definitions must avoid logical circularity (dawr). This passage examines a classic problem: defining 'Mushaf' (the bound Quran) using 'Quran' itself. The author distinguishes essential definition (mahiyya) from distinguishing description (tamyiz), showing that only the latter can break the circle. We will work through the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of definition
The passage contrasts a distinguishing interpretation (tafsir/tamyiz) that merely identifies the object by custom or indication, with an essential definition (ta'rif al-mahiyya) that aims to capture the quiddity.
Distinguishing description does not require prior knowledge of the essence.
2
Recognize the circularity condition
Circularity occurs only when the definition is intended as an essential definition of Kitab or Quran. If it is a distinguishing description, no circularity occurs.
The author explicitly says: 'If it is made a definition of the essence... circularity occurs.'
3
Understand the identity of essences
The essence of Kitab and the essence of Quran are identical – they are two names for one thing. Therefore, dependency on one implies dependency on the other, reinforcing the circularity.
This is a key Hanafi position: al-Kitab and al-Quran are synonymous in essence.
4
Evaluate the counterarguments
The passage considers objections: (a) defining Mushaf linguistically as 'collection of pages' with condition of tawatur, (b) defining it as the concrete whole known by custom. The Hanafi response rejects these as departures from haqiqa to majaz.
Customary definitions are not precise enough for usul, although they may work in everyday language.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
The definition of Mushaf for usul purposes is a distinguishing description relying on custom/indication, not an essential definition. This avoids circularity while maintaining precision.
The author's discussion is about defining the concrete whole (majmū' shakhṣī), not the universal concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فإن تمام الجواب معلوم على هذا يعني إن جعل التعريف المذكور تفسيرا للفظ الكتاب أو القرآن وتمييزا له عن سائر الكتب أو الكلام الأزلي يجوز في معرفة المصحف الاكتفاء بالعرف أو الإشارة ونحو ذلك ولا يلزم الدور وإن جعل تعريفا لماهية الكتاب أو القرآن فلا بد من معرفة ماهية المصحف وهي موقوفة على معرفة ماهية القرآن ضرورة أنه لا معنى له إلا ما كتب فيه القرآن فيلزم الدور. لا يقال فالدور إنما يلزم إذا جعل تعريفا لماهية القرآن دون الكتاب: لأنا نقول ماهية الكتاب هي بعينها ماهية القرآن لما مر من أنهما اسمان لشيء واحد فتوقف المصحف على ماهية القرآن توقفه على ماهية الكتاب، وبهذا يظهر أن تفسير المصحف بما جمع فيه الوحي المتلو لا يدفع الدور؛ لأنه أيضا مرادف للكتاب والقرآن فالمصنف صرح بأنه ليس تعريفا للماهية سواء عرف به الكتاب أو القرآن إشارة إلى أنه لا فرق في لزوم الدور بين الصورتين، ثم قال وإنما يلزم الدور إن أريد تعريف ماهية القرآن إشارة إلى أن ماهية الكتاب هي ماهية القرآن فذكر أحدهما مغن عن ذكر الآخر، فإن قيل يفسر المصحف بما جمع فيه الصحائف مطلقا على ما هو موضوع في اللغة ويخرج منسوخ التلاوة عن التعريف بقيد التواتر فلا دور قلنا عدول عن الظاهر إلى الخفي وعن الحقيقة إلى المجاز العرفي فلا يحسن في التعريفات. فإن قيل تعريف الأصولي إنما هو للمفهوم الكلي الصادق على المجموع وعلى كل بعض ومعرفة المصحف إنما تتوقف على القرآن بمعنى المجموع الشخصي وهو معلوم معهود بين الناس يحفظونه ويتدارسونه فلا يشتبه عليهم فلا دور. قلنا لو سلم معرفة المجموع الشخصي بحقيقته بدون معرفة المفهوم الكلي فمبنى كلام المصنف على أن التعريف للمجموع الشخصي دون المفهوم الكلي.
His saying: 'Indeed the completion of the answer is known on this basis' means: If the mentioned definition is made an interpretation of the word Kitab or Quran and a distinction for it from other books or the eternal speech, then in knowing the Mushaf it is permissible to suffice with custom or indication and the like, and circularity does not occur. But if it is made a definition of the essence of Kitab or Quran, then knowledge of the essence of Mushaf is necessary, and it is dependent on knowledge of the essence of Quran, by necessity that it has no meaning except that in which the Quran is written, so circularity occurs. It cannot be said: Circularity only occurs if it is made a definition of the essence of Quran without Kitab, for we say: The essence of Kitab is identical to the essence of Quran, because they are two names for one thing. Thus the dependency of Mushaf on the essence of Quran is its dependency on the essence of Kitab. And by this it becomes apparent that interpreting Mushaf as 'that in which the revealed recited text is collected' does not repel circularity, because it is also synonymous with Kitab and Quran. The author explicitly states that it is not a definition of essence, whether one defines Kitab or Quran by it, indicating that there is no difference between the two cases in the occurrence of circularity. Then he said: Circularity only occurs if one intends to define the essence of Quran, indicating that the essence of Kitab is the essence of Quran, so mentioning one suffices from mentioning the other. If it is said: Mushaf is interpreted as 'that in which the pages are collected absolutely' according to its linguistic coinage, and the abrogated recitation is excluded from the definition by the condition of tawatur, so there is no circularity. We say: That is a departure from the apparent to the hidden, and from the reality to the customary metaphor, and that is not good in definitions. If it is said: The usuli's definition is only for the universal concept that applies to the whole and to every part, and knowledge of the Mushaf only depends on the Quran in the sense of the concrete whole, which is known and conventional among people—they memorize it and study it—so it is not ambiguous for them, and there is no circularity. We say: Even if knowledge of the concrete whole by its reality without knowledge of the universal concept is conceded, the basis of the author's statement is that the definition is for the concrete whole, not the universal concept.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage discusses the problem of circularity (dawr) in defining the term 'Mushaf' (the bound copy of the Quran). The author distinguishes two types of definition: (1) a distinguishing description (tafsir/tamyiz) that merely identifies the object by custom or indication, which does not require prior knowledge of the essence and thus avoids circularity; (2) an essential definition (ta'rif al-mahiyya) that aims to capture the quiddity, which leads to circularity because Mushaf is defined as 'that in which the Quran is written,' but the Quran itself is defined as 'what is written in the Mushaf.' The commentator then addresses objections: (a) defining Mushaf as 'collection of pages' with the condition of tawatur is rejected because it moves from the apparent (haqiqa) to the obscure (khafi) and from reality to custom; (b) the usuli's definition is for the universal concept (mafhūm kullī) whereas the knowledge of Mushaf depends on the concrete whole (majmū' shakhsī), which is known by custom, so the author's discussion is about defining the concrete whole, not the universal concept.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Circular reasoning in definition, where the definition of A depends on B and B depends on A.
ماهية (māhiyya): The essence or quiddity of a thing, as opposed to a mere distinguishing description.
مفهوم كلي (mafhūm kullī): A universal concept that applies to the whole and each part, like 'Quran' as a genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when does circularity (dawr) occur in defining Mushaf?
A) When Mushaf is defined as a collection of pages with tawatur.
B) When the definition is meant as an essential definition (ta'rif mahiyya) of Kitab or Quran.
C) When the definition is purely by custom or indication.
D) When Mushaf is defined as the concrete whole known by custom.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, definitions of technical terms like Mushaf must avoid circularity by being distinguishing descriptions rather than essential definitions.

Avoiding Circularity in Defining Mushaf: Essential vs. Distinguishing Definitions
Analyzing objections to defining Mushaf via Quran/Kitab and avoiding circularity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the problem of circularity (dawr) in defining Mushaf and apply the Hanafi distinction between essential (haqiqi) and distinguishing (tamyizi) definitions to avoid it.

Core Idea
Mushaf, Quran, and Kitab are synonymous in essence — defining one by the other causes circularity unless the definition is for distinction, not essence.

Precision in defining key terms is fundamental in usul al-fiqh. This passage from a classical sharh tackles the logical problem that arises when defining Mushaf (the physical codex) by reference to Quran or Kitab. Since these terms are essentially synonymous, any definition that aims to reveal the essence (haqiqa) will fall into circularity. The author demonstrates that the only way out is to treat the definition as merely identifying (tamyiz) the object, not disclosing its inner reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Terms and Their Relationship
Recognize that the passage treats Quran, Kitab, and Mushaf as names for one single essence (shay' wahid). Understand that they are synonyms in the sense of mutual dependence.
This is the basis for circularity: if A is defined by B and B by A, we have dawr.
2
Understand the Circularity Problem
If Mushaf is defined as 'that in which the Quran/Kitab is collected', then to know Mushaf one must already know Quran/Kitab. But if Quran/Kitab is then defined by reference to Mushaf, a circle results.
The passage says 'fa-tawaqquf al-mushaf 'ala mahiyyat al-qur'an tawaqqufuhu 'ala mahiyyat al-kitab' — the dependence is identical.
3
Differentiate Essential vs. Distinguishing Definition
A haqiqi definition reveals the essence (mahiyya) and requires full knowledge of all defining parts. A tamyizi definition merely separates the defined thing from others, without needing complete knowledge of its essence.
Hanafi usul emphasizes that definitions in fiqh texts are often tamyizi for practical recognition.
4
Apply the Distinction to the Passage
The author states that if the definition of Quran (by which Mushaf is defined) is meant as tamyiz — simply to distinguish it from other books or eternal speech — then circularity does not arise. But if the definition aims at the essence, dawr is inevitable.
The key phrase: 'wa innama yalzam al-dawru idha urida ta'rif mahiyyat al-qur'an'.
5
Evaluate the Objections and Responses
The passage presents two objections: (1) defining Mushaf lexically as 'collection of sheets' avoids circularity; (2) defining Mushaf via the known individual whole (majmu' shakhsi) of Quran avoids confusion. The author dismisses the first as departure from haqiqa to majaz 'urfi, and the second as irrelevant because definitions are for the universal concept, not the individual whole.
Understand why 'urf is less preferred in formal definitions, and why the author insists on the universal concept.

That they are two names for one thing. So the dependence of Mushaf on the essence of Quran is its dependence on the essence of Kitab. By this it becomes apparent that interpreting Mushaf as 'that in which the revealed recited (wahy al-matlu) is collected' does not avoid circularity, because it is also synonymous with Kitab and Quran. So the author explicitly states that it is not a definition of the essence, whether Kitab or Quran is defined by it, indicating that there is no difference in the necessity of circularity between the two forms. Then he said: 'Circularity only occurs if the definition of the essence of Quran is intended', indicating that the essence of Kitab is the essence of Quran, so mentioning one suffices from mentioning the other. If it is said that Mushaf is interpreted as 'that in which the sheets (suhuf) are collected in absolute terms, according to its lexical usage, and the abrogated of recitation (mansukh al-tilawah) is excluded from the definition by the condition of tawatur, so there is no circularity.' We say: this is a departure from the apparent to the hidden, and from the real (haqiqa) to customary metaphor (majaz 'urfi), so it is not good in definitions. If it is said: The definition of the usuli is only for the universal concept (mafhum kulli) that applies to the whole and to every part, and knowledge of Mushaf only depends on Quran in the sense of the individual whole (majmu' shakhsi), and it is known and customary among people, they memorize and study it, so it is not ambiguous to them, so there is no circularity. We say: Even if knowledge of the individual whole by its reality without knowledge of the universal concept is conceded, then the basis of the author's statement is that the definition is for the individual whole, not the universal concept. Translation (of the Urdu): His statement 'fa-in atamma al-jawab' means that if the mentioned definition is taken as interpretation of Kitab or Quran and for distinguishing from all books or from eternal speech, then it is permissible to suffice in defining Mushaf with custom or indication, and circularity will not arise. But if taken as definition of the essence of Kitab or Quran, then knowledge of the essence of Mushaf becomes necessary, and that depends on knowledge of the essence of Quran because Mushaf means only that in which Quran is written, so circularity arises. And it cannot be objected that circularity does not arise when defining essence of Quran and not Kitab, because the essence of Kitab is identical to the essence of Quran. And this shows that interpreting Mushaf as 'that in which the revealed recited is collected' does not avoid circularity. Then he said that circularity is only necessary if definition of essence of Quran is intended. Then if it is objected that Mushaf be interpreted as 'that in which sheets are collected' absolutely lexically, with tawatur condition excluding abrogated recitation, we say: this departs from apparent to hidden, from reality to customary metaphor. Then if it is objected that the usuli's definition is for the universal concept applying to whole and parts, and knowledge of Mushaf depends on Quran as individual whole known to people, so no ambiguity, we say: even if they know the individual whole, the author's basis is that definition is for the individual whole, not universal concept. If this definition of Quran is for distinction from others, no circularity arises. Explanation: This is the first part of the commentator's clarification: if the definition of Quran is non-real (not of essence) but only to separate from others, then circularity does not arise because real definition requires knowledge of all parts, whereas non-real definition does not. Therefore knowledge of the word Mushaf is not necessary; custom or indication suffices.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a earlier matn dealing with the definition of the Mushaf and the problem of circularity (dawr). The author argues that the terms 'Quran', 'Kitab', and 'Mushaf' are synonymous in essence — they are names for the same thing. Therefore, if one defines Mushaf in terms of Quran or Kitab, a circularity arises because each term's definition presupposes knowledge of the other. The only way to avoid circularity is to define these terms not as essential (haqiqi) definitions but as distinguishing (tamyizi) definitions, i.e., merely to differentiate them from other things. For example, defining Quran as 'the revealed recited speech' is sufficient for distinguishing it from eternal speech or other books, even if the definition includes the word Mushaf, because the definition's purpose is not to reveal the essence but to identify. Similarly, defining Mushaf as 'that in which the sheets are collected' is lexically valid but departs from the real (haqiqa) to customary metaphor (majaz 'urfi), which is not ideal in definitions. The text also discusses the usuli's definition: it is for the universal concept (mafhum kulli), but knowledge of Mushaf depends on the specific individual whole (majmu' shakhsi) of Quran, which is commonly known among Muslims. The commentator concludes that the author's position is that the definition is for the individual whole, not the universal concept, so circularity is avoided.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Circularity: a situation where the definition of a term presupposes knowledge of the term being defined
مصحف (mushaf): The physical codex containing the written Quran
حقيقة (haqiqah): Real definition that reveals the essence (mahiyyah) of a thing
مجاز عرفى (majaz 'urfi): Customary metaphor: usage that departs from the literal meaning due to common custom
مفهوم كلي (mafhum kulli): Universal concept that applies to all individuals and parts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does circularity (dawr) in defining Mushaf become inevitable?
A) When the definition is meant to distinguish Quran from other books
B) When the definition aims to reveal the essence (mahiyyah) of Quran or Kitab
C) When the definition uses the phrase 'that in which the sheets are collected'
D) When the definition is based on custom (urf) rather than literal meaning

Key Takeaway
Circularity in defining Mushaf is avoided when the definition is for distinction (tamyiz), not for revealing essence (haqiqa).

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
The Individual Cannot Be Defined by Essential Constituents: A Usul Debate
Debate on whether the individual can be defined by essential constituents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the usul debate on whether an individual can be defined by a proper definition (hadd) and identify the correct Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A definition captures essence, not individuality — the individual can only be pointed to, not defined by essential constituents.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the question of whether individuals can be defined by a proper definition is a classic logical puzzle. This passage presents the core arguments: the claim that individuals cannot be defined, the objector's appeal to composite entities, and the responses that clarify the limits of definition. The correct position distinguishes between distinguishing an individual in existence versus giving a unique mental specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
The passage begins with the statement 'al-shakhsi la yuhadd' — the individual is not defined. Note the reason given: knowledge of the individual is only obtained by pointing or proper name, not by essential constituents.
The 'complete definition' (al-hadd al-tamm) includes only genus and differentia, not accidental features.
2
Follow the objector's counterargument
An objector argues that al-shakhsi is a composite entity (murakkab i'tibari) of essence and individuality, so why can it not be defined by something covering both?
The objector's reasoning appeals to the possibility of a definition that includes both essential and individuating components.
3
Analyze the responses to the objector
First response: if the composite entity of the Quran were defined similarly, no other premises would be needed — an absurdity. Second response: restricting to essentials does not specify the individual; including accidents risks non-permanence.
The text then offers a rebuttal: accidents can be included because their removal would mean the individual ceases to exist, so the definition remains valid.
4
Distill the correct position
The correct position (al-haqq) is that the individual can be defined by what gives its distinction in existence (bi-ma yufidu imtiyazahu 'an jami' ma 'adahu bi-hasab al-wujud), not by giving a unique mental specification that precludes sharing, since that only comes by pointing.
This distinction is crucial: definition can distinguish the individual in the external world, but not capture its unique haecceity in the mind.

قَوْلُهُ ) عَلَى أَنَّ الشَّخْصِيَّ لَا يُحَدُّ ) وَلِأَنَّ مَعْرِفَتَهُ لَا تَحْصُلُ إِلَّا بِتَعْيِينِ مُشَخْصَاتِهِ بِالْإِشَارَةِ أَوْ نَحْوِهَا كَالتَّعْبِيرِ عَنْهُ بِاسْمِهِ الْعَلَمِ وَالْحَدُّ لَا يُفِيدُ ذَلِكَ ؛ لأنْ غَايَتَهُ الحَدُّ التَّامُ ، وَهُوَ إِنَّمَا يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى مُقَوِّمَاتِ الشَّيْء دُونَ مُشَخْصَاتِهِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَقُولَ الشَّخْصِيُّ مُرَكَّبٌ اعْتِبَارِيٌّ ، وَهُوَ مَجُمُوعُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ وَالنَّشَخْصِ فَلِمَ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُحَدَّ بِمَا يُفِيدُ مَعْرِفَةَ الْأَمْرَيْنِ لَا يُقَالُ تَعْرِيفُ الْمُرَكَّبِ الِاعْتِبَارِى لَفْظِيٌّ وَالْكَلَامُ فِي الْحَدّ الْحَقِيقِيّ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ لَوْ سُلّمَ ذَلِكَ فَمَجُمُوعُ الْقُرْآنِ مُرَكَّبٌ اعْتِبَارِيٌّ لَا مَحَالَةَ فَحِينَئِذٍ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى سَائِرِ الْمُقَدَّمَاتِ وَلَا إِلَى مَا ذَكَرَ فِي تَشْخِيصِهِ مِنَ التَّكَلُفَاتِ ، وَقَدْ يُقَالُ إِنْ اقْتَصَرَ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الشَّخْصِي عَلَى مُقَوِّمَاتِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ لَمْ يَخْتَصَّ بِالشَّخْصِي فَلَمْ يُفِدُ التَّمُسِيرُ الَّذِى هُوَ أَقَلُّ مَرَاتِبِ التَّعْرِيفِ ، وَإِنْ ذَكَرَ مَعَهَا الْعَرَضِيَّاتِ الْمُشَخْصَةَ أَيْضًا لَمْ يَجِبُ دَوَامُ صِدْقِهَا لِإِمْكَانِ زَوَالِهَا فَلا يَكُونُ حَدًا ، وَفِيهِ نَظَرٌ لِجَوَازِ أَنْ يَذْكُرَ مَعَهَا الْعَرَضِيَّاتِ المُشَخْصَةَ وَعِندَ زَوَالِهَا يَزُولُ الْمَحْدُودُ أَيْضًا أَعْنِي ذَلِكَ الشَّخْصِيَّ فَلا يَضُرُّ عَدَمُ صِدْقِ الحَدٌ ، بَلْ يَجِبُ : وَالْحَقُّ أَنَّ الشَّخْصِيَّ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُحَدَّ بِمَا يُفِيدُ امْتِيَازَهُ عَنْ جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ بِحَسْبِ الْوُجُودِ لَا بِمَا يُفِيدُ تَعَيَّنَهُ وَتَشَخَّصَهُ بِحَيْثُ لَا يُمْكِنُ اشْتِرَاكُهُ بَيْنَ كَثِيرِينَ بِحَسَبِ الْعَقْلِ فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ إِنَّمَا يَحْصُلُ بِالْإِشَارَةِ لَا غَيْرُ .
His statement: 'That the individual is not defined' — and because knowledge of it is not obtained except by specifying its distinguishing features by pointing or the like, such as expressing it by its proper name, and the definition does not serve that; because its ultimate is the complete definition, and it only includes the essential constituents of the thing, not its distinguishing features. And an objector may say: Al-shakhsi is a composite entity (iʿtibārī), and it is the aggregate of essence and individuality. So why is it not permissible to define it by something that gives knowledge of both? It should not be said: The definition of a composite entity is verbal, and the discourse concerns the real definition; because we say: If that is conceded, then the aggregate of the Quran is inevitably a composite entity. Then there would be no need for all the premises, nor for what was mentioned in identifying it of the artificialities. And it may be said: If one restricts the definition of al-shakhsi to the essential constituents of the essence, it is not specific to al-shakhsi, so it does not provide the distinguishing (tamyīz) which is the lowest level of definition. And if one mentions with them the distinguishing accidents as well, their perpetual truth is not necessary due to the possibility of their removal, so it would not be a definition. But there is a consideration because it is permissible to mention with them the distinguishing accidents, and when they are removed, the defined (i.e., that individual) also ceases, so the lack of truth of the definition is not harmful; rather, it is necessary. And the truth is that al-shakhsi can be defined by what gives its distinction from all others according to existence, not by what gives its specific identity and individuality such that it cannot be shared among many according to the intellect; for that is only obtained by pointing, not otherwise.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usūl al-fiqh debate) concerning whether an individual (al-shakhṣī) can be defined by a proper definition (ḥadd). The text presents the argument that it cannot, because a complete definition (al-ḥadd al-tāmm) includes only the essential constituents (muqawwimāt) of a thing — such as genus and differentia — and not the accidental distinguishing features (mushakhkhiṣāt) that uniquely identify an individual, like pointing or proper name. An objector counters that al-shakhṣī is a composite entity (murakkab iʿtibārī) consisting of essence (māhiyya) and individuality (tashakhkhuṣ), so why can it not be defined by something covering both? The response argues that if accepted, the entire Quran (which is also a composite entity) would require no other premises to be defined, which is absurd. Another objection notes that if definition is limited to essentials, it is not specific to the individual; if accidents are added, they may not be permanent. The text counters by saying that if accidents are included and later removed, the defined individual also ceases, so the definition is still valid. The correct position is that the individual can be defined in terms of distinguishing it in existence (al-wujūd), not by giving a unique mental specification that precludes sharing, as the latter only comes by pointing. This debate illustrates the usul principle that a genuine definition (ḥadd ḥaqīqī) is of universal natures, not individuals.

Key Terms
الشخصي (al-shakhṣī): The individual as a concrete entity, distinct in existence from all others.
الحد (al-ḥadd): A definition that expresses the essential constituents (muqawwimāt) of a thing, typically genus and differentia, and aims to give complete knowledge of the essence.
مقومات (al-muqawwimāt): The essential constituents that constitute the essence of a thing, without which it would cease to be what it is.
عرضیات مشخصہ (al-ʿaraḍiyyāt al-mushakhkhiṣa): Accidental properties that distinguish one individual from another but are not part of the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct position on defining al-shakhṣī?
A) It is absolutely impossible to define an individual by any definition.
B) It can be defined by what distinguishes it in existence, but not by a unique mental specification.
C) It can be defined only by pointing or proper name.
D) It can be defined by a complete definition that includes both essential and accidental features without restriction.

Key Takeaway
The individual can be defined by existence-based distinction, but its unique mental haecceity is only captured by pointing or proper name, not by a proper definition.
